Free Trade Agreement between the United Mexican States and the Republic of Costa Rica
Preamble
The Government of the United Mexican States and the Government of the Republic of Costa Rica,
DETERMINED TO
STRENGTHEN the special bonds of friendship, solidarity and cooperation between their peoples;
ACCELERATE and strengthen the revitalization of American integration schemes;
ACHIEVE a better balance in trade relations between their countries, taking into account their relative levels of economic development;
CONTRIBUTE to harmonious development, the expansion of world trade and the expansion of international cooperation;
CREATE a more extensive and secure market for goods produced and services supplied in their territories;
REDUCE distortions in trade;
ESTABLISH clear and mutually beneficial rules for your commercial exchange;
ENSURE a predictable commercial framework for the planning of productive activities and investment;
DEVELOP their respective rights and obligations derived from the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade (GATT), as well as from other bilateral and multilateral cooperation instruments;
STRENGTHEN the competitiveness of their companies in world markets;
ENCOURAGE innovation and creativity through the protection of intellectual property rights;
CREATE new job opportunities, improve working conditions and living standards in their respective territories;
TO UNDERTAKE all of the above in a manner consistent with the protection and conservation of the environment;
PRESERVE its ability to safeguard the public welfare;
PROMOTE sustainable development;
STRENGTHEN the preparation and application of environmental laws and regulations;
PROMOTE the dynamic participation of the different economic agents, particularly the private sector, in efforts aimed at deepening economic relations between the Parties and developing and maximizing the possibilities of their joint presence in international markets; Y
PROTECT and strengthen the fundamental rights of its workers.
CELEBRATE this Free Trade Agreement.
Chapter I
Initial Provisions
Article 1-01: Establishment of the free trade zone.
The Parties establish a free trade area in accordance with the provisions of Article XXIV of the GATT.
Article 1-02: Objectives.
1. The objectives of this Agreement, developed specifically through its principles and rules, including those of national treatment, most favored nation treatment and transparency, are the following:
a. stimulate the expansion and diversification of trade between the Parties;
b. eliminate trade barriers and facilitate the circulation of goods and services between the Parties;
c. promote conditions of fair competition in trade between the Parties;
d. substantially increase investment opportunities in the territories of the Parties;
and. protect and enforce, adequately and effectively, intellectual property rights in the territory of each Party;
F. establish guidelines for further cooperation between the Parties, as well as at the regional and multilateral level aimed at expanding and improving the benefits of this Agreement;
g. create effective procedures for the application and compliance of this Agreement, for its joint administration and for the settlement of disputes.
2. The Parties shall interpret and apply the provisions of this Agreement in light of the objectives set out in paragraph 1 and in accordance with the applicable rules of international law.
Article 1-03: Relationship with other international treaties and agreements.
1. The Parties confirm the rights and obligations in force between them in accordance with the GATT and other treaties and agreements to which they are party.
2. In case of inconsistency between the provisions of the treaties and agreements referred to in paragraph 1 and the provisions of this Agreement, the provisions of this Agreement shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 1-04: Observance of the Treaty.
Each Party shall ensure, in accordance with its constitutional provisions, compliance with the provisions of this Agreement in its territory at the central or federal, state or municipal level, except in cases where this Agreement provides otherwise.
Article 1-05: Succession of treaties.
Any reference to another international treaty or agreement shall be understood to be made in the same terms to any successor treaty or agreement to which the Parties are party.
Chapter II
General Definitions
Article 2-01: Definitions of General Application.
1. For the purposes of this Agreement, unless otherwise specified, it shall be understood as:
customs duty: any import tax, duty or tribute and any charge of any kind applied in connection with the importation of goods, including any form of surcharge or additional charge on imports, except:
a. any charge equivalent to an internal tax established in accordance with Article III:2 of the GATT or any equivalent provision of a successor agreement to which the Parties are a party, in respect of like goods, direct competitors or substitutes of the Party, or in respect of goods from which the imported good has been manufactured or produced in whole or in part;
b. any countervailing duty that is applied in accordance with the legislation of each Party;
c. any duties or other charges related to importation, proportional to the cost of services rendered; Y
d. any premium offered or collected on imported goods, derived from any bidding system, regarding the administration of quantitative restrictions on imports or tariffs-quota or tariff preference quotas.
good of a Party: national products as understood in the GATT, those goods that the Parties agree upon, and includes originating goods; a good of a Party may incorporate materials from other countries;
originating good: good that complies with the rules of origin established in Chapter V (Rules of origin);
Customs Valuation Code: the Agreement on the Application of Article VII of the GATT, including its interpretative notes;
Commission: the Administrative Commission established in accordance with article 16-01 (Administrative Commission);
countervailing duty: antidumping duties and quotas or countervailing duties according to the legislation of each Party;
days: calendar days, including Saturday, Sunday and holidays;
business: any entity incorporated or organized under applicable law, whether or not for profit and whether privately or governmental owned, including any partnerships, foundations, companies, branches, trusts, shares, ethnically owned businesses, joint ventures, or other associations;
state enterprise: an enterprise that is owned or controlled by a Party through equity participation;
enterprise of a Party: an enterprise incorporated or organized under the laws of a Party;
tariff fraction: the breakdown of a Harmonized System tariff classification code to more than six digits;
measure: any law, regulation, procedure, administrative provision, or practice, among others;
national: a natural person who has the nationality of a Party under its law. It shall be understood that the term also extends to persons who, in accordance with the legislation of that Party, have the status of permanent residents in the territory thereof;
Party: any State for which this Treaty has entered into force;
Exporting Party: the Party from whose territory a good or service is exported;
Importing Party: the Party into whose territory a good or service is imported;
heading: a Harmonized System tariff classification code at the four-digit level;
person: a natural person or a company;
person of a Party: a national or company of a Party;
Tariff Reduction Program: the one established in article 3-04 (Tariff Reduction);
Secretariat: the Secretariat established in accordance with Article 16-02 (Secretariat);
Harmonized System: the Harmonized Commodity Designation and Coding System, including the General Classification Rules and their explanatory notes;
subheading: a Harmonized System tariff classification code at the six-digit level;
territory: means, for each Party, the territory of that Party as defined in the annex to this article.
Annex to the Article2-01:
Country-specific definitions
Unless otherwise provided, for the purposes of this Agreement, the following shall be understood as:
territory:
a. regarding Mexico:
i) the states of the Federation and the Federal District;
ii) islands, including reefs and cays in adjacent seas;
iii) the islands of Guadalupe and Revillagigedo, located in the Pacific Ocean;
iv) the continental platform and the submarine bases of the islands, cays and reefs;
v) the waters of the territorial seas, to the extent and terms established by international law, and internal maritime waters;
vi) the space located on the national territory, with the extension and modalities established by international law itself; Y
vii) any area beyond the territorial seas of Mexico within which Mexico may exercise rights over the seabed and subsoil and over the natural resources they contain, in accordance with international law, including the United Nations Convention on Law of the Sea, as well as with its internal legislation;
b. with respect to Costa Rica, the national territory including the maritime and air space, where the State exercises complete and exclusive sovereignty or special jurisdiction in accordance with articles 5 and 6 of its Political Constitution.
Chapter III
National Treatment and Market Access for Goods
Section A - Definitions
Article 3-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
consumed:
a. actually consumed; either
b. processed or manufactured in a way that results in a substantial change in the value, form or use of a good or in the production of another good;
material: material according to the definition of chapter V (Rules of origin);
samples of no commercial value: commercial samples that are marked, broken, perforated, or otherwise treated in a way that makes them unfit for sale or for any use other than as samples;
performance requirement: the requirement of:
a. export a certain volume or percentage of goods or services;
b. substitute imported goods or services with goods or services from the Party granting an exemption from customs duties;
c. that the person benefiting from an exemption from customs duties buys other goods or services in the territory of the Party that grants it, or gives preference to goods or services of national production;
d. that the person benefiting from an exemption from customs duties produces goods or provides services in the territory of the Party that grants it, with a given level or percentage of national content; either
and. relate in any way the volume or value of imports with the volume or value of exports or with the amount of foreign currency input.
Section B - Scope of application and national treatment
Article 3-02: Scope of application.
This chapter shall apply to trade in goods between the Parties, except as provided in other chapters.
Article 3-03: National treatment.
1. Each Party shall grant national treatment to the goods of the other Party in accordance with Article III of the GATT, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article III of the GATT and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this Agreement and are an integral part thereof.
2. The provisions of paragraph 1 mean, with respect to a state or municipality, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment that state or municipality accords to any like goods, direct competitors or substitutes, as the case may be, of the Party of which are members.
3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply to the measures listed in the annex to this article and to article 3-09.
Section C - Customs Duties
Article 3-04: Tariff relief.
1. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party may increase any existing customs duty, or adopt any new customs duty, on originating goods. one 23
2. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, each Party shall progressively eliminate its customs duties on originating goods in accordance with the provisions of the annex to this article (Tariff Elimination Program).
3. At the request of any of them, the Parties will hold consultations to examine the possibility of accelerating the elimination of customs duties provided for in the Tariff Elimination Program. Once approved by the Parties, in accordance with their applicable legal procedures, the agreement on the accelerated elimination of the customs duty on a good that is reached between the Parties, shall prevail over any customs duty or period of relief indicated in accordance with the Program of Tariff Deduction for that good.
4. Except as otherwise provided, this Agreement incorporates the tariff preferences previously negotiated between the Parties, in accordance with the Second Modifying Protocol of the Partial Scope Agreement signed between the United Mexican States and the Republic of Costa Rica, in the manner set forth reflected in the Tariff Elimination Program. Likewise, as of the entry into force of this Agreement, the preferences previously negotiated or granted between the Parties within the framework of the Second Modifying Protocol of the Partial Scope Agreement signed between the United Mexican States and the Republic of Costa Rica are null and void.
5. Each Party may adopt or maintain measures on imports in order to allocate the quota of imports carried out under a quota through tariffs (tariff-quota) established in the Tariff Elimination Program and in Annex 3 to Article 4- 05 (Trade in sugar), as long as these measures do not have restrictive trade effects on imports, in addition to those derived from the imposition of the quota tariff.
6. Upon the written request of either Party, the Party applying or proposing to apply measures on imports in accordance with paragraph 5 shall hold consultations to review the administration of those measures.
Article 3-05: Restrictions on the refund of customs duties on exported goods and on customs duty deferral programs.
1. For the purposes of this article, the following shall be understood as:
customs duties: the customs duties that would be applicable to a good that is imported for consumption in the customs territory of a Party if the good were not exported to the territory of another Party;
consumables: consumables as defined in Chapter V (Rules of Origin);
identical or similar goods: goods that are the same in everything, including their physical characteristics, quality and commercial prestige, as well as goods that, although they are not the same in everything, have similar characteristics and composition, which allows them to fulfill the same functions and be commercially interchangeable.
2. Neither Party may refund the amount of customs duties paid or waive or reduce the amount of customs duties due, in relation to a good imported into its territory, that is:
a. used as a material in the production of another good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party; either
b. substituted by an identical or similar good used as a material in the production of another good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party;
in an amount that exceeds the total customs duties paid or owed on that quantity of that imported good that is physically incorporated into the good exported to the territory of the other Party, or substituted by identical or similar goods physically incorporated into the good exported to the territory of the other Party. another Party, with due discount for waste.
3. No Party, subject to export, may reimburse, exempt or reduce:
a. the countervailing duties that are applied in accordance with the legislation of the Party;
b. the premiums that are offered or collected on imported goods, derived from any bidding system related to the application of quantitative restrictions on imports, tariff-quota, or preferential tariff quotas; either
c. customs duties, paid or owed, with respect to a good imported into its territory and replaced by an identical or similar good that is subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party.
4. Except as otherwise provided in this Article, as of the date and in the circumstances indicated in paragraphs 7 and 8, neither Party may refund the amount of customs duties paid, or waive or reduce the amount of customs duties owed. , in relation to a good imported into its territory, provided that the good is:
a. used as a material in the production of an originating good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party; either
b. substituted by an identical or similar good used as a material in the production of an originating good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party.
5. As of the date and in the circumstances indicated in paragraphs 7 and 8, when a good is imported into the territory of a Party in accordance with a customs duty deferral program and any of the conditions indicated in paragraphs are met. a) and b) of paragraph 4, the Party from whose territory the good was exported:
a. it will determine the amount of customs duties as if the exported good had been destined for internal consumption; Y
b. within 60 days from the date of export, it will collect the amount of customs duties as if the exported good had been destined for domestic consumption.
6. Paragraphs 3, 4 and 5 do not apply to:
a. a good that is imported under bond or guarantee to be transported and exported to the territory of the other Party;
b. a good that is exported to the territory of the other Party in the same condition in which it was imported into the territory of the Party from which it is exported. Processes such as testing, cleaning, repackaging, inspection or preservation of the good in its same condition will not be considered as changes in the condition of a good. When a good has been mixed with fungible goods and exported in the same condition, its origin, for the purposes of this paragraph, may be determined based on the inventory methods established in Chapter V (Rules of Origin);
c. a good imported into the territory of a Party that is subsequently deemed to be exported from its territory or used as a material in the production of another good that is subsequently deemed to be exported to the territory of the other Party, or is substituted for an identical or similar used good as a material in the production of another good that is later considered to be exported to the territory of the other Party, due to:
i) sending it to a store free of customs duties; either
ii) their shipment to stores on board ships or as supplies for ships or aircraft;
d. the reimbursement made by a Party of the customs duties paid on a specific good imported into its territory and subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party, when such reimbursement is granted because the good does not correspond to the samples or specifications of the object object, or due to the shipment of that good without the consent of the consignee; either
and. an originating good imported into the territory of a Party that is subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party, or is used as a material in the production of another good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party, or is substituted by an identical or similar good used as a material in the production of another good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party.
7. Subject to paragraph 8, paragraphs 4 and 5 shall apply:
a. from the moment Costa Rica applies to a non-Party country provisions similar to those contained in those paragraphs; either
b. With respect to a good imported into the territory of a Party that meets the conditions of subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 4, for three years when it is shown that the reimbursement, exemption, or reduction of customs duties simultaneously:
i) creates a significant distortion of the tariff treatment applied by the Party that grants the reimbursement, exemption or reduction of tariffs in favor of the export of goods from the territory of that Party; Y
ii) causes damage to the national production of identical, similar or direct competitive goods of the other Party.
8. In no event shall paragraphs 4 and 5 apply before January 1 , 2002.
9. For the purposes of paragraph 7, there is a significant distortion of the tariff treatment applied by the Party that grants the refund, exemption or reduction of tariffs in favor of the export of goods from the territory of that Party, when:
a. the amount of duties reimbursed, exempted or reduced on goods imported into the territory of that Party that meet the conditions indicated in subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 4 and for which there is production in the territory of the Parties, exceeds 5% of the total value of imports of originating goods during a year covered in a tariff fraction of the Party to whose territory those originating goods are exported; either
b. a Party reimburses, exempts, or reduces customs duties on goods or materials originating from the territory of non-Parties on whose importation it maintains quantitative restrictions and those goods or materials are subsequently exported to the other Party, used in the production of goods subsequently exported to the other Party. another Party, or substituted by identical or similar materials used in the production of goods subsequently exported to the other Party.
10. For the purposes of paragraph 7, for the determination of damage:
a. Injury is understood as a significant impairment of national production; Y
b. Domestic production is understood to be the producer or producers of identical or similar or directly competitive goods that operate within the territory of a Party and that constitute a significant proportion greater than 35% of the total national production of those goods.
11. The Party that refunds, exempts or reduces customs duties will provide, at the request of the other Party, the information required to verify the existence of the conditions established in paragraph 7, including statistical information regarding the imports for which it grants refunds. , exemptions or reductions of customs duties in relation to a good exported to the territory of another Party.
12. As a condition to exclude from the calculation of the percentage referred to in subparagraph a) of paragraph 9, refunds, exemptions or reductions of customs duties granted on a good that meets the conditions of subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 4, the Party that reimburses, exempts or reduces those customs duties will demonstrate that there is no production in the free trade area of ​​a good identical or similar to that good.
13. For the purposes of paragraph 12, at the request of the Party that refunds, waives or reduces customs duties on a good, the other Party shall provide to the extent possible relevant and available information on that good.
14. Each Party shall establish clear and strict procedures for the application of paragraphs 4 and 5, in accordance with the following:
a. the Party that decides to initiate an investigation to apply paragraphs 4 and 5 will publish the initiation of the investigation in the corresponding official dissemination bodies and will notify the exporting Party in writing the day after the publication;
b. For purposes of determining a significant distortion and damage in accordance with numerals i) and ii) of letter b) of paragraph 7, the competent authorities will evaluate all the factors of an objective and quantifiable nature;
c. To determine the application of paragraphs 4 and 5, a direct causal relationship between the reimbursement, exemption, or reduction and the distortion and damage to the national production of identical, similar or direct competitive goods will also be demonstrated;
d. If, as a result of this investigation, the competent authority determines, based on objective evidence, that the assumptions set forth in this article are met, the importing Party may initiate consultations with the other Party;
and. the consultation procedure will not oblige the Parties to reveal the information that has been provided confidentially, the disclosure of which may impede compliance with the laws of the Party that regulate the matter or harm commercial interests;
F. The period for prior consultations will begin on the day following the receipt by the exporting Party of the notification requesting the initiation of consultations. The prior consultation period will be 45 days unless the Parties agree on a shorter period;
g. The notification referred to in subparagraph f) will be made through the competent authority and will contain sufficient information to support the application of paragraphs 4 and 5, including:
i) the names and addresses of the national producers of identical or similar goods or direct competitors representative of the national production, their participation in the national production of that good and the reasons that lead them to affirm that they are representative of that sector;
ii) a clear and complete description of the good subject to the procedure, the tariff subheading in which it is classified and the current tariff treatment, as well as the description of the identical, similar or direct competitive good;
(iii) import data for each of the three most recent calendar years that provide the basis that the good is being imported in increasing quantities, either in absolute terms or relative to domestic production;
iv) the data on the total national production of the identical or similar good or direct competitor corresponding to the last three most recent years;
v) the data that demonstrate damage caused by imports of the good in question in accordance with subparagraphs b) and c) ;
h. the application of paragraphs 4 and 5 may only be adopted once the prior consultation period has concluded;
Yo. during the consultation period, the exporting Party will make all the observations it deems pertinent; Y
j. The exporting Party will apply paragraphs 4 and 5 at the conclusion of the consultation period provided for in subparagraph f) if the existence of any assumption established in paragraph 7 is verified.
15. The Parties shall hold annual consultations regarding the application of this Article.
Article 3-06: Temporary importation of goods.
Each Party shall authorize the temporary importation without payment of customs duty to the following goods that are imported from the territory of the other Party, regardless of their origin and whether similar goods, direct competitors or substitutes are available in the territory of the Party:
a. professional equipment necessary for the exercise of the activity, trade or profession of a business person;
b. press equipment or for broadcasting radio or television signals and cinematographic equipment;
c. goods for sporting purposes or intended for exhibition or demonstration, including components, ancillary devices and accessories; Y
d. commercial samples and publicity films.
2. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, the Parties may subject the temporary importation without payment of customs duty of a good of the type indicated in subparagraphs a), b) or c) of paragraph 1, to any of the following conditions, without the possibility of adopting additional conditions:
a. that the good is imported by a national or resident of the other Party;
b. that the property is used exclusively by the visiting person, or under his personal supervision, in the performance of his activity, trade or profession;
c. that the good is not subject to sale, lease or assignment in any other way while it remains in its territory under the temporary importation regime;
d. that the good is accompanied by a bond or guarantee that does not exceed 110% of the charges that would be owed in its case for the definitive entry or importation, or of another form of guarantee, refundable at the time of export of the good, except that no bond or guarantee may be required for customs duties on an originating good;
and. that the good is susceptible to identification by any reasonable means established by the customs authority;
F. that the good is exported upon the departure of that person or within the term that corresponds to the purpose of the temporary importation;
g. that the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use;
h. that the good does not undergo any transformation or modification during the authorized import period, except for wear and tear due to the normal use of the good; Y
Yo. that the good complies with the phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures and with the applicable standardization measures, in accordance with the provisions of section B of chapter IV (Phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures) and in chapter XI (Standardization measures) respectively.
3. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, the Parties may subject the temporary importation without payment of customs duty of a good of the type indicated in subparagraph d) of paragraph 1, to any of the following conditions, without being able to additional conditions may be adopted:
a. that the good is imported only for the purposes of placing orders for goods or services that are supplied from the territory of the other Party or from another country that is not a Party;
b. that the property is not subject to sale, lease or assignment in any other way, and is used only for demonstration or exhibition while it remains in its territory;
c. that the good is accompanied by a bond or guarantee that does not exceed 110% of the charges that would be owed in its case for the definitive entry or importation, or of another form of guarantee, refundable at the time of export of the good, except that no bond or guarantee may be required for customs duties on an originating good;
d. that the good is susceptible to identification by any reasonable means established by the customs authority;
and. that the good is exported within a period that reasonably corresponds to the purpose of the temporary importation;
F. that the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use;
g. that the good does not undergo any transformation or modification during the authorized import period, except for wear and tear due to the normal use of the good; Y
h. that the good complies with the phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures and with the applicable standardization measures, in accordance with the provisions of section B of chapter IV, (Phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures) and in chapter XI (Standardization measures) respectively.
4. When a good that is imported temporarily does not meet any of the conditions that a Party imposes in accordance with paragraphs 2 and 3, that Party may apply the customs duties and any other charges that would be due for the final entry or importation of the good. .
Article 3-07: Import free of customs duty for samples without commercial value.
Each Party will authorize the free import of samples without commercial value from the territory of the other Party.
Article 3-08: Exemption from customs duties.
1. No Party may adopt a new customs duty exemption measure when the exemption is conditioned, explicitly or implicitly, on the fulfillment of a performance requirement.
2. As of January 1 , 2002, no Party may condition, explicitly or implicitly, the validity of any current customs duty exemption on the fulfillment of a performance requirement.
3. The Party that grants an exemption or a combination of exemptions from customs duties to goods intended for commercial use by a designated person, will stop doing so or make it available to any importer, if the other Party can demonstrate that such exemption or combination of them has an unfavorable effect on:
a. your economy;
b. the business interests of a person of that Party; either
c. the business interests of an enterprise owned or controlled by a person of that Party, located in the territory of the Party granting the exemption.
Section D - Non-tariff measures
Article 3-09: Import and export restrictions.
1. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party may adopt or maintain any prohibition or restriction on the import of any good of the other Party or on the export or sale for export of any good destined for the territory of the other Party. , except as provided for in Article XI of the GATT, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article XI of the GATT and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this Agreement and are an integral part thereof.
2. The Parties understand that the rights and obligations of the GATT incorporated in paragraph 1 prohibit, in all circumstances in which any other type of restriction is prohibited, the requirements of export prices and, except as permitted for the application of sanctions and commitments in terms of countervailing duties, import price requirements.
3. In cases where a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the import or export of goods from or to a non-Party, nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to prevent it from:
a. limit or prohibit the importation of the goods of the country that is not a Party, from the territory of the other Party; either
b. require as a condition for the export of those goods from the Party to the territory of the other Party, that they not be re-exported to the country that is not a Party, directly or indirectly, without being consumed in the territory of the other Party.
4. In the event that a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the importation of a good from a non-Party, at the request of either Party, the Parties shall consult in order to avoid undue interference or distortion. in the price, marketing and distribution mechanisms in the other Party.
5. Paragraphs 1 through 4 shall not apply to the measures set out in the annex to this article and article 3-03.
Article 3-10: Export taxes.
Neither Party shall adopt or maintain any tax, duty or charge on the export of any good destined for consumption in the territory of the other Party, unless they are adopted or maintained on that good when it is destined for domestic consumption.
Article 3-11: Customs processing fees.
Neither Party shall increase or establish any customs duty for the service rendered by customs on originating goods and shall eliminate such duties on originating goods on July 1 , 1999.
Article 3-12: Country of origin marking.
The annex to this article shall apply to measures related to country of origin marking.
Section E - Publication and notification
Article 3-13: Publication and notification.
1. Each Party shall promptly publish and notify the laws, regulations, procedures, and administrative provisions of general application that it has put into effect and that refer to the classification, valuation, or customs appraisal of goods, customs duty rates, taxes or other charges or import or export measures, restrictions or prohibitions, or the transfer of payments related thereto, or the sale, distribution, transportation, insurance, storage, inspection, display, processing, mixing or any other use of those goods, so that governments and traders or interested persons of the other Party have knowledge of them.Each Party shall also publish agreements related to international trade policy that are in force between the government or a government agency of that Party and the government or a government agency of the other Party.
2. To the extent possible, each Party shall publish in advance any measure indicated in paragraph 1 that it proposes to adopt and shall provide interested persons a reasonable opportunity to comment on the proposed measures.
3. Neither Party shall apply before its official publication any measure of a general nature adopted by that Party that has the effect of increasing a customs duty or other charge on the importation of goods of the other Party, or that imposes a new or more onerous measure, restriction or prohibition for imports of goods from the other Party or for transfers of funds related to them.
4. The provisions of this Article shall not oblige any Party to disclose information of a confidential nature, the disclosure of which may constitute an obstacle to compliance with the law, is contrary to the public interest, or harm the legitimate business interests of public or private companies.
5. Each Party will identify, in terms of the tariff fractions and the nomenclature that corresponds to them in accordance with their respective rates, the measures, restrictions or prohibitions on the import or export of goods for reasons of national security, public health, preservation of the flora or fauna, the environment, plant health, standards, labels, international commitments, public order requirements or any other regulations.
Section F - Provisions on textile goods
Article 3-14: Temporary Flexibility Levels for goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System.
1. Each Party shall grant goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System, produced in the territory of the other Party in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 2 and imported into its territory, the preferential tariff treatment established in the Tariff Elimination Program Tariff corresponding to original goods, in accordance with the amounts and dates established in the annex to this article.
2. For the purposes of this article:
a. the threads and yarns classified in headings 51.06 to 51.10, 52.04 to 52.07, 53.07 to 53.08 and 55.08 to 55.11 of the Harmonized System must be totally produced in the territory of the exporting Party from non-originating fiber;
b. the goods classified in headings 54.01 to 54.06 of the Harmonized System must be totally produced in the territory of the exporting Party from non-originating materials classified in chapters 29 and 39;
c. fabrics classified in headings 51.11 to 51.13, 52.08 to 52.12, 53.10 to 53.11, 54.07 to 54.08, 55.12 to 55.16 and 60.01 to 60.02 of the Harmonized System must be wholly woven or woven in the territory of the exporting Party from thread or yarn not originating;
d. textile goods classified in chapters 56 to 59 of the Harmonized System must be entirely produced in the territory of the exporting Party from non-originating cloth, thread or yarn; Y
and. garments and other goods classified in chapters 61 through 63 of the Harmonized System shall be wholly cut (or knit to shape) and sewn or otherwise assembled in the territory of the exporting Party from cloth, thread, or non-originating yarn.
3. The total annual amounts established in the annex to this article assignable to the assets described in paragraph 1, may not be assigned to the assets classified in a certain heading in an amount that exceeds 30% of the total annual amount.
4. As of January 1 , 2000, each Party shall only grant preferential tariff treatment to originating goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System.
5. Regarding the goods that exceed the amounts determined in the annex to this article, each Party will only grant them the preferential tariff treatment established in the Tariff Elimination Program if they comply with the corresponding rule of origin established in the annex to article 5- 03 (Specific rules of origin).
Annex to articles3-03 and 3-09
Exceptions to articles 3-03 and 3-09
Section A - Measures of Costa Rica
1. Annex to the article3-04
Tariff Elimination Program
1. Except as otherwise provided in each Party's tariff staging schedule, the following tariff staging categories apply to the elimination of customs duties by each Party under Article 3-04:
a. customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category A in a Party's staging list shall be completely eliminated and such goods shall be free of customs duty as of January 1 , 1995;
b. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff headings of staging category B in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 5 equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1995, and such goods shall be free of customs duty to beginning January 1 , 1999;
c. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff headings of staging category C in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 10 equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1995, and such goods shall be free of customs duties at beginning January 1 , 2004;
d. customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category D in the staging list of a Party shall continue to receive duty-free treatment;
and. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category E in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 15 equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1995, and such goods shall be free of customs duties at beginning January 1 , 2009;
F. Customs duties on goods included in tariff items of staging category C-2 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 6 equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1997, and such goods shall be duty free customs from January 1 , 2002;
g. the customs duties on the goods included in the tariff headings of the Bp staging category in the staging list of a Party shall remain unreduced until December 31, 1998, and such goods shall be free of customs duty as of December 1, 1998 . January 1999;
h. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category C1 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 10 annual stages as of January 1 , 1995, and such goods shall be free of customs duty as of January 1 , 2004; the first five stages will each consist of reductions equivalent to 3% of the base customs duty rate and the residual customs duty will be eliminated in five equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1999;
Yo. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category E1 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 15 annual stages beginning on January 1 , 1995, and such goods shall be duty-free as of January 1, 1995. January 1 , 2009; the first six stages will each consist of reductions equivalent to 2.5% of the base customs duty rate and the residual customs duty will be eliminated in nine equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 1999;
j. the customs duties on the goods included in the tariff headings of the staging category AE in the staging list of a Party shall be applied in accordance with the provisions of Annex 3 to Article 4-04 (Trade in sugar);
k. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category C3 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in two equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 2003, and such goods shall be free of customs duties at beginning January 1 , 2004;
he. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category E3 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in 4 equal annual stages starting on January 1 , 2006, and such goods shall be free of customs duties at as of January 1 , 2009.
m. the customs duty on the goods included in the tariff fraction of the tariff reduction category C2 in the tariff reduction list of Costa Rica will be eliminated in ten equal annual stages as of January 1, 1995 and these goods will be free of customs duty as of January 1, 2004; From January 10, 1995 to December 31, 2003, Costa Rica will apply a quota tariff on the goods included in this tariff fraction, in such a way that 800 annual tons from Mexico are imported free of customs duty; Y
no. Customs duties on goods included in the tariff items of staging category E2 in a Party's staging list shall be eliminated in ten equal annual stages as of January 1, 2000, and these shall be free of customs duty as of January 1, 2000. January 1, 2009.

Annex to the article3-12
Country of Origin Marking
1. For the purposes of this annex, it shall be understood as:
final buyer: the last person who, in the territory of the importing Party, acquires it in the form in which it is imported. This buyer is not necessarily the final user of the good;
container: among others, a container, packaging, packaging or wrapping;
common container: the container in which the good will usually arrive at the final purchaser;
legible: capable of being read easily;
Sufficient permanence: that the mark will remain on the good until it reaches the final purchaser, unless it is intentionally removed;
customs value: the value of a good for the purpose of imposing customs duties on an imported good; Y
visible: that can be seen with the ordinary handling of the good or container.
2. Each Party may require that a good of the other Party imported into its territory bear a country of origin mark that indicates the name of the country of origin to the final buyer of the good.
3. Each Party may require, among its general consumer information measures, that an imported good bear the country of origin mark in the manner prescribed for goods of the importing Party.
4. By adopting, maintaining and applying any country of origin marking measure, each Party shall minimize the difficulties, costs and inconvenience that such measure may cause to the trade and industry of the other Party.
5. Each Party:
a. will accept any reasonable method of marking a good of the other Party, such as the use of adhesive or pressure labels, tags or paint, which ensures that the mark is visible, legible and of sufficient permanence;
b. shall exempt from the requirement of marking of origin a good of the other Party that:
i) is not capable of being marked;
ii) it cannot be marked before being exported to the territory of the other Party without damaging it;
iii) cannot be marked except at a cost that is substantial in relation to its customs value so as to discourage its export to the territory of the other Party;
iv) cannot be marked without material impairment of its operation or substantial deterioration of its appearance;
v) is in a container marked in such a way that the origin of the good is reasonably indicated to the final buyer;
vi) is raw material;
vii) is to be produced in the territory of the importing Party by or on behalf of the importer, in such a way that the good becomes a good of the importing Party;
viii) due to its nature or the circumstances of its importation, the final buyer can reasonably know its country of origin, even if it is not marked;
ix) it has been produced more than 20 years before it was imported;
x) has been imported without the required marking and cannot be marked afterwards except at a cost that is substantial in relation to its customs value, provided that the omission of marking was not for the purpose of circumventing the country of origin marking requirements ;
xi) is in transit, in guarantee or at the disposal of the customs authority for purposes of temporary importation without payment of customs duties;
xii) is an original work of art; either
xiii) has been imported for the importer's use and not to be sold in the form in which it was imported.
6. With the exception of the goods described in numerals vi, vii, viii, ix, xi, and xii of letter b) of paragraph 5, a Party may provide that, when a good is exempt from the country of origin marking requirement In accordance with subparagraph b) of paragraph 5, the common outer container is marked in such a way as to indicate the country of origin of the good it contains.
7. Each Party shall provide that:
a. a common container that is imported empty, disposable or not, will not require country of origin marking, but the container in which it is imported may be required to be marked with the country of origin of its content; Y
b. a full common container, disposable or not:
i) will not require country of origin marking; but
ii) may be required to be marked with the name of the country of origin of its contents, unless its contents are already marked and the container can be easily opened for inspection, or the marking of the contents is clearly visible through the container.
8. Whenever administratively and legally feasible, each Party shall allow the importer to mark a good of the other Party after importing it, but before releasing it from the control or custody of customs authorities, unless the importer has committed repeated violations of the Party's country of origin marking requirements and has been previously notified in writing that the good must be marked prior to importation.
9. Each Party shall provide that, except for importers who have been notified in accordance with paragraph 8, no special assessment or penalty shall be imposed for failure to comply with that Party's country of origin marking requirements, unless that the goods are withdrawn from the control or custody of the customs authorities without having been adequately marked or misleading marks have been affixed to them.
10. The Parties shall cooperate and consult with each other on matters related to this Annex, including additional exemptions from the country of origin marking requirement.

Chapter IV
Agricultural sector and phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures
Section A - Agricultural Sector
Article 4-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this section, it shall be understood as:
agricultural good: a good classified in any of the following chapters, headings or subheadings of the Harmonized System.
Descriptions are provided for reference purposes
fish and fish products: fish, crustaceans, molluscs or any other aquatic invertebrates, marine mammals and their derivatives, classified in any of the following chapters, headings or subheadings of the Harmonized System:
Descriptions are provided for reference purposes
export subsidies:
a. the granting of direct export subsidies, including payments in kind by governments or public bodies to a company, a branch of production, producers of an agricultural good, a cooperative or other association of such producers, or to a marketing council;
b. the sale or placement for export of non-commercial stocks of agricultural goods by governments or public agencies at a price less than the comparable price charged to buyers in the domestic market for a similar agricultural good;
c. payments for exports of agricultural goods financed by virtue of government measures, whether or not they are debited in the public accounts, including payments financed from revenues from a lien imposed on the agricultural good in question or on an agricultural good to from which the exported good is obtained;
d. the provision of subsidies to reduce the costs of marketing exports of agricultural goods (except readily available export promotion and advisory services), including handling, processing and other processing costs, and the costs of international transport and freight;
and. internal transportation and freight costs for export shipments established or imposed by governments on more favorable terms than for internal shipments;
F. subsidies on agricultural goods subject to their incorporation into exported goods;
over-quota duty rate: the duty rate applied to quantities in excess of the amount specified in a quota-duty.
Article 4-02: Scope of application.
This section applies to measures related to agricultural trade adopted or maintained by any Party.
Article 4-03: Consultations.
Before adopting a measure that may affect trade in an agricultural good between the Parties, a Party shall consult with the other Party within a reasonable period of time to avoid the annulment or impairment of a concession granted by that Party in the Tariff Elimination Program.
Article 4-04: Access to markets.
1. The Parties shall facilitate access to their respective markets by reducing or eliminating barriers to trade in agricultural goods. Except as expressly provided in this Agreement, the Parties shall not establish new barriers to trade.
Quantitative restrictions and customs duties.
2. The Parties waive the rights granted by Article XI:2 c) of the GATT and those same rights incorporated in Article 3-09 (Restrictions on imports and exports), with respect to any measure adopted or maintained on the import of agricultural goods.
3. When the tariff rate applied by a Party on an agricultural good indicated in the Tariff Elimination Program is higher than the tariff rate specified for that good in its GATT Schedule of Tariff Concessions as of January 1 , 1994, the other The Party will renounce the rights conferred by Articles II, XXII and XXIII of the GATT and its interpretative notes regarding the application of the tariff rate determined in that Schedule. This paragraph shall not apply to the goods listed in annex 1 to this article.
4. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 3, when pursuant to an agreement resulting from multilateral negotiations on agricultural trade under the GATT that has entered into force with respect to a Party, that Party agrees to convert a prohibition or restriction on its imports into an agricultural good in a tariff-quota or in a customs tariff, that Party may not apply to that agricultural good a customs tariff that is higher than the lower of the customs tariff established in:
a. its list contained in the Tariff Elimination Program; Y
b. that deal.
5. Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement, with respect to the agricultural goods listed in Annex 1 to this article, any Party may adopt or maintain a prohibition or restriction, or a customs duty on the importation of those agricultural goods in accordance with their rights and obligations derived from the GATT. Once a year from the entry into force of this Agreement, the Agricultural Trade Committee established in article 4-08, will examine the possibility of gradually eliminating the prohibitions, restrictions or customs duties on imports of goods indicated in the Agreement. annex 1 to this article. Also, once a year from the entry into force of this Agreement,
6. The Parties establish a base rate for tariff relief other than the applicable most-favored-nation rate for the agricultural goods listed in Annex 2 to this Article, as provided in that Annex.
7. Trade in sugar will be regulated in accordance with the provisions of Annex 3 to this article.
Restriction on the return of customs duties on exported agricultural goods.
8. Notwithstanding the provisions of the annex to Article 5-03 (Specific Rules of Origin), as of the date of entry into force of this Agreement, neither Party may reimburse the amount of customs duties paid, nor exempt or reduce the amount of customs duties owed, in relation to any agricultural good imported into its territory that is:
a. replaced by an identical or similar agricultural good subsequently exported to the territory of the other Party; either
b. replaced by an identical or similar agricultural good used as a material in the production of another agricultural good subsequently exported to the territory of another Party.
Article 4-05: Internal supports.
1. The Parties recognize that domestic support measures can be of vital importance for their agricultural sectors, but that they can also distort trade and affect production. In addition, they recognize that commitments on the reduction of domestic support may arise in multilateral agricultural negotiations within the GATT framework. In this sense, when a Party decides to support its agricultural producers, it will strive to move towards domestic support policies that:
a. have minimal or no distorting effects on trade or production; either
b. are exempted from any commitment to reduce internal support that could be negotiated under the GATT.
2. The Parties also acknowledge that any of them may modify their domestic support measures, including those that may be subject to reduction commitments, in accordance with their GATT rights and obligations.
Article 4-06: Export subsidies.
1. The Parties share the objective of achieving the multilateral elimination of export subsidies for agricultural goods and in this sense they will cooperate in the effort to reach an agreement within the GATT framework.
2. The Parties shall eliminate the export subsidy on an agricultural good at the moment in which the customs duty that the importing Party applies to the exporting Party under the Tariff Elimination Program for that agricultural good reaches zero.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 2, neither Party may maintain or introduce export subsidies on agricultural goods in their reciprocal trade as of January 1 , 1999. Likewise, as of that date, the Parties renounce the rights that the GATT confers on them to use export subsidies, as well as the rights regarding the use of these subsidies that could result from multilateral agricultural trade negotiations within the framework of the GATT.
Article 4-07: Agricultural standardization and marketing measures.
1. In addition to the commitments established in Chapter XI (Standardization measures), in the event that any Party makes use of agricultural standardization or marketing measures that correspond to requirements imposed on an agricultural good in terms of packaging, grades and size of the goods, that Party shall accord to an identical agricultural good originating in the other Party treatment no less favorable than that accorded to a good of that Party with respect to the application of those standards.
2. The Parties establish the Committee for Agricultural Standardization and Marketing Measures made up of representatives of each one, which will meet annually or at the request of a Party. The Committee will review, in coordination with the Committee for Standardization Measures established in Article 11-17 (Committee for Standardization Measures), the operation of agricultural classification and quality standards that affect trade between the Parties, and will resolve issues that may arise in relation to the operation of the rules. This Committee will report its activities to the Agricultural Trade Committee established in article 4-08.
Article 4-08: Committee on Agricultural Trade.
The Parties establish an Agricultural Trade Committee made up of representatives of each of them, which will meet at least once a year. The Committee will monitor and promote cooperation between the Parties for the application and administration of this chapter and will serve as a consultation forum for the Parties on matters related to it. The Committee shall submit an annual report to the Commission on the implementation of this Chapter.

Annex 3 to the article4-04
Trade in sugar
1. In the event that Mexico requires sugar in a particular year, the percentage participation of sugar originating from Costa Rica over the
total sugar requirements of Mexico (preferential quota of sugar that Mexico grants to Costa Rica) will be 19%. . In the event that Mexico grants a
percentage participation to other countries in a trade agreement, Mexico will modify the percentage participation of Costa Rica two years after the entry into force of that trade agreement, adjusting its percentage participation in accordance with the following formula:
PE x NCR
CPCR= -------------------------
TPE x N
CPCR = Preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica.
PE x NCR = Costa Rica's average net exports of sugar during the last three years for which information is available.
TPE x N = Total sum of the average net exports of sugar from the countries with which Mexico has commitments derived from a trade agreement during the last three years for which information is available (including Colombia and Venezuela).
2. The preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica will not be modified in the event that Mexico grants a preferential sugar quota to Colombia or Venezuela.
3. The preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica in accordance with paragraph 1 shall never be less than 8%.
4. The preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica will be taxed with a 0% tariff and its sale price to Mexico will have as a reference Contract 14 of the New York Coffee, Cocoa and Sugar Exchange. Since this market reflects the price of raw or raw sugar, when refined sugar is exported, the corresponding adjustment for refined sugar will have to be made according to internationally recognized conversions.
5. In the event that Mexico does not require sugar in a particular year, the preferential quota of sugar that Mexico grants to Costa Rica will be zero. Therefore, for that particular year, there will be no concession of preferential access for Costa Rica.
6. For the tariff that is applied above the preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica, notwithstanding the provisions of article 4-04, Mexico may maintain its rights and obligations under the GATT.
7. The Parties establish the Sugar Committee made up of representatives of each of them, whose function will be to monitor the application and administration of this annex. Likewise, the Sugar Committee will monitor the application of the preferential sugar quota that Mexico grants to Costa Rica based on the qualities and prices offered by Costa Rica. When the Sugar Committee concludes that the quality or price requirements referred to in paragraph 4 are not met, Mexico may reallocate the quota among other exporting countries in order to meet those requirements. The Sugar Committee shall meet at least once a year or at the request of a Party.
8. For the purposes of this annex and article 4-04, sugar shall be understood as the tariff fractions described in the Mexican General Import Tax Law Tariff: 1701.11.01, 1701.11.99, 1701.12.01, 1701.12.99 , 1701.91 (except those containing flavorings), 1701.99.01 and 1701.99.99.
9. For the purposes of paragraph 1, originating sugar shall be understood to mean sugar that complies with the corresponding rule of origin established in Chapter V (Rules of Origin).
10. This annex will be valid until December 31, 2007.
Section B - Phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures
Article 4-11: Definitions.
For the purposes of this section, it shall be understood as:
animal: any animal, including domestic animals, fish, and wildlife;
contaminant: any contaminant, including residues of pesticides, fertilizers and agricultural chemicals, as well as veterinary drugs and other foreign substances;
risk assessment: an assessment of:
a. the probability of entry, establishment and spread of a disease or pest and the possible biological, agronomic and economic consequences; Y
b. the likelihood of adverse effects to human, animal, or plant life or health from the presence of an additive, contaminant, toxin, or disease-causing organism in a product;
scientific information: data or information derived from the use of scientific principles and methods;
phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure: a measure, including a criterion related to the final product; a process or production method directly related to the product; a test, inspection, certification, or approval procedure; a relevant statistical method; a sampling procedure; a risk assessment method; a packaging and labeling requirement directly related to food safety; and a quarantine regime, such as a relevant requirement associated with the transport of animals or plants, or with material necessary for their survival during transport, that a Party adopts, maintains or applies to:
a. protect animal or plant life or health in its territory from the risks arising from the introduction, establishment or spread of a pest or disease;
b. protect human, animal or plant life or health in its territory from risks resulting from the presence of an additive, contaminant, toxin or pathogenic organism in a product;
c. protect human life or health in its territory from risks from an organism that causes a pest or disease carried by an animal or plant or a derivative thereof; either
d. prevent or limit other damage to its territory from the introduction, establishment and spread of a pest or disease;
appropriate level of phytosanitary or animal health protection: the level of protection of human, animal or plant life or health that a Party considers adequate;
international standard, guideline or recommendation: a standard, guideline or recommendation:
a. in relation to food safety, that established by the Codex Alimentarius Commission , including that related to product decomposition, prepared by the Codex Alimentarius Committee on Fish and Fishery Products, food additives, contaminants, hygiene practices and analysis and sampling methods;
b. in relation to animal health and zoonoses, the one elaborated under the auspices of the International Office of Epizootics;
c. in relation to plant health, the one prepared under the auspices of the Secretariat of the International Plant Protection Convention; Y
d. that established by, or developed in accordance with, other international organizations agreed upon by the Parties;
pest: any pest including the living stages of any insect, mite, nematode, slug, snail, protozoan, or other invertebrate animal, bacteria, fungi, other parasitic plants or reproductive parts thereof, virus, mycoplasma, weeds, or any similar organism or the same associated with any of the above or any infectious substance that may directly or indirectly damage or cause disease to the terminal plants or their parts and to other processed products or manufactures;
approval procedure: any registration, notification or any other mandatory administrative procedure for:
a. approve the use of an additive for a defined purpose or under defined conditions; either
b. establish a tolerance for a defined purpose or with adherence to defined conditions for a contaminant; in a food, drink, or feed prior to permitting the use or marketing of a food, drink, or feed containing the additive or contaminant;
control or inspection procedure: any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine whether a phytosanitary or animal health measure is being complied with, including sampling, testing, inspection, verification, monitoring, auditing, evaluation of the application of phytosanitary and animal health measures, accreditation , registration, certification or other procedures that involve the physical examination of a product, product packaging, or equipment or facilities directly related to the production, marketing or use of a product, but does not mean an approval procedure;
product: animals, plants and their products and by-products;
vegetable: Any vegetable, including crops of economic, scientific, medicinal, ornamental interest and wild flora;
zone: a country, part of a country, parts of several countries, or all parts of several countries;
area of ​​low pest or disease prevalence: an area in which a specific pest or disease occurs at low levels;
pest or disease free zone: an area in which a specific pest or disease is not present;
Article 4-12: Scope of application.
In order to establish a framework of disciplines and rules that guide the development, adoption and compliance of phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures, the provisions of this section apply to any of those measures that may directly or indirectly affect trade between the Parties. .
Article 4-13: Main rights and obligations.
1. Each Party may, in accordance with this section, establish, adopt, maintain or apply any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure necessary for the protection of human, animal and plant life and health in its territory, even those that are stricter than an international standard, guideline or recommendation.
adoption of measures
2. Each Party may adopt, maintain and apply a phytosanitary and zoosanitary measure that regulates the protection of human, animal or plant life or health. These measures include those that ensure their compliance or application, including those that prohibit the importation of any product from the territory of the Parties, when they do not comply with the applicable requirements, or do not satisfy the approval procedures defined in these measures.
3. Each Party shall ensure that any phytosanitary or animal health measure it adopts, maintains or applies:
a. is based on scientific principles, taking into account, where appropriate, both relevant factors and different geographical conditions;
b. be maintained only when there is a scientific basis to support it; Y
c. that is based on a risk assessment appropriate to the circumstances.
non-discriminatory treatment
4. When similar or identical conditions exist, each Party shall ensure that a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure that it adopts, maintains or applies does not arbitrarily or unjustifiably discriminate between its products and similar products of the other Party, or between products of the other Party. Part and similar products from another country.
unnecessary obstacles
5. Each Party shall ensure that no phytosanitary or animal health measures are prepared, adopted or applied, which have the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade between the Parties. In this sense, phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures will not restrict trade more than is necessary in order to protect human, animal or plant life or health in their territory, taking into account technical and economic feasibility.
covert restrictions
6. No Party may adopt, apply or maintain any phytosanitary or animal health measure that has the purpose or consequence of creating a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties.
Support in non-governmental organizations
7. Each Party shall ensure that any non-governmental body that it relies on for the application of a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure, acts in a manner consistent with this section.
Right to set the level of protection
8. Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, each Party, in order to protect human, animal or plant life or health in its territory, may set its appropriate levels of protection, in accordance with the provisions of Article 4-16.
Article 4-14: Use of international standards.
1. Each Party shall use, as a basis for its phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures, international standards, guidelines, or recommendations or their relevant or imminently adopted elements, except when such measures do not constitute an effective or adequate means to protect life or health. human, animal or vegetable in its territory; for example, due to factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature, or for scientifically justified reasons or because the level of protection considered appropriate is not obtained.
2. A phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure of a Party that conforms to an international standard shall be presumed to be consistent with paragraphs 4 and 5 of Article 4-13.
3. Nothing in paragraph 1 shall be construed to prevent a Party, in the protection of human, animal or plant life or health in its territory from adopting, maintaining or applying any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure, which results in a higher level of protection than would have been obtained if the measure were based on an international standard, guideline or recommendation.
4. When a Party has reason to suppose that a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure of the other Party affects or may adversely affect its exports and the measure is not based on relevant international standards, guidelines or recommendations, it may request to be informed of the reasons. of measure. The other Party will inform it in writing within a period not exceeding 40 days.
5. Each Party shall participate, to the greatest extent possible, in the relevant international standard-setting organizations, including the Codex Alimentarius Commission, the International Office of Epizootics and the International Convention for the Protection of Plants, in order to promote the development and the periodic review of international standards, guidelines and recommendations.
Article 4-15: Equivalence.
1. The Parties will make their respective phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures equivalent to the greatest possible degree or identical when appropriate, without reducing the level of protection of human, animal or plant life or health in their territory without prejudice to the rights that they have. confers this section taking into account international standardization activities, in order to facilitate the trade of products between them.
2. Each importing Party:
a. treat a phytosanitary or animal health measure adopted or maintained by the exporting Party as equivalent to its own, when the latter provides the importing Party with scientific or other information, in accordance with the risk assessment methods agreed by them to objectively demonstrate, with adherence to literal b), that the measure of the exporting Party reaches the appropriate level of protection of the importing Party;
b. may, when there is a scientific basis for it, rule that the measure of the exporting Party does not reach the level of protection that the importing Party deems appropriate; Y
c. shall provide the exporting Party in writing, upon request, with its reasons for a finding in accordance with subparagraph b).
3. Each Party will accept the results of the phytosanitary and zoosanitary control procedures that are carried out in the territory of the other Party, as long as satisfactory guarantees are offered that the product complies with the applicable measure or with the standards that are developed. or maintain in the territory of that Party.
Article 4-16: Risk assessment and appropriate level of protection.
1. In the search for the protection of human, animal or plant life and health in its territory, each Party may carry out risk assessments. In making those evaluations, the Party shall take into account, among other factors related to a product, any of the following:
a. available scientific and technical information;
b. Appropriate risk assessment methods and techniques, developed by international standardization organizations;
c. critical control points in production processes, or methods of operation, handling, packaging, inspection, sampling, or testing;
d. the existence of pests and diseases that need to be taken into account, including the existence of pest and disease free areas and areas of low pest and disease prevalence;
and. ecological and other relevant environmental conditions; either
F. the quarantine measures and applicable treatments that satisfy the importing country such as quarantines, chemical and physical treatments, destruction, reshipment and other measures accepted by the Parties.
2. In accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1, when establishing their appropriate level of protection, taking into account the risk associated from the point of view of the consequences of the introduction, establishment or spread of a pest or disease and, when evaluating risk, each Party shall also take into account, where relevant, the following economic factors:
a. loss of production or sales as a result of the pest or disease;
b. the costs of controlling or eradicating the pest or disease in its territory; Y
c. the cost-effectiveness of other options to limit risks.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2 and subparagraph c) of paragraph 3 of Article 4-13, when a Party carries out a risk assessment and concludes that the scientific knowledge or other information available is insufficient to After completing the assessment, it may provisionally adopt a phytosanitary or animal health measure, basing it on the pertinent information available. Once sufficient information has been submitted to complete the risk assessment, the Party will have a reasonable period of time to complete its assessment, review and, where appropriate, modify the provisional phytosanitary or animal health measure in light of that assessment.
4. When a Party is capable of achieving its appropriate level of protection through the gradual application of a phytosanitary or animal health measure, it may, at the request of the other Party and in accordance with this section, allow such gradual application or grant specific exceptions for the measure. , for limited periods, taking into account the export interests of the requesting Party.
Article 4-17: Adaptation to regional conditions.
1. Each Party shall adapt any of its phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures related to the introduction, establishment or spread of a pest or disease, to the phytosanitary or zoosanitary characteristics of the area where a product subject to that measure is produced and to the area in its territory. to which the product is destined, taking into account any pertinent conditions, including those related to transportation and loading between those zones. When evaluating the phytosanitary or zoosanitary characteristics of an area, taking into account whether it is an area free of pests or diseases, or an area with a low prevalence of these, and can be conserved as such, as the case may be, each Party shall take into account, among other factors:
a. the prevalence of pests and diseases in that area;
b. the existence of eradication and control programs in that area; Y
c. any relevant international standards, guidelines or recommendations.
2. In addition to the provisions of paragraph 1, each Party, when establishing whether an area is free of pests or diseases or an area of ​​low prevalence thereof, shall base its opinion on factors such as geographic conditions, ecosystems, epidemiological surveillance, the effectiveness of the phytosanitary or zoosanitary controls in that area or the recognition of the corresponding international organization.
3. An area in the territory of the exporting Party shall be recognized by the importing Party as an area free of pests or diseases or an area of ​​low pest or disease prevalence, and may be conserved as such, as the case may be, when the exporting Party provides the importing Party scientific or other information sufficient to demonstrate it to the satisfaction of the importing Party. To this end, the exporting Party shall provide reasonable access to its territory to the importing Party for inspection, testing and other relevant procedures.
4. Each Party, subject to any relevant conditions, may, in accordance with this section:
a. adopt, maintain or apply a different risk assessment procedure for an area free of pests or diseases than for an area of ​​low prevalence; either
b. determine a different final destination for the disposal of a product produced in an area free of pests or diseases, than for a product produced in an area of ​​low prevalence of these, including those related to transport and cargo.
5. When adopting, maintaining or applying a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure in relation to the introduction, establishment or spread of a pest or disease, each Party shall grant to a product produced in a pest or disease free zone in the territory of another Party, a treatment no less favorable than that granted to a product produced in a zone free of these in another country that presents the same level of risk. The Party shall use equivalent risk assessment techniques to assess relevant conditions and controls in the pest or disease free zone and in the area adjacent to that zone, and shall take into account any relevant conditions, including those related to transportation and cargo. .
6. The importing Party shall seek, upon request, an agreement with the exporting Party on specific requirements, compliance with which allows a product produced in an area of ​​low prevalence of pests or diseases in the territory of the exporting Party, to be imported into its territory if achieves its appropriate level of protection.
Article 4-18: Control, inspection and approval procedures.
1. Each Party, in relation to any control or inspection procedure that it carries out:
a. initiate and conclude the proceeding in the most expeditious manner possible and no less favorable for a product of another Party than for a like product of the Party or of any other country;
