7. The notification referred to in paragraph 6 will contain:
a. the identification of the competent authority making the notification;
b. the name of the exporter or producer you intend to visit;
c. the date and place of the proposed verification visit;
d. the object and scope of the proposed verification visit, making specific mention of the good or goods subject to verification to which the certificate(s) of origin refer;
and. the names, personal data and positions of the officials who will carry out the verification visit; Y
F. the legal basis for the verification visit.
8. Any modification to the information referred to in subparagraph e) of paragraph 7, shall be notified in writing to the exporter or producer and to the competent authority of the exporting Party before the verification visit. Any modification of the information referred to in paragraphs a), b), c), d) and f) of paragraph 7, will be notified in the terms of paragraph 6.
9. If within 30 days after notification of the verification visit proposed under paragraph 6 is received, the exporter or producer does not provide written consent for the verification visit, the importing Party may deny tariff treatment. preferential to the good or goods that would have been the object of the verification visit.
10. Each Party shall permit the exporter or producer, whose good or goods are the subject of a verification visit, to designate two witnesses to be present during the visit, provided that the witnesses intervene only in that capacity. If there is no designation of witnesses by the exporter or the producer, this omission will not result in the postponement of the visit.
11. Within 120 days following the conclusion of the verification, the competent authority will provide a written resolution to the exporter or producer whose good or goods have been subject to verification in which it determines whether or not the good qualifies as originating, which will include the findings of fact and the legal basis for the determination.
12. When the verification carried out by a Party establishes that the exporter or producer has falsely or unfoundedly certified or declared more than once that a good qualifies as originating, the importing Party may suspend the preferential tariff treatment of the goods. identical products that that person exports or produces, until they prove that they comply with the provisions of Chapter V (Rules of Origin).
13. Each Party shall provide that, when it determines that a certain good imported into its territory does not qualify as originating in accordance with the tariff classification or the value applied by that Party to one or more materials used in the production of the good, and this differs from the tariff classification or the value applied to the materials by the Party from whose territory the good has been exported, the decision of that Party shall not take effect until it notifies in writing both the importer of the good and the person who has filled and signed the certificate of origin that protects it.
14. The Party shall not apply a ruling made under paragraph 13 to an import made before the date the ruling takes effect, provided that the competent authority of the Party from whose territory the good was exported has issued a ruling or a advance judgment on the tariff classification or value of materials, on which a person may rely in accordance with its laws and regulations.
15. When a Party denies preferential tariff treatment to a good pursuant to a ruling made in accordance with paragraph 13, that Party shall postpone the effective date of the denial for a period not to exceed 90 days, provided that the importer of the good good or the exporter or producer who has completed and signed the certificate or declaration of origin that protects it, accredits having relied in good faith, to its own detriment, on the tariff classification or value applied to the materials by the customs authority of the Party of whose territory the good was exported.
16. Each Party will maintain the confidentiality of the information collected in the origin verification process in accordance with the provisions of its legislation.
Article 6-08: Review and challenge.
1. Each Party shall grant the same rights to review and challenge resolutions for determination of origin and advance criteria, provided for an importer in its territory, to an exporter or a producer of the other Party that:
a. fill out and sign a certificate or declaration of origin that covers a good that has been the subject of a determination of origin according to paragraph 11 of article 6-07; either
b. received advance judgment pursuant to section 6-10.
2. The rights referred to in paragraph 1 include access to at least one instance of administrative review, independent of the official or agency responsible for the resolution subject to review, and access to a level of judicial or quasi-judicial review of the resolution or decision made at the final level of administrative review, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
Article 6-09: Penalties.
Each Party shall establish or maintain criminal, civil or administrative sanctions for violations of its laws and regulations related to the provisions of this chapter.
Article 6-10: Advance criteria.
1. Each Party shall provide that, through its competent authority, prior written criteria be granted expeditiously prior to the importation of a good into its territory. The anticipated criteria will be issued to the importer in its territory or to the exporter or producer in the territory of the other Party, based on the facts and circumstances stated by them regarding whether the goods qualify as originating according to the established rules of origin. in chapter V (Rules of origin).
2. The anticipated criteria will deal with:
a. if the non-originating materials used in the production of a good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification indicated in the annex to article 5-03 (Specific Rules of Origin);
b. if the good meets the regional content value requirement established in Chapter V (Rules of Origin);
c. if the method applied by the exporter or producer in the territory of the other Party, in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code, to calculate the transaction value of the good or materials used in the production of a good with respect to which an advance criterion is requested, it is adequate, to determine if the good complies with the requirement of regional value content according to chapter V (Rules of origin);
d. whether the method applied by the exporter or producer in the territory of the other Party for the reasonable allocation of costs in accordance with the annex to Article 5-01 (Net cost) is adequate to determine whether a good meets the value content requirement regional according to chapter V (Rules of origin);
and. if the country of origin marking carried out or proposed for a good satisfies the provisions of article 3-12 (Country of Origin Marking); Y
F. Other matters that the Parties agree.
3. Each Party shall adopt or maintain procedures for the issuance of advance criteria upon publication thereof, including:
a. information reasonably required to process a request;
b. The power of its competent authority to request additional information at any time from the person requesting the advance judgment during the application evaluation process;
c. a period of 120 days for the competent authority to issue the advance ruling once it has obtained all the necessary information from the person requesting it; Y
d. the obligation to fully explain, founded and motivated to the applicant the reasons for the anticipated judgment when it is unfavorable for the applicant.
4. Each Party shall apply the advance criteria to imports into its territory from the date of issuance of the criterion or from a later date indicated therein, unless the advance criterion is modified or revoked in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 6.
5. Each Party shall grant to any person who requests an advance judgment, the same treatment, the same interpretation and application of the provisions of Chapter V (Rules of Origin) referring to the determination of origin, that it has granted to any other person to the that has issued an early judgment, when the facts and circumstances are identical in all substantial aspects.
6. The anticipated criterion may be modified or revoked by the competent authority in the following cases:
a. when it was founded on some error:
i) in fact;
ii) in the tariff classification of a good or a material;
iii) whether the good meets the regional value content requirement;
b. when it is not in accordance with an interpretation agreed between the Parties or a modification with respect to article 312 (Marking of country of origin) or chapter V (Rules of origin);
c. when the circumstances or facts that support it change; either
d. in order to comply with an administrative or judicial decision.
7. Each Party shall provide that any modification or revocation of an advance ruling takes effect on the date it is issued or on a later date established therein and may not be applied to imports of a good made before those dates, unless that the person to whom it has been issued has not acted in accordance with its terms and conditions.
8. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 7, the Party issuing the advance judgment shall postpone the effective date of the modification or revocation for a period not to exceed 90 days, when the person to whom it has been issued the advance criterion has been based on that criterion in good faith and to its detriment.
9. Each Party shall provide that, when considering the regional value content of a good for which an advance ruling has been issued, its competent authority shall assess whether:
a. the exporter or producer complies with the terms and conditions of the advance judgment;
b. the exporter's or producer's operations are consistent with the circumstances and substantial facts that support that criterion; Y
c. the supporting data and calculations used in applying the method to calculate value or allocate cost are correct in all material respects.
10. Each Party shall provide that when its competent authority determines that any of the requirements set forth in paragraph 9 has not been met, the competent authority may modify or revoke the advance judgment, as the circumstances warrant.
11. Each Party shall provide that, when the competent authority of a Party decides that the advance judgment has been based on incorrect information, the person to whom it was issued shall not be penalized, if he demonstrates that he acted with reasonable care and good faith when stating the facts and circumstances that motivated the anticipated judgment.
12. Each Party shall provide that, when advance ruling is issued to a person who has falsely stated or omitted material facts or circumstances on which the advance ruling is based, or has failed to act in accordance with the terms and conditions thereof, the authority authority that issues the anticipated criteria can apply the measures that the circumstances warrant.
13. The validity of an early judgment will be subject to the permanent obligation of the holder of the early judgment to inform the competent authority of any substantial change in the facts or circumstances on which it relied to issue that judgment.
Article 6-11: Customs Procedures Committee.
1. The Parties establish a Customs Procedures Committee made up of representatives of each of them that will meet at least twice a year, as well as at the request of any of them.
2. It will correspond to the Committee:
a. try to reach agreements on:
i) the interpretation, application and administration of this chapter;
ii) tariff classification and valuation issues related to origin determination resolutions;
iii) the procedures for the request, approval, issuance, modification, revocation and application of the anticipated criteria;
iv) modifications to the certificate or declaration of origin referred to in article 6-02;
v) any other matter referred to it by a Party; Y
b. examine the proposals for administrative or operational modification related to this section on customs matters that may affect the flow of trade between the Parties.
Section B - Customs Administration.
Article 6-12: General principles.
1. The Parties acknowledge:
a. that their competent authorities need to strengthen their cooperation ties;
b. that, to the extent possible, it is convenient to stimulate coordination practices between their competent authorities, defining the fields of action, procedures, terms and scope of assistance, as well as intensifying relations between them in order to exchange experiences that allow for improvement and harmonize applicable customs systems and procedures based on a principle of reciprocity; Y
c. that it is convenient to strengthen the commercial exchange between them through mechanisms that expedite the transit of goods and customs clearance operations, without prejudice to the application of controls aimed at avoiding illegal trade, unfair international trade practices and other policies that cause trade distortions.
2. In particular, the Parties shall endeavor to facilitate the customs clearance of originating goods.
3. The Parties shall endeavor not to diminish the degree of compliance of the customs facilitation measures agreed upon by them relating to this section upon the entry into force of this Agreement.
Article 6-13 : Cooperation and mutual assistance.
1. In relation to subparagraph a) of paragraph 1 of Article 6-12, the Parties will give priority to the areas of harmonization of procedures, information technology and training.
2. The Parties shall endeavor to organize on a cost-recovery basis training programs in customs matters that include:
a. training for officials directly involved in customs procedures; Y
b. user training.
Article 6-14: International transit of goods.
The Parties will simplify, to the extent of their possibilities, and make the users aware of the procedures for international transit of goods, the required documentation, the conditions required for the transport units, the hours of operation of the customs, the information on the authorized means of communication, access and infrastructure of the customs of the Parties.
Article 6-15: Dispatch of goods.
1. Each Party shall ensure that its competent authority carries out the immediate clearance of goods from the other Party that enter its territory. For these purposes, as far as possible, automated controls of residence time and selective or random criteria for review, weighing, and physical verification will be used.
2. The Parties will seek the elimination or simplification of documents for internal transit and will allow importers to request the change of customs regime in accordance with the legislation of the importing Party.
3. Each Party shall inform the other Party of the procedures that facilitate and expedite the dispatch of goods, including the requirements for their entry into the territory of the Party, for the reception, unloading and storage in accordance with the import and export regimes of goods, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
4. The dispatch related to the import and export of goods may be carried out through automated verification systems according to selectivity or randomness criteria. The competent authorities of the Parties may establish internally, under the conditions and terms established by them, the modalities of physical or documentary verification and direct dispatch in companies.
5. The Parties shall establish a common format for the import or export of goods. While the date of its entry into force has not been agreed, each Party will continue to use the declaration or petition provided by its legislation.
Article 6-16: Internment of transport units.
1. Each Party shall ensure that its competent authority applies expedited procedures that facilitate the temporary entry of transport units.
2. The procedures referred to in paragraph 1 shall be, to the extent possible, computerized, uniform, and shall contemplate registration in a register of transport units and companies of each Party. Registration in this registry will allow the entry of transport units into the territory of the Parties, subject to the other conditions established by the Customs Coordination Committee. Their period of stay will be 30 days from the date of their entry into the territory of the importing Party.
3. The competent authorities of the Parties shall use a common format for the temporary importation of transport units.
4. For the purposes of this article and article 6-14, the following shall be understood as:
a. transport units: trailers, semi-trailers and special cargo transport equipment; Y
b. special cargo transport equipment: those trailers or semi-trailers exclusively used for the transport of certain goods, such as liquids, gases, refrigerated goods or vehicles.
Article 6-17: Fairs and exhibitions.
The Parties will provide facilities in all customs procedures and services for holding fairs, exhibitions or other events of a similar nature.
Article 6-18: Samples or samples.
Each Party will grant facilities for the entry into its territory of samples or samples and will prepare instructions for samples or samples in which it will include the procedure and the commercial, banking or customs documentation necessary to identify the samples or samples subject to importation.
Article 6-19: Passenger baggage.
Each Party shall simplify customs procedures and formalities, in accordance with its legislation, for the entry into its territory of passenger goods and baggage.
Article 6-20: A Use of electronic information systems.
1. Each Party, taking into account its possibilities, will implement systems for the electronic transmission of information for customs management.
2. Each Party shall establish rules for the operation of electronic information transmission systems that include:
a. use of user codes and access codes;
b. probative value of data and records;
c. confidentiality of information;
d. responsibility of the officials who operate the system and of the users; Y
and. the information storage system.
Article 6-21 : Exchange of information.
The Parties shall exchange, through their competent authorities, information and experience, to the extent of their possibilities, on:
a. customs classification and valuation;
b. rules of origin;
c. documents and requirements for import and export;
d. import and export statistics, in terms of the legislation of each Party;
and. goods subject to non-tariff measures; Y
F. customs regimes and procedures.
Article 6-22: Customs Coordination Committee.
The Parties establish a Customs Coordination Committee made up of the representative of each Party as established in the annex to this article, or the persons designated by them. The Committee shall be in charge of the development, application and administration of this section.
Article 6-23: Functions of the Customs Coordination Committee.
1. The Customs Coordination Committee will have the following functions:
a. propose uniform guidelines for the improvement of customs procedures;
b. propose uniform formats for official customs documents;
c. seek the establishment of mechanisms that allow the exchange of information and experiences on the application of customs procedures;
d. inform the Commission of any customs procedure that is incompatible with the provisions of this section; Y
and. report annually to the Commission on its activities.
2. The Committee will meet at least once a year, and at the request of any Party, within 30 days following the date of the request.
Annex to article 6-02
The Parties shall establish, no later than January 1 , 1995, a common format for the "certificate of origin" and the "declaration of origin", which may be modified by agreement of the Parties.
Annex to article 6-22
For purposes of Article 6-22, the representative of the Parties is:
a. in the case of Costa Rica, the Director General of Customs or his successor; Y
b. in the case of Mexico, the General Customs Administrator or his successor.
 
Chapter VII
Safeguard measures
Article 7-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
competent authority: the competent authority as provided in the annex to this article;
direct competitor good: that which, not being identical or similar to the one being compared, is essentially equivalent for commercial purposes, because it is dedicated to the same use and is interchangeable with it;
identical good: that which coincides in all its characteristics with the good being compared;
Similar good: that which, although it does not coincide in all its characteristics with the good that is being compared, presents some identical ones, especially in its nature, use, function and quality;
Serious prejudice: a general and significant impairment of a domestic industry;
domestic industry: the producer or producers of identical, similar or directly competitive goods that operate within the territory of a Party and constitute a significant proportion of the total domestic production of those goods. This significant proportion may not be less than 35%.
Article 7-02: General provisions.
The Parties may apply to imports of goods carried out in accordance with the Tariff Elimination Program safeguard measures whose application will be based on clear, strict criteria and with a defined temporality. The Parties may adopt safeguard measures of a bilateral or global nature.
Article 7-03: Bilateral measures.
1. The Parties may adopt and apply bilateral measures up to 24 months after the customs duty for the good in question under the Tariff Elimination Program reaches zero, if the import volume of one or several goods benefited by the Program of Tariff Reduction increases at a rate and under such conditions that it causes serious damage to the national production of identical, similar or direct competitive goods.
2. Bilateral measures may only be applied when they are strictly necessary to offset the serious injury caused by the imports referred to in paragraph 1.
3. The bilateral measures will be temporary and of a tariff type. The customs duty that is determined in no case may exceed the lesser of:
a. the customs tariff in force against third countries for that good on the date of adoption of the bilateral measure; Y
b. the customs duty corresponding to the good the day before the entry into force of the Tariff Reduction Program.
4. The measures may be adopted for a single occasion and applied for a period of up to one year and may be extended for a single time and for up to an equal and consecutive period.
5. Upon concluding the application of the bilateral measure, the tariff rate that will apply to the good in question will be the one that corresponds to it on that date according to the Tariff Elimination Program.
6. The Party that decides to initiate a procedure that could result in the adoption of a bilateral measure, will notify the other Party in writing and request consultations in accordance with the provisions of Article 7-05.
7. The Party that intends to apply a bilateral measure shall grant the affected Party mutually agreed compensation, which shall consist of additional tariff concessions whose effects on the trade of the exporting Party are equivalent to the impact of the measure. If the Parties fail to agree on compensation, the Party that intends to apply the bilateral measure will be empowered to apply it and the Party affected by that measure may suspend tariff concessions that have trade effects equivalent to those of the measure adopted.
8. The compensation referred to in paragraph 7 will be determined at the stage of consultations prior to the application of bilateral measures.
Article 7-04: Global measures.
1. The Parties retain their rights and obligations to apply safeguard measures in accordance with Article XIX of the GATT.
2. When a Party decides to adopt a safeguard measure in accordance with Article XIX of the GATT, it may only apply it to the other Party when imports from that Party, considered individually, represent a substantial part of total imports and contribute significantly to serious prejudice to the importing Party. For this determination, the following criteria will be taken into account, among others:
a. it will be considered that the originating imports of the other Party are substantial, if they are included within the imports of the main supplying countries, of the good subject to the procedure whose exports represent 80% of the total imports of that good in the importing Party;
b. imports originating in a Party shall not normally be considered to be a significant contributor to serious injury if their growth rate during the period in which the injurious increase of such imports occurred is substantially less than the growth rate of imports from all sources during the same period;
c. Changes in the Party's share in total imports and their volume will also be taken into account for the determination of significant participation in serious damage.
3. In no case may the importing Party apply the measures set forth in paragraph 2 without prior written communication to the other Party and without prior consultations. For this purpose, all notification and procedural requirements set forth in this chapter shall be met.
4. The Party that intends to apply a global measure grant to the affected Party mutually agreed compensation, in the form of concessions that have commercial effects equivalent to the impact of that measure. If the Parties are unable to agree on compensation, the Party proposing to apply the global measure will be empowered to apply it, and the affected Party may impose measures that have trade effects equivalent to those of the adopted measure.
5. The compensation referred to in article 7-03 will be determined at the stage of consultations prior to the application of global measures.
Article 7-05: Procedure.
1. Each Party shall establish clear and strict procedures for the adoption and application of safeguard measures, in accordance with this Chapter.
2. To determine the origin of the application of a safeguard measure, the competent authority of the importing Party will carry out the pertinent investigation.
3. The Party that decides to initiate an investigation to adopt safeguard measures will publish the initiation of the same in the corresponding official dissemination bodies and will notify the exporting Party in writing the day after the publication.
4. For the purposes of determining serious prejudice, the competent authorities will evaluate all the factors of an objective and quantifiable nature that are related to the affected industry, in particular the rate and amount of the increase in imports of the good in question. , in absolute and relative terms, the part of the domestic market absorbed by the increase in imports, changes in the level of sales, domestic prices, production, productivity, utilization of installed capacity, market share, profits and losses, and employment.
5. To determine the origin of the safeguard measures, a direct causal relationship will also be demonstrated between the increase in imports of the good in question and the serious damage to the domestic industry.
6. If there are factors other than the increase in imports from the other Party that simultaneously harm the domestic industry, the damage caused by those factors cannot be attributed to the aforementioned imports.
7. If as a result of this investigation the competent authority determines, based on objective evidence, that the assumptions set forth in this chapter are met, the importing Party may initiate consultations with the other Party.
8. The consultation procedure does not oblige the Parties to reveal information that has been provided confidentially, the disclosure of which may impede compliance with the laws of the Party that regulate the matter or harm commercial interests. Notwithstanding this, the importing Party that intends to apply the safeguard measure shall provide the other Party with a non-confidential summary of the confidential information.
9. The period for prior consultations will begin on the day following the receipt by the exporting Party of the notification requesting the initiation of consultations. The prior consultation period will be 45 days unless the Parties agree on a shorter period.
10. The notification referred to in paragraph 9 will be made through the competent national authority and will contain sufficient information to support the application of the measures, including:
a. the names and available addresses of the national producers of identical or similar goods or direct competitors representative of the national production, their participation in the national production of that good and the reasons that lead them to affirm that they are representative of that sector;
b. a clear and complete description of the good subject to the procedure, the tariff subheading in which it is classified and the current tariff treatment, as well as the description of the identical, similar or direct competitive good;
c. import data for each of the three most recent calendar years that provide the basis that the good is being imported in increasing quantities, either in absolute terms or relative to domestic production;
d. the data on the total national production of the identical, similar or directly competitive good corresponding to the last three most recent calendar years;
and. data demonstrating serious injury caused by imports to the sector in question in accordance with paragraphs 4 and 5;
F. an enumeration and a description of the presumed causes of the injury, and a summary of the grounds for alleging that the increase in imports of that good in either relative or absolute terms of national production is the cause thereof;
g. where appropriate, the criteria and objective information that demonstrates that the assumptions established in this chapter are met for the application of a global measure to the other Party; Y
h. information on the tariff measures that are intended to be adopted and their duration.
11. The measures provided for in this chapter may only be adopted once the prior consultation period has concluded.
12. During the consultation period, the exporting Party will make all the observations it deems pertinent, particularly regarding the admissibility of the proposed measures.
13. If the importing Party determines that the reasons that gave rise to the application of the safeguard measures subsist, it shall notify the competent authorities of the other Party, at least 60 days prior to the expiration of the validity of those measures, its intention to extend them, and provide information to support this decision, including evidence that the causes that led to the adoption of the safeguard measure persist. The notification, the prior consultations on the extension and the respective compensation will be carried out in the terms provided in this chapter.
Annex toarticle 7-01
For the purposes of this chapter, the competent authority shall mean:
a. in the case of Costa Rica, the Ministry of Foreign Trade or its successor; Y
b. in the case of Mexico, the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development or its successor.
Chapter VIII
Provisions regarding countervailing duties
Article 8-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
investigation: an investigation procedure on unfair international trade practices;
Interested party: the complainant producers, importers, exporters of the goods under investigation, as well as any national or foreign person who has a direct interest in the investigation in question, and includes the government of the Party whose goods are subject to investigation. an investigation on subsidies;
definitive resolution: the resolution of the competent authority that determines whether or not the imposition of definitive countervailing duties is appropriate;
initiation resolution: the resolution of the competent authority that formally declares the initiation of an investigation;
preliminary resolution: the resolution of the competent authority that determines the continuation of an investigation and, where appropriate, whether or not the imposition of provisional countervailing duties is appropriate;
direct export subsidies: those classified as prohibited subsidies in the Agreement on Subsidies and Countervailing Measures of the GATT of 1994.
Article 8-02: General principle.
The Parties reject all unfair international trade practices and recognize the need to eliminate export subsidies and other internal policies that cause trade distortions.
Article 8-03: Direct export subsidies.
1. Neither Party shall grant new direct subsidies for the export of its goods to the territory of the other Party after the entry into force of this Agreement.
2. Each Party shall eliminate direct export subsidies, existing on a good on the date of entry into force of this Agreement, exported to the territory of the other Party, when the customs duty that the importing Party applies to the exporting Party on that well under the Tariff Elimination Program, reach the level of zero.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 2, each Party shall eliminate direct subsidies for the export of its goods to the territory of the other Party on January 1 , 1999.
4. Notwithstanding what is established in paragraphs 2 and 3, and only during the period in which direct export subsidies remain in force, the Parties may impose countervailing duties on direct export subsidies when the importing Party of benefited goods With these subsidies, consider that their granting has unfavorable effects on your trade. The procedure against direct export subsidies will be governed in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 8 to 10 of this article.
5. For the purposes of paragraph 4, there may be unfavorable effects on the trade of the importing Party, when the subsidized exports have as a consequence, due to the direct export subsidy received:
a. a significant change in market share unfavorable to the identical or similar good of the importing Party;
b. significant price reduction or suppression of the importing Party's identical or similar good, or loss of sales in the same market; either
c. a significant and sustained increase in the growth rate of subsidized imports.
6. It shall not be concluded that there are unfavorable effects on the trade of the importing Party, if the exporting Party reasonably demonstrates with the information available that the subsidy has not produced the effects referred to in subparagraphs a), b) or c) of paragraph 5.
7. The importing Party shall offer its cooperation, to the extent possible, to the exporting Party for the purpose of providing it with information.
8. Each Party may request in writing that the other Party hold consultations on the provisions of this article. Consultations will be held and concluded within 30 days of receipt of the request.
9. If the Parties do not reach an agreement regarding the direct export subsidy in question and the exporting Party does not suspend its granting within 30 days from the conclusion of the consultations, the importing Party may impose countervailing duties. in the amount necessary to eliminate the unfavorable effect on their trade, which in no case will exceed the total amount of the direct export subsidy granted to those goods.
10. The exporting Party will have a period of 60 days from the start of the consultations to present to the importing Party evidence that the direct export subsidies have not produced the unfavorable effects on the importing Party's trade referred to. refer to literals a), b) or c) of paragraph 5.
Article 8-04: Principles for the application of national legislation.
1. Each Party shall uniformly, impartially and reasonably apply its legislation on unfair international trade practices in a manner consistent with the provisions of this Chapter, with the principles of the GATT, the Agreement Relating to the Application of Article VI of the GATT and of the GATT Agreement on Subsidies and Countervailing Measures.
2. The Parties will carry out the investigations through the competent national public agencies, agencies or entities and will not apply, in their bilateral relationship, any international instrument negotiated with third countries that implies asymmetric, non-reciprocal treatment and that deviates from the provisions in this chapter.
Article 8-05: Obligation to terminate an investigation.
1. The importing Party shall terminate an investigation:
a. with respect to an interested party, when its competent authority determines that:
i) the dumping or subsidy margin is de minimis; either
ii) there is insufficient evidence of dumping, subsidy or injury; either
b. when its competent authority determines that the volume of the dumped or subsidized imports, or the damage is negligible.
2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, it will be considered that:
a. the dumping margin is de minimis when it is less than 2% expressed as a percentage of the export price;
b. the subsidy margin is de minimis when it is less than 1.5% ad valorem; Y
c. the volume of the dumped or subsidized imports or the injury is negligible if the volume of the imports represents less than 1% of the domestic market or if it represents less than 3% of the importing Party's total imports of the identical or similar goods .
3. For the purposes of subparagraph c) of paragraph 2, the domestic market shall be understood as apparent national consumption understood as the sum of national production plus total imports minus exports of identical or similar goods.
Article 8-06: Proof of damage.
Each Party will carry out the damage test as a prerequisite for the imposition of countervailing duties.
Article 8-07 : Accumulation.
For the purposes of establishing the existence of damage, threat of damage or appreciable delay in the creation of a production, the determination of the effects of imports from several countries and that are simultaneously subject to investigation in the importing Party, shall not be accumulated. imports from the other Party when:
a. the dumping or subsidy margin is de minimis, or the volume of imports from the other Party is insignificant, in accordance with the provisions of Article 8-05; either
b. the growth rate of the volume of imports of the other Party under investigation and its share in the domestic market, does not show any indication of a sustained increase during the investigated period or the real probability that it will increase in the immediate future; their sales in the national market are isolated and sporadic and, due to the nature of the investigated good, as well as the specific characteristics of the national market, the presence of these imports does not have any identifiable influence on domestic prices or on the factors that influence prices. the prices of the national good and the conditions of the national industry that produces an identical or similar good.
Article 8-08: Regional damage.
1. For the purposes of this article, an isolated market shall be understood, with respect to the production of a specific good, as the division that, in exceptional circumstances, is made by a Party of its territory into two or more competing markets for the purposes of considering the production of each market as a distinct output if:
a. the producers in that market sell all or nearly all of their production of that good in that market; Y
b. Simultaneously, the producers of the good located elsewhere in the territory do not satisfy the demand in that market to a substantial degree.
2. It may be considered that there is injury even when a significant portion of the total national production is not injured, provided that there is a concentration of dumped or subsidized imports in an isolated market and those imports cause injury to the producers of all or almost all of the production of that market.
3. When the imposition of provisional or final compensatory duties is determined, importers whose affected goods are destined for a market outside the isolated market in question may request the investigating authority not to impose these compensatory duties.
4. Once the request and the evidence that proves the facts described in paragraph 3 have been submitted, importers may choose to pay the compensatory fee or guarantee payment thereof. The investigating authority will decide what is relevant within 130 business days following receipt of the request. At any time, the investigating authority may order any procedure in order to ascertain the veracity of the importers' statements.
5. If in the corresponding resolution the investigating authority confirms the compensatory quota, the guarantees that have been granted will become effective. If in that resolution the compensatory duty was revoked, in favor of the interested importer, the guarantees will be canceled or, where appropriate, the amounts that have been paid will be returned.
6. The resolution of the investigating authority in the terms of paragraph 4 shall be published in the official publication of the importing Party and the interested importers shall be personally notified.
Article 8-09: Publication of resolutions.
The Parties will publish in their official dissemination bodies the resolutions on the matter, those that declare the administrative investigation concluded due to commitments by the foreign exporter or, where appropriate, by the government of the exporting Party, or by holding conciliatory hearings, as well as the resolutions by which the complaints are dismissed or the denouncements of the complainants are accepted.
Article 8-10: Notifications and deadlines.
1. The competent authorities of each Party shall carry out all reasonable actions within their reach to identify and locate those interested in the investigation in order to guarantee the exercise of the right to legitimate defense and shall notify the resolutions in writing directly to the interested parties of whom it is aware, to the government of the other Party, in the case of a subsidy investigation, and to the competent authority of the other Party.
2. The notification of the initiation resolution shall be sent by the most expeditious means of postal mail available to the competent authorities of each Party within a period of five business days following the day of its publication in the official body of dissemination of the Part. The notification will include the following information:
a. deadlines for submitting reports, declarations and other documents;
b. the place where the complaint and other documents presented during the investigation can be inspected; Y
c. the name, address, and telephone number of the office where additional information can be obtained.
3. With the notification referred to in paragraph 2, a copy of the respective publication in the official publication of the Party conducting the investigation shall be sent, as well as a copy of the written complaint and the public version of its annexes.
4. The competent authorities of each Party shall grant the interested parties a minimum response period of 30 business days from the official publication of the initiation of the investigation in order for them to appear to state what is right to them. The same term will be granted for the same effects to the interested parties as of the official publication of the preliminary resolution.
5. The initial, preliminary or final resolutions will contain, when appropriate, at least the following:
a. the name of the applicant or other petitioner;
b. the indication of the imported good subject to investigation and its tariff classification;
c. the elements and evidence used to determine the existence of dumping or subsidy, damage and its causal relationship;
d. the factual and legal considerations that led the investigating authority to initiate an investigation or impose a countervailing duty; Y
and. any legal reasoning, data, fact or circumstance that is recorded in the administrative file, on which the resolution in question is based and motivates.
Article 8-11: Rights and obligations of the interested parties.
The Parties shall ensure that interested parties have the same rights and obligations in an investigation.
Article 8-12: Conciliatory hearings.
In the course of the investigation, any interested party may request the competent authority to hold conciliatory hearings in order to reach a satisfactory solution.
Article 8-13: Preliminary resolution.
1. Within a period of 130 days, but in no case before 45 days, counted from the publication of the initiation resolution, the competent authority will issue a preliminary resolution. The preliminary resolution will determine if it is appropriate to continue with the investigation and, if applicable, the imposition and amount of the provisional countervailing duties.
2. With the exception of confidential information, when the preliminary resolution determines the imposition of countervailing duties, in addition to the corresponding data indicated in paragraph 5 of article 8-10, it will include:
a. the normal value of the good subject to investigation, its export price, the dumping or subsidy margin and its incidence in the export price obtained by the investigating authority; as well as a description of the methodology that was followed to determine them;
b. a description of the damage or threat of damage to the national production and the explanation of the analysis of each one of the factors that have been taken into account; Y
c. where appropriate, the amount of the provisional compensatory quota.
Article 8-14: Retroactive application of countervailing duties.
The retroactive application of countervailing duties shall be subject to the provisions of Article 10 of the Agreement on the Application of Article VI of the GATT 1994 and Article 20 of the Agreement on Subsidies and Countervailing Measures of the GATT 1994.
Article 8-15: Clarifications.
1. Once a provisional or definitive compensatory quota has been issued, the interested parties may request the competent authority to decide whether a particular asset is subject to the compensatory quota imposed or to clarify any aspect of the corresponding resolution.
2. In the procedure to determine if an asset is subject to the compensatory duty imposed, the corresponding substantive and procedural provisions set forth in this chapter for an investigation in accordance with the provisions of article 8-04 will be observed.
Article 8-16: Import of parts or components.
The importation of parts or components of goods subject to provisional or final countervailing duties intended for assembly operations in the territory of a Party; the assembly of these parts or components in a third country to export them as finished goods, or the export of goods with relatively minor physical differences with respect to what is subject to provisional or final countervailing duties in order to avoid payment thereof, will cause the importation of these parts, components or goods is subject to the payment of the corresponding compensatory quota.
Article 8-17: Review of quotas.
1. The definitive compensatory quotas may be reviewed by the competent authority, annually at the request of the interested party and at any time ex officio, in the event of a change in circumstances. Likewise, any producer, importer or exporter who, without having participated in the investigation, accredits his legal interest, may request the review of a countervailing duty.
2. The review may have the effect of ratifying, modifying or eliminating the corresponding fees.
3. In the final countervailing duty review procedure, the substantive and procedural provisions set forth in this chapter shall be observed in accordance with the provisions of article 8-04.
Article 8-18: Automatic elimination of definitive countervailing duties.
Definitive countervailing duties will be eliminated automatically when, after five years from their effective date or from the date of the last review, they have not been reviewed in accordance with the provisions of article 8-17.
Article 8-19: Sending copies.
Each interested party will timely send to the other interested parties copies of each of the reports, documents and evidence that it submits to the investigating authority in the course of the investigation, excluding confidential information.
Article 8-20: Information meetings.
1. The investigative authority of the importing Party, upon request of the interested parties, will hold information meetings in order to disclose all pertinent information on the content of the preliminary and final resolutions.
2. Regarding preliminary resolutions, the request referred to in paragraph 1 may be submitted at any time during the investigation. In the case of final resolutions, the request shall be submitted within five days following its publication in the official dissemination body of the Party. In both cases, the competent authority will carry out the information gathering within a period of 15 days from the presentation of the request.
3. In the information meetings referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2, the interested parties will have the right to review the technical reports, the methodology, the spreadsheets and any other element on which the corresponding resolution has been based, with the exception of of confidential information.
Article 8-21: Public hearings.
1. The competent authority will hold, ex officio or at the request of a party, a public hearing in which the interested parties may appear and question their counterparts regarding the information or evidence that the investigating authority deems appropriate.
2. The competent authority will notify the holding of the public hearing 15 working days in advance.
3. The competent authority will give the interested parties the opportunity to present arguments after the public hearing, even if the period for the presentation of evidence had ended. The allegations will consist of the written presentation of conclusions related to the information and argumentation provided in the investigation.
Article 8-22: Access to confidential information.
Within the constitutional framework of each Party, the independent advisers or lawyers of the parties in the investigation may have access to confidential information of their counterparts for the exclusive purpose of defending their interests, subject to a strict confidentiality commitment, the violation of which will be sanctioned according to to the legislation of each Party.
Article 8-23: Access to non-confidential information.
The competent authority of each Party will give interested parties timely access to the non-confidential information contained in the administrative files of any other investigation, within the term provided by the legislation of each Party, but in no case later than 60 days from of the definitive resolution of these investigations in accordance with the provisions of its internal legal system. If other administrative or judicial appeals have been filed against the final resolution, the Parties will grant such access to non-confidential information in accordance with their domestic legal system.
Article 8-24: Refund of amounts paid in excess.
If a compensatory duty lower than the provisional compensatory duty is determined in a final resolution, the competent authority of the importing Party shall refund the amounts paid in excess.
Article 8-25: Settlement of disputes.
When the final decision of an arbitral tribunal, rendered in accordance with Chapter XVII (Dispute Settlement) declares that the application of a countervailing duty by a Party is incompatible with any provision of this chapter, the importing Party shall cease to apply the countervailing duty. in question to the respective assets of the complaining Party.
Chapter IX
General principles on trade in services
Article 9-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
company: any legal person, constituted or organized under the laws of the Party, whether or not for profit and privately or governmental property, as well as other organizations or economic units that are constituted or, in any case, duly organized under that legislation, such as branches, trusts, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures or other associations;
enterprise of a Party: an enterprise incorporated or organized under the laws of a Party and having its domicile in the territory of that Party; and a branch located in the territory of a Party that carries out business activities therein;
federal, central or state governments: which includes non-governmental organizations that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated by those governments;
measure: any measure adopted by a Party whether in the form of a law, regulation, rule, procedure, administrative decision or provision, requirement or authorized practice, or in any form;
service provider of a Party: a person of the Party who intends to provide or provides a service;
quantitative restrictions: a non-discriminatory measure that imposes limitations on:
a. the number of service providers, whether through a quota, monopoly or an economic necessity test, or by any other quantitative means; either
b. the operations of any service provider, whether through a quota, monopoly or an economic necessity test, or by any other quantitative means;
specialized air services: aerial mapping; aerial surveying; aerial photography; forest fire control; Firefighting; aerial advertising; gliders towing; skydiving services; aerial services for construction; air transport of logs; scenic flights; training flights; aerial inspection and surveillance and aerial spraying;
professional services: services that require higher specialized university education for their provision and the exercise of which is authorized or restricted by a Party, but does not include services provided by persons who practice a trade or to the crew of merchant ships and aircraft.
Article 9-02: Scope of application.
1. This Chapter applies to measures that a Party adopts or maintains on trade in services carried out by service providers of the other Party, including those relating to:
a. the production, distribution, marketing, sale and provision of a service;
b. the purchase, use or payment of a service;
c. access to, and use of, distribution and transportation systems in connection with the provision of a service;
d. access to, and use of, public telecommunications networks and services;
and. the presence in its territory of a service provider of the other Party;
F. the granting of a bond or other form of financial guarantee, as a condition for the provision of a service.
2. For the purposes of this chapter, trade in services is defined as the supply of a service:
a. from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party;
b. in the territory of a Party to a consumer of another Party;
c. through the presence of companies providing services of one Party in the territory of another Party;
d. by natural persons of a Party in the territory of another Party.
3. This chapter does not apply to:
a. air services, including national and international air transport, with and without a fixed itinerary, as well as auxiliary activities in support of air services, except:
i) aircraft repair and maintenance services during the period in which an aircraft is withdrawn from service;
ii) specialized air services; Y
iii) computerized reservation systems;
b. financial services;
c. subsidies or grants provided by a Party or a State enterprise, including government-supported loans, guarantees and insurance; neither
d. government services or functions such as, but not limited to, law enforcement, rehabilitation services, income security or insurance, social security or insurance, social welfare, public education, public training, health and care for children.
4. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to:
a. impose any obligation on a Party with respect to a national of another Party who seeks to enter its labor market or who has permanent employment in its territory, nor to confer any right on that national, with respect to that income or employment; neither
b. impose any obligation or grant any right to a Party, with respect to government purchases made by a Party or a State enterprise.
5. For purposes of this Chapter, "measures that a Party adopts or maintains" shall mean measures adopted or maintained by:
a. the federal, central and state governments, if applicable; Y
b. non-governmental organizations that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated to them by those governments.
6. Regarding the non-governmental organizations mentioned in subparagraph b) of paragraph 5 that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated to them in accordance with the legislation of each Party, the federal or central government will take the measures reasonable within their power to bring such agencies into compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
7. The provisions of this chapter shall apply to the measures related to the services contemplated in its annexes only to the extent and terms stipulated in those annexes.
Article 9-03: Most favored nation treatment.
1. Each Party shall accord to services and service providers of another Party treatment no less favorable than that accorded, in similar circumstances, to services and service providers of any other country.
2. The provisions of this Chapter shall not be interpreted in the sense of preventing a Party from conferring advantages to adjacent countries, in order to facilitate exchanges, limited to contiguous border areas, of services that are produced or consumed locally.
Article 9-04: National treatment.
1. Each Party shall grant to the services and service providers of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that granted in similar circumstances to its own services or service providers.
2. Treatment accorded by a Party pursuant to paragraph 1 means, with respect to a state, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment accorded by that state, in like circumstances, to service providers of the Party to which that belong.
Article 9-05: Local presence.
No Party shall require a service provider of another Party to establish or maintain a representative office or other type of business, or to reside in its territory, as a condition of providing a service.
Article 9-06: Consolidation of measures.
1. No Party shall increase the degree of non-conformity of its existing measures with respect to Articles 9-03 to 9-05. Any amendment to any of these measures will not decrease the degree of compliance of the measure as it was in effect immediately prior to the amendment.
2. The Parties, within a period not exceeding one year from the entry into force of this Agreement or, if that occurs later, the date of entry into force of the General Agreement on Trade in Services (GATS), shall draw up a list of federal and central measures that do not conform to articles 9-03 to 9-05.
3. For state measures that do not conform to articles 9-03 to 9-05, the term to prepare the list will be no more than two years from the entry into force of this Agreement.
4. The Parties are not required to list municipal measures.
Article 9-07: Quantitative restrictions.
1. Each Party will have one year from the date of entry into force of this Agreement to prepare a list of quantitative restrictions that, not including municipal governments, it maintains at the federal or central and state levels.
2. Periodically, at least once every two years, the Parties shall endeavor to negotiate to liberalize or eliminate:
a. existing quantitative restrictions that you maintain:
i) a Party at the federal or central level, according to the list referred to in paragraph 1; either
ii) a state as indicated by a Party on the list referred to in paragraph 1; Y
b. quantitative restrictions that a Party has adopted after the entry into force of this Agreement.
3. Each Party shall notify the other Party of any quantitative restrictions, other than those at the municipal government level, that it adopts after the entry into force of this Agreement, and shall indicate the restriction in the list referred to in paragraph 1.
Article 9-08 : Future liberalization.
Through future negotiations to be convened by the Commission, the Parties will deepen the liberalization achieved in the different service sectors, with a view to achieving the elimination of the remaining restrictions listed in accordance with paragraphs 2 and 3 of Article 9-06.
Article 9-09 : Liberalization of non-discriminatory measures.
Each Party shall prepare a list of its commitments to liberalize quantitative restrictions, requirements for the granting of authorizations, permits or licenses and other non-discriminatory measures.
Article 9-10: Procedures.
The Parties shall establish procedures for:
a. for a Party to notify another Party and include in its relevant lists:
i) federal or central measures, in accordance with paragraph 2 of article 9-06;
ii) State measures, in accordance with paragraph 3 of Article 9-06;
iii) non-discriminatory quantitative restrictions, in accordance with Article 9-07;
iv) the modifications to the measures referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 of article 9-06; Y
v) the measures according to article 9-09;
b. holding future negotiations aimed at perfecting the global liberalization of services between the Parties, in accordance with Article 9-08.
Article 9-11: Disclosure of confidential information.
Nothing in this chapter shall impose an obligation on any Party to provide confidential information the disclosure of which would constitute an obstacle to compliance with laws or otherwise be contrary to the public interest, or could harm the legitimate business interests of public or private companies.
Article 9-12: Granting of permits, authorizations and licenses.
In order to ensure that any measure that a Party adopts or maintains in relation to the requirements and procedures for the granting of permits, authorizations and licenses to nationals of another Party does not constitute an unnecessary barrier to trade, each Party shall endeavor to ensure that those measures:
a. are based on objective and transparent criteria, such as the capacity and aptitude to provide a service;
b. are not more burdensome than necessary to ensure the quality of a service; Y
c. do not constitute a disguised restriction on the cross-border provision of a service.
Article 9-13: Recognition of titles and granting of professional licences.
1. When a Party recognizes or revalidates, unilaterally or by agreement with another country, titles obtained in the territory of another Party or of any country that is not a Party:
a. nothing in Article 9-03 shall be construed to require that Party to recognize or revalidate degrees obtained in the territory of that other Party; Y
b. the Party will provide the other Party with an adequate opportunity to demonstrate that the titles obtained in the territory of that other Party will also be recognized or revalidated, or to negotiate or celebrate an arrangement or agreement that has equivalent effects.
2. Each Party, within a period of two years from the date of entry into force of this Agreement, shall eliminate any requirement of nationality or permanent residence that it maintains for the recognition of titles and the granting of licenses for the professional practice to professional service providers of another Party. Where a Party fails to comply with this obligation with respect to a particular sector, the other Party may, in the same sector and for as long as the non-compliant Party maintains its requirement, maintain, as the sole remedy, an equivalent requirement indicated in the list referred to in Article 9-06 or reinstate by notification to the non-compliant Party:
a. any of those requirements at the federal or central level that it has eliminated in accordance with this article; either
b. any such state-level requirements that would have been in effect on the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
3. The annex to this article establishes procedures for the recognition of titles and granting of licenses that govern professional service providers.
Article 9-14: Commercial practices.
1. The Parties recognize that certain commercial practices of service providers, other than those referred to in subparagraph c) of paragraph 1 of Article 9-19, may limit competition and, therefore, restrict trade in services.
2. Each Party, at the request of another Party, shall enter into consultations with a view to eliminating the practices referred to in paragraph 1. The Party to which the request is made shall consider it fully and with understanding and shall cooperate in facilitating the non-confidential information that is available to the public and that is related to the matter in question. That Party shall also provide other information at its disposal, subject to its law and subject to the conclusion of a satisfactory agreement on the safeguarding of the confidentiality of such information by the requesting Party.
Article 9-15: Denial of benefits.
Each Party may deny the benefits derived from this chapter to a service provider of another Party, prior notification and consultation, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out significant business activities in the territory of that Party. another Party, and which, in accordance with the laws of each Party, is owned or controlled by persons of a non-Party.
Article 9-16: Exceptions.
Provided that the measures listed below are not applied in a way that would constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between countries where similar conditions prevail, or a disguised restriction on international trade in services, nothing in this chapter shall be construed in the sense of preventing a Party from adopting or applying measures:
a. necessary to protect morality and public order;
b. necessary to protect the life and health of people, animals or to preserve plant species in its territory, or for the implementation of rules and regulations of international agreements, to which the Party is a party for the conservation of the environment;
c. imposed for the protection of national or artistic, historical or archaeological treasures;
d. necessary for fiduciary reasons; either
and. necessary to ensure compliance with laws or regulations that are not inconsistent with the provisions of this Agreement, including those for the prevention of deceptive or fraudulent practices.
Article 9-17: Exceptions for security reasons.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to:
a. impose an obligation on a Party to provide information the disclosure of which, in its opinion, would be contrary to its essential security interests;
b. prevent a Party from adopting any measure it deems necessary for the protection of its essential security interests; either
c. prevent a Party from adopting measures in fulfillment of its obligations under the United Nations Charter for the Maintenance of International Peace and Security.
Article 9-18: Technical cooperation.
The Parties will establish, within a period of 24 months after the entry into force of this Agreement, a system to provide service providers with information regarding their markets in relation to:
a. the commercial and technical aspects of the provision of services;
b. the possibility of obtaining technology in terms of services; Y
c. all those aspects that the Commission identifies, in terms of services.
Article 9-19: Future jobs.
1. The Commission will determine the procedures for establishing the necessary disciplines related to:
a. urgent safeguard measures;
b. trade distorting subsidies; Y
c. monopoly service providers.
2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, the work of the relevant international organizations will be taken into account.
Article 9-20: Relationship with multilateral agreements on services.
1. The Parties undertake to apply to each other the provisions contained in the multilateral agreements on services to which the Parties are party.
2. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1, in the event of any inconsistency between those agreements and this Agreement, the Agreement shall prevail over the former.
Annex toarticle 9-13
Professional services
1. Definitions.
For the purposes of this annex, the following shall be understood as:
specialized higher education: all academic training that has culminated in obtaining a degree awarded by an educational center, at the university or professional technical level;
professional exercise: the provision of any service or act of each profession that requires government authorization;
professional services: services that require specialized higher education for their provision and the exercise of which is authorized or restricted by a Party, but does not include services provided by persons who practice a trade or to the crew of merchant ships and aircraft.
2. Objective.
The purpose of this annex is to establish the rules to be observed by the Parties to reduce and gradually eliminate, in their territory, the barriers to the provision of professional services.
3. Coverage.
This annex will apply to all measures related to the criteria for the mutual recognition or revalidation of titles and the granting of licenses for professional practice.
4. Development of professional standards and criteria.
a. The Parties acknowledge that the process of mutual recognition or revalidation of titles and granting of licenses for professional practice in their territory will be based on raising the quality of professional services through the establishment of standards and criteria for recognition or revalidation. titling and licensing, while protecting consumers and safeguarding the public interest.
b. The Parties shall encourage relevant bodies, inter alia, competent government agencies and professional associations and colleges to:
i) develop such criteria and standards; Y
ii) formulate and present recommendations on the mutual recognition or revalidation of titles and granting of licenses for the professional practice of the professional service providers of the Parties.
c. The elaboration of criteria and norms referred to in literals a) and b) may consider the following elements: education, exams, experience, conduct and ethics, professional development and updating, renewal or updating of certificates and licenses, field of action, knowledge local law and consumer protection, as well as any other that the relevant agencies deem necessary.
d. In order to put into practice the provisions of subparagraphs a) to c), the Parties undertake to provide, within a period not exceeding 12 months from the entry into force of this Agreement, the detailed and necessary information for mutual recognition or revalidation of titles and granting of licenses for professional practice, including that corresponding to: academic courses, guides and study materials, rights, exam dates, hours, locations, affiliation with societies and/or professional associations. This information includes federal, central, state or provincial legislation, administrative directives and measures of general application and those developed by governmental and non-governmental bodies.
5. Review.
a. Based on the review of the recommendations received by the Parties and if they are consistent with the provisions of the Agreement, each Party will encourage the competent authority to adopt those recommendations.
b. The Parties shall periodically review, at least once every three years, the application of the provisions of this Annex.
Chapter X
Temporary entry of business persons
Article 10-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
labor certification: the procedure carried out by the competent administrative authority aimed at determining whether a foreign individual from a Party who intends to temporarily enter the territory of another Party displaces national labor in the same labor branch or significantly harms the labor conditions of the same ;
temporary entry: the entry of a business person of a Party into the territory of another Party, without the intention of establishing permanent residence;
immigration measure: any measure, whether in the form of a law, regulation, rule, procedure, decision or administrative provision or requirement, in immigration matters;
national: as defined in the annex to this article for the Parties stipulated therein;
business person: the national of a Party who participates in the trade of goods or provision of services, or in investment activities;
recurring practice: a practice carried out by the migration authorities of a Party on a repetitive basis during a representative period prior to and immediately after its execution;
in force: as defined in the annex to this article for the Parties stipulated therein.
Article 10-02: General principles.
The provisions of this chapter reflect the preferential commercial relationship between the Parties, the convenience of facilitating the temporary entry of business persons in accordance with the principle of reciprocity, and the need to establish transparent criteria and procedures for this purpose. Likewise, they reflect the need to guarantee the security of the borders and to protect the work of their nationals and permanent employment in their respective territories.
Article 10-03: General obligations.
1. Each Party shall apply the measures related to this Chapter in accordance with Article 10-02, in particular, shall apply them expeditiously to avoid undue delay or damage in trade in goods and services, or in investment activities included in this Treaty.
2. The Parties shall endeavor to develop and adopt common criteria, definitions and interpretations for the application of this Chapter.
3. The Parties may modify their immigration measures, as long as these modifications do not alter the commitments made in this chapter.
Article 10-04: Temporary entry authorization.
1. In accordance with the provisions of this chapter, including those contained in the annex to this article, each Party shall authorize the temporary entry of business persons who comply with the other applicable measures, related to public health and safety, as well as with the relating to national security.
2. Each Party may deny the issuance of a migration document that authorizes employment to a business person, when their temporary entry adversely affects:
a. the solution of any labor conflict that exists in the place where they are employed or will be employed; either
b. the employment of any person involved in that conflict.
3. When a Party denies the issuance of an immigration document authorizing employment, in accordance with paragraph 2, that Party:
a. inform the affected business person in writing of the reasons for the refusal; Y
b. promptly notify the Party whose national is refused entry in writing of the reasons for the refusal.
4. Each Party shall limit the amount of the fees caused by the processing of applications for temporary entry to the approximate cost of the processing services provided.
5. The temporary entry of a business person does not authorize professional practice.
Article 10-05: Availability of information.
1. In addition to the provisions of Article 15-02 (Publication), each Party:
a. provide another Party with the information that allows it to know the measures related to this Chapter; Y
b. no later than 12 months after the date of entry into force of the Agreement, prepare, publish and make available to interested parties, both in its territory and in that of another Party, a consolidated document explaining the requirements for temporary entry under to this chapter, so that they can be known by business persons of another Party.
2. Each Party shall collect, maintain and make available to another Party, in accordance with its legislation, information regarding the granting of temporary entry authorizations, in accordance with this Chapter, to persons of the other Party to whom such authorizations have been issued. immigration documentation.
Article 10-06: Committee on Temporary Entry.
1. The Parties establish a Committee on Temporary Entry, composed of representatives of the Parties, including immigration officials.
2. The Committee will meet at least once every 18 months to review:
a. the application and administration of this chapter;
b. the elaboration of measures that further facilitate the temporary entry of business persons in accordance with the principle of reciprocity; Y
c. proposals for modifications or additions to this chapter.
Article 10-07: Settlement of disputes.
1. The Parties may not initiate the procedures provided for in article 17-06 (Intervention of the Commission, good offices, conciliation and mediation), with respect to a refusal to authorize temporary entry in accordance with this chapter, nor with respect to any particular case. included in article 10-03, except that:
a. the matter refers to a recurring practice; Y
b. the affected person has exhausted the administrative remedies available to him or her with respect to that particular matter.
2. The remedies mentioned in subparagraph b) of paragraph 1 will be considered exhausted when the competent authority has not issued a final resolution in 12 months from the start of the administrative procedure and the resolution has not been delayed for reasons attributable to the person business affected.
Article 10-08: Relationship with other chapters.
Except as provided in this chapter and in chapters I (Initial provisions), II (General definitions), XV (Publication, notification and guarantees of hearing and legality), XVII (Dispute resolution) and XIX (Final provisions), no provision of this Agreement shall impose any obligation on the Parties with respect to their immigration measures.
Annex toArticle 10-01
Specific Definitions by Party
For the purposes of this chapter, the following shall be understood as:


business activity: those legitimate activities of a commercial nature created and operated in order to obtain profits in the market. It does not include the possibility of obtaining employment, or salary or remuneration from a Costa Rican or Mexican source;
national: with respect to Mexico, a national or citizen, in accordance with the current provisions of articles 30 and 34 of the Political Constitution of the United Mexican States; with respect to Costa Rica, a national or citizen, in accordance with the current provisions of articles 13 to 18 of its Political Constitution; Y
in force: the binding quality of the legislative precepts of the Parties at the time of entry into force of this Agreement.
Annex to the article10-04
Temporary entry of business persons
Section A - Business Visitors
1. Each Party will authorize the temporary entry of the business person who, at the prior request of a company registered in the Bilateral Register of the Parties for section A, intends to carry out an activity expressly mentioned in appendix A.1, without requiring employment authorization, provided that, in addition to complying with current immigration measures applicable to temporary entry, it exhibits:
a. proof of nationality of a Party;
b. documentation proving the prior request of a company established in the territory of a Party;
