c. documentation proving that you will undertake those activities and stating the purpose of your entry; Y
d. proof of the international character of the proposed business activity and that the person does not intend to enter the local labor market.
2. Each Party shall stipulate that a business person can meet the requirements indicated in subparagraph d) of paragraph 1, when he demonstrates:
a. that the main source of remuneration for that activity is located outside the territory of the Party authorizing temporary entry; Y
b. that the principal place of business and where most of the profits are obtained are outside this territory.
3. For the purposes of paragraph 2, each Party will normally accept a declaration as to the principal place of business and the place of obtaining profits. When a Party requires additional verification, a letter from the employer registered in the Bilateral Register of Companies stating these circumstances will normally be considered sufficient proof.
4. Each Party shall authorize the temporary entry of a business person who intends to carry out a business activity other than those indicated in Appendix A.1, in terms no less favorable than those provided for in the current provisions of the measures indicated in Appendix A.3, provided that the business person also complies with current immigration measures applicable to temporary entry.
5. Neither Party may:
a. require as a condition to authorize temporary entry pursuant to paragraph 1, prior approval procedures, petitions, labor certification tests, or other procedures of similar effect; Y
b. impose or maintain any numerical restriction on temporary entry in accordance with paragraph 1 or 4.
6. Notwithstanding paragraph 5, a Party may require a business person applying for temporary entry under this section to obtain a visa or equivalent document prior to entry. Before imposing the visa requirement, the Party shall consult with the Party whose persons would be affected, in order to avoid the application of the requirement. When a visa requirement exists in a Party and at the request of the Party whose business persons are subject to it, they shall consult with each other with a view to eliminating it.
Section B - Investors
1. Each Party shall authorize temporary entry and provide the corresponding documentation to the business person who intends to establish, develop, manage or provide key technical advice or services, in supervisory, executive functions or those involving essential skills, to carry out or manage an investment in which the person or their company has committed, or is in the process of committing, a significant amount of capital, provided that the person also complies with the immigration measures applicable to temporary entry.
2. Neither Party may:
a. require proof of labor certification or other procedures of similar effect, as a condition for authorizing temporary entry under paragraph 1; neither
b. impose or maintain numerical restrictions in relation to temporary entry pursuant to paragraph 1.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 2, a Party may examine, at a peremptory time, the investment proposal of a business person to assess whether the investment complies with the applicable legal provisions.
4. Notwithstanding paragraph 2, a Party may require a business person applying for temporary entry under this section to obtain, prior to entry, a visa or equivalent document.
Section C - Personnel transfers within a company
1. Each Party shall authorize temporary entry and issue supporting documentation to the business person employed by a company listed in the Bilateral Register of Parties for section C, who intends to perform managerial, executive or specialized knowledge functions in that company. or in one of its subsidiaries or affiliates, provided that that person and that company comply with the current immigration measures applicable to temporary entry. Each Party may require that the person have been employed by the company continuously for one year within the three years immediately preceding the filing date of the application.
2. Neither Party may:
a. require proof of labor certification or other procedures of similar effect, as a condition for authorizing temporary entry under paragraph 1; neither
b. impose or maintain numerical restrictions in relation to temporary entry pursuant to paragraph 1.
3. Notwithstanding paragraph 2, a Party may require a business person applying for temporary entry under this section to obtain, prior to entry, a visa or equivalent document. Before imposing the visa requirement, the Party shall consult with the other Party whose business persons would be affected, in order to avoid applying the requirement. When a visa requirement exists in a Party and at the request of the Party whose business persons are subject to it, they shall consult with each other with a view to eliminating it.
Definitions.
For the purposes of this annex, the following shall be understood as:
employment authorization: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section A, the written permission granted by the competent administrative authority of a Party to an individual national of another Party in which he is authorized to obtain employment in salaried activities in the territory of the Authorizing Party;
business-essential expertise: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section C, that an individual has business-essential expertise if he or she has special knowledge of the good or service that the business provides in international markets, or has a high degree of knowledge about the processes and procedures of the company;
be in the process of committing a significant amount of capital: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section B, that a person or a company is in the process of committing a significant amount of capital where the funds are irrevocably directed towards the investment in such a way that it is irreversible;
supervisory functions: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section B, those functions in which the individual has supervisory responsibilities for a significant part of the operations of a company and does not involve the supervision of low-level employees;
executive functions: for the purposes of paragraphs 1 of sections B and C, those assigned functions within an organization, under which the individual essentially has the following responsibilities:
a. direct the administration of the organization or a relevant component or function thereof;
b. establish the policies and objectives of the organization, component or function;
c. exercise wide latitude in making decisions that are at your discretion; Y
d. receive general supervision or direction only from the highest level executives, the Board of Directors or the Council of Administration of the organization or the shareholders of the same;
managerial functions: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section C, those assigned functions within an organization, under which the individual has essentially the following responsibilities:
a. manage the organization or an essential function within it;
b. supervising and controlling the work of other professional employees, supervisors or administrators;
c. have the authority to hire and fire or recommend these actions, as well as others, with respect to the management of the personnel that is directly supervised by the individual and perform functions at a higher level within the organizational hierarchy or with respect to the function under their charge; Y
d. perform actions at their discretion with respect to the daily operation of the function over which the individual has authority;
functions involving essential skills: for the purposes of paragraph 1 of section B, that an individual performs functions involving essential skills when they are an individual with specialized knowledge or own skills that are essential to the effective operation of the business. The individual must be employed in a position of high responsibility that requires independent judgment, creativity, training, or supervision of other employees and must not be employed to perform routine work that can be performed by skilled labor. He must have a high degree of preparation and experience in the operation of the company.
Appendix A.1
Business Visitors
I. Definitions.
For the purposes of this appendix, it shall be understood as:
tourist bus operator: the natural person required for the operation of the vehicle during the tourist trip, including relief personnel who accompany or join him later;
transport operator: the natural person, who is not a tour bus operator, required for the operation of the vehicle during the trip, including relief personnel who accompany or join him later;
territory of another Party: the territory of a Party other than that of the Party from which temporary entry is sought.
II. Activities.
Research and design.
- technical, scientific and statistician researchers who carry out research independently or for a company located in the territory of the other Party.
Cultivation, manufacturing and production.
- purchasing and production personnel, at the managerial level, who carry out commercial operations for a company located in the territory of the other Party.
Commercialization.
- researchers who carry out research or analysis, including market analysis, independently or for a company located in the territory of the other Party.
- Trade fair and promotional staff attending trade conventions.
Sales.
- buyers who make acquisitions for a company located in the territory of the other Party.
Distribution.
- Customs brokers who provide advisory services regarding facilitating the import or export of goods.
- transport operators that carry out operations to transport goods or passengers to the territory of a Party from the territory of another Party, or carry out loading and unloading operations of goods or passengers from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party, without carrying out loading or unloading operations, in the territory of the Party to which entry is requested, of goods that are in that territory or of passengers boarding in it.
Post-sale services.
- installation, repair, maintenance and supervisory personnel who have the specialized technical knowledge essential to fulfill the seller's contractual obligation and who provide services, or train workers to provide such services, pursuant to a warranty or other contract of services related to the sale of commercial or industrial equipment or machinery, including computer programs purchased from a company located outside the territory of the Party to which temporary entry is requested, during the term of the warranty or service contract.
General services.
- managerial and supervisory personnel involved in commercial operations for a company located in the territory of the other Party.
- public relations and advertising personnel who provide advice to clients or who attend or participate in conventions.
- tourism personnel (tour and travel agents, tour guides or tour operators) attending or participating in conventions.
- translators or interpreters who provide services as employees of a company located in the territory of the other Party.
- tour bus operators entering the territory of a Party:
a. with a group of passengers on a tour bus trip that started in the territory of another Party and is going to return to it;
b. to pick up a group of passengers on a tour bus tour that will terminate and take place for the most part in the territory of another Party; either
c. with a group of passengers on a tourist bus whose destination is in the territory of the Party to which temporary entry is requested, and that returns without passengers or with the group to transport it to the territory of another Party.
Appendix A.3
Immigration measures in force
1. In the case of Costa Rica:
- General Law on Migration and Immigration, 1986, with its reforms.
- Regulation of the General Law of Migration and Aliens, 1989, with its reforms.
2. In the case of Mexico:
- General Population Law, 1974, with its amendments and its Regulations.
Chapter XI
Standardization measures
Article 11-01: Definitions.
1. For the purposes of this chapter, the terms presented in the sixth edition of ISO/IEC Guide 2: 1991, "General Terms and their Definitions in Relation to Standardization and Related Activities", shall have the same meaning when used in this chapter. , unless defined differently here.
2. For the purposes of this chapter, the following shall be understood as:
risk assessment: assess the potential damage to human, animal and plant health and safety or the environment could be caused by any good or service that is traded between the Parties;
make compatible: bring to the same level, different standardization measures but with the same scope, approved by different standardization bodies, so that they are identical, equivalent, or have the effect of allowing goods and services to be used interchangeably or for the same purpose. same purpose, so that goods and services are allowed to be traded between the Parties;
certification mark of conformity: a protected mark applied or issued under the rules of a certification system that indicates, with an appropriate level of confidence, that a good or process conforms to, or complies with, a specified technical regulation or standard or another specific normative document;
standardization measures: standards, technical regulations or conformity assessment processes;
standard: the document approved by a recognized institution, which provides for common and repeated use, rules, guidelines or characteristics for goods or related processes and production methods, or for related services or methods of operation, and the observance of which is not mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging, marking or labeling requirements applicable to a related good, service, process or production method;
international standard: a standardization measure, or other guide or recommendation, adopted by an international standardization body and made available to the public;
legitimate objectives: which include the guarantee of safety and the protection of human, animal and plant life and health, the environment and the prevention of practices that may mislead consumers, including matters related to the identification of goods or services, considering, among other aspects, when appropriate, fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure type or scientific justification;
standardization body: a body whose standardization activities are recognized by the governments of the Parties;
international standardization body: a standardization body, open to the participation of the relevant bodies of at least the signatory countries of the GATT Agreement on Technical Barriers to Trade, including the International Organization for Standardization (ISO), the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC), the Codex Alimentarius Commission , the World Health Organization (WHO), the International Organization of Legal Metrology (OIML), or any other body designated by the Parties;
reasonable period: that period of time determined by the competent institution of that Party for the interested parties to make the necessary changes or take the necessary measures in light of the existing circumstances;
conformity assessment procedure: any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine that the relevant requirements established by technical regulations or standards are met, including sampling, testing, inspection, evaluation, verification, assurance of conformity, accreditation, certification, registration or approval, used for those purposes, but does not mean an approval process;
approval process: the registration, notification or any other mandatory administrative process to obtain a permit in order for a good or service to be commercialized or used for defined purposes or according to established conditions;
administrative refusal: actions taken by a public administration body of the importing Party, in the exercise of its powers, to prevent a shipment from entering its territory or the provision of services, for technical reasons;
technical regulation: a document that establishes the characteristics of the goods, services or their processes and related production methods, including the applicable administrative provisions, and compliance with which is mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging or labeling requirements applicable to a related good, service, process or production method; Y
service: which does not include:
a. air services, including national and international air transport, with and without a fixed itinerary, as well as auxiliary activities in support of air services, except:
i) aircraft repair and maintenance services during the period in which an aircraft is withdrawn from service;
ii) specialized air services; Y
iii) computerized reservation systems;
b. financial services;
c. subsidies or grants provided by a Party or a State enterprise, including government-supported loans, guarantees and insurance; neither
d. government services or functions such as, but not limited to, law enforcement, rehabilitation services, income security or insurance, social security or insurance, social welfare, public education, training public health and care for children.
Article 11-02: Scope of application.
The provisions of this chapter apply to the standardization, metrology and measures related to all of them of each Party that may affect, directly or indirectly, reciprocal trade in goods and services between them. The provisions of this chapter do not apply to phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures found in section B of chapter IV (Phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures).
Article 11-03: Scope of obligations.
Each Party shall comply with the provisions of this Chapter and shall adopt the necessary measures to guarantee its compliance by any competent authority regardless of whether or not it is within the scope of the central or federal government, as well as the measures in that regard that are within its reach with respect to non-governmental standardization bodies duly accredited in its territory.
Article 11-04: Reaffirmation of international rights and obligations.
The Parties reaffirm their rights and obligations related to standardization measures emanating from GATT and all other international treaties and laws related to safety, protection of human, animal and plant life, protection of their environment and practices that avoid mislead consumers, of which the two Parties are parties.
Article 11-05: Obligations and basic rights.
1. Neither Party shall develop, adopt, maintain or apply any standardization measure that has the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to reciprocal trade. To that end, each Party shall ensure that its standardization measures do not restrict trade more than is required to achieve its legitimate objectives in its territory, taking into account the risks that failure to achieve them would create.
2. Standardization measures of a Party shall not be considered to create unnecessary obstacles to trade when:
a. the demonstrable purpose of those measures is to achieve the legitimate objectives of that Party; Y
b. function in such a way that they do not exclude the goods and services of the other Party that fulfill their legitimate objectives.
3. Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, each Party may set the level of protection it deems appropriate in the pursuit of its legitimate objectives.
4. Pursuant to paragraph 3, each Party may develop, apply and maintain the standardization measures that allow guaranteeing its level of protection, as well as the measures that guarantee the application and compliance with those measures, including the relevant approval procedures.
5. Each Party shall grant to goods and services originating from the territory of the other Party, national treatment and no less favorable than that granted to similar goods and services originating from any other country.
Article 11-06: Use of international standards.
1. Each Party shall use, as a basis for its own standardization measures, current international standards, or those of imminent adoption, or their relevant elements, except when those standards do not constitute an effective or adequate means to achieve its legitimate objectives; among others, due to fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
2. Standardization measures of a Party that conform to an international standard shall be presumed to be consistent with the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 5 of Article 11-05.
3. In the pursuit of its legitimate objectives, each Party may adopt, maintain or apply any standardization measure that achieves a higher level of protection than would have been obtained if the measure were based on an international standard due, inter alia, to fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature.
Article 11-07: Compatibility and equivalence.
1. The Parties recognize the central role that standardization measures play in strengthening, promoting and protecting legitimate objectives, and will therefore work together, in accordance with this Chapter.
2. The Parties will make their respective technical regulations and conformity assessment procedures compatible, to the greatest extent possible, without reducing the level of protection of their legitimate objectives without prejudice to the rights conferred by this chapter on a Party and taking into account account international standardization activities or parameters.
3. At the request of a Party, the other Party shall adopt reasonable measures within its power to promote the compatibility of the specific standardization measures that exist in its territory, with the standardization measures that exist in the territory of the other Party, taking into account account international standardization activities or parameters.
4. The importing Party shall accept as equivalent to its own technical regulation the one adopted or maintained by the exporting Party when the latter proves to the satisfaction of the former that its technical regulation adequately meets the legitimate objectives of the importing Party. For the purposes of this accreditation, the importing Party shall cooperate with the exporting Party. The importing Party shall communicate in writing to the exporting Party, at its request, the reasons for non-acceptance of a technical regulation.
5. Each Party, whenever possible, shall accept the results of conformity assessment procedures carried out in the territory of the other Party, even when those procedures differ from its own, provided that those procedures:
a. provide satisfactory assurance that the relevant good or service complies with applicable technical regulations or standards developed or maintained in the territory of that Party; Y
b. that this guarantee is equivalent to the one offered:
i) in the proceedings carried out by the Party; either
ii) in proceedings carried out in its territory and whose result it accepts.
6. In relation to paragraph 5, the Party shall review, if applicable, the pertinent normalization measure.
7. In accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 5 and 6, prior to the acceptance of the results of a conformity assessment procedure, and in order to strengthen confidence in the continuing integrity of each of those results, the Parties may consult on matters such as the technical capacity of conformity assessment bodies, taking into account verified compliance with relevant international standards and recommendations.
Article 11-08: Conformity assessment.
1. The Parties accept the convenience of achieving reciprocal recognition of their conformity assessment systems, including, among others, the bodies accredited by the corresponding competent authority, in order to facilitate reciprocal trade in goods and services and undertake to work to achieve this end.
2. In addition to what is established in paragraph 1, and recognizing the existence of differences in their conformity assessment procedures in their respective territories, the Parties shall make their respective conformity assessment systems and procedures compatible to the greatest extent possible. conformity so that they are mutually recognized in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
3. For the mutual benefit of the Parties and reciprocally, each Party through its competent authorities or the institutions designated by them:
a. evaluate and recognize the national accreditation system of the other Party; Y
b. shall accredit, approve, license or recognize conformity assessment bodies in the territory of the other Party on terms no less favorable than those granted to such bodies in its territory.
4. Each Party shall give favorable consideration to requests submitted by the other Party to negotiate agreements on mutual recognition of the results of the Parties' conformity assessment procedures.
5. When it is required to carry out a procedure for the evaluation of conformity with technical regulations or standards, each Party shall have the obligation to:
a. not adopt or maintain stricter conformity assessment procedures and not apply them more strictly than is necessary to be certain that the good or service conforms to the applicable technical regulation or standard, taking into account the risks that it may create non-conformity;
b. initiate and complete that procedure in the most expeditious manner possible;
c. establish a non-discriminatory order for processing applications;
d. publish the normal duration of each of these procedures or communicate, at the applicant's request, the approximate duration of the procedure;
and. ensure that the competent authority or the institutions designated by it:
i) upon receipt of an application, promptly examine all necessary documentation for completeness and accurately and fully inform the applicant of any deficiencies;
(ii) as soon as possible, convey to the applicant the results of the conformity assessment procedure in an accurate and complete manner, so that the applicant can take any corrective action;
iii) when the application is deficient, continue with the procedure to the extent possible, if requested by the applicant; Y
iv) report, at the applicant's request, the status of their application and the reasons for any delay;
F. limit to what is necessary, and in accordance with its law, the information that the applicant must submit to assess conformity and to determine the relevant rights;
g. grant to the confidential information that derives from the procedure or that is presented in connection with it:
i) the same treatment as information regarding a national good or service; Y
(ii) in any case, treatment that protects the legitimate business interests of the applicant in accordance with the law of that Party;
h. ensure that the amount of any duty charged for assessing the conformity of a good or service that is exported from the other Party is not greater than any duty charged for assessing the conformity of an identical or similar domestic good or service, taking into account the costs of communication, transportation, consular fees and other related costs;
Yo. ensure that the location of the facilities where the conformity assessment procedures are carried out does not cause unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative;
j. where possible, ensure that the procedure is carried out at the manufacturing facility of the good and that a mark of conformity is given, where appropriate;
k. limit the procedure, in the case of a good or service that has been modified after the determination of the assessment of conformity with the technical regulations or applicable standards, to what is necessary to determine that said good or service continues to comply with those regulations or standards; Y
he. limit to what is reasonable any requirement related to samples of a good and ensure that the selection of samples does not cause unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative in accordance with the sampling procedures used and approved internationally.
6. Each Party shall apply the provisions of paragraph 5 to its approval procedures, with any modifications required.
7. At the request of another Party, each Party shall adopt reasonable measures within its power to facilitate access to its territory or when it is intended to carry out conformity assessment activities.
Article 11-09: Notification, publication and delivery of information.
1. In addition to the provisions of Articles 15-02 (Publication) and 15-03 (Notification and provision of information), each Party shall notify the other Party of the standardization measures that it intends to establish before their entry into force and shall not after their nationals.
2. When proposing the adoption or modification of any standardization measure, each Party:
a. publish a notice and notify the other Party in writing of its intention to adopt or modify that measure, in order to allow interested persons to become familiar with the proposal, at least 60 days in advance of its adoption or modification, except in the cases of any measure related to standardization related to perishable goods, in which case the Party, in the best possible way, will publish the notice and simultaneously notify the other Party and its national producers, at least 30 days in advance of the adoption or reform of these measures;
b. In said notice and notification, it will identify the good or service to which the measure will be applied, and will include a brief description of its objective and motivation;
c. provide a copy of the proposed measure to the other Party and to any interested person who requests it and, where possible, identify provisions that deviate substantially from relevant international standards;
d. without discrimination, allow the other Party and interested persons to make comments in writing and, upon request, discuss and take into account those comments, and the results of the discussions; Y
and. expeditiously publish the adopted measure or in some other way make it available in its territory to interested persons so that they can become familiar with it.
3. When there is no relevant or imminent international standard for a proposed standardization measure, or that standardization measure is not substantially the same as an international standard, and when the standardization measure may have a significant effect on trade of the other Party, each Party:
a. publish a notice and deliver a written notice of the type required in subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 2, at an appropriate initial stage; Y
b. The provisions of subparagraphs c) and d) of paragraph 2 shall be observed.
4. With respect to technical regulations other than those issued by the central or federal government, each Party:
a. ensure that a notice is published and the other Party is notified in writing of its intention to adopt or modify that regulation at an appropriate early stage;
b. ensure that the notice and notification identifies the good or service to which the technical regulation will apply and will include a brief description of the purpose and motivation of that regulation;
c. ensure that a copy of the proposed regulation is provided to the other Party and to any interested person who requests it;
d. shall take reasonable steps within its power to ensure that upon adoption of the technical regulation, it is promptly published or otherwise made available in its territory to interested persons in the Party to become familiar with it.
5. Each Party shall annually notify the other Party about its plans and standardization programs.
6. When a Party considers it necessary to address an urgent problem related to its legitimate objectives, it may omit any of the steps established in subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 2 provided that, when adopting the standardization measure:
a. immediately notify the other Party, in accordance with the requirements established in subparagraph b) of paragraph 2, including a brief description of the urgent problem;
b. deliver a copy of the measure to the other Party and interested persons who so request a copy of the measure;
c. allow, without discrimination, the other Party and interested persons to make comments in writing and, upon request, discuss and take into account those comments, as well as the results of the discussions; Y
d. publish the measure expeditiously, or make it available in its territory to interested persons so that they can become familiar with it.
7. The Parties shall allow a reasonable period of time between the publication of their standardization measures and the date they come into force, so that there is time for interested persons to adjust to these standardization measures, except when it is necessary to make addressing one of the urgent problems identified in paragraph 6.
8. Where a Party allows non-government persons from its territory to be present during the standardization process, it shall also allow non-government persons from the other Party's territory to be present.
9. Each Party shall designate a government authority as responsible for the application of the notification provisions of this chapter at the central or federal level, and shall notify the other Party within three months of the entry into force of this chapter. Treaty. When a Party designates two or more government authorities for this purpose, it shall inform the other Party, without ambiguity or exceptions, of the scope of responsibilities of those authorities.
10. When a Party administratively rejects a shipment or supply of services due to non-compliance with a measure related to standardization, it shall promptly inform the person holding the shipment or the service provider in writing of the technical justification for the rejection. .
11. Once the information referred to in paragraph 10 has been generated, it shall be sent immediately to the information center or centers for standardization measures located in the territory of that Party, which in turn will notify the center. or information centers of the other Party.
Article 11-10: Information centers.
1. Each Party shall ensure that there is at least one information center within its territory capable of answering all reasonable questions and requests from the other Party and interested persons, as well as providing the relevant documentation regarding:
a. any standardization measure adopted or proposed in its territory at the level of its central or federal, state, or municipal government;
b. the membership and participation of that Party, and of and its competent authorities at the central or federal, state, or municipal level in international or regional standardization bodies and conformity assessment systems, in bilateral or multilateral agreements, within the scope of application of the chapter, as well as the provisions of those systems and agreements;
c. the location of notices published pursuant to this chapter or where such information may be obtained;
d. the location of information centers; Y
and. the Party's risk assessment processes, the factors it takes into consideration in conducting the assessment, and the establishment, pursuant to paragraph 3 of Article 11-05, of the levels of protection it deems appropriate.
2. When a Party designates more than one information center:
a. inform the other Party, unambiguously and completely, about the scope of responsibilities of each of these centers; Y
b. will ensure that any request sent to the wrong information center is forwarded, expeditiously, to the correct information center.
3. Each Party shall take reasonable measures within its power to ensure that there is at least one information center within its territory capable of answering all questions and requests from the other Party and interested persons, as well as to provide the pertinent documentation or the information from where such documentation can be obtained related to:
a. any standard or conformity assessment process adopted or proposed by non-governmental standards bodies in its territory; Y
b. membership and participation in international and regional standardization bodies and conformity assessment systems of relevant non-governmental bodies in their territory.
4. Each Party shall ensure that when the other Party or interested persons request copies of the documents in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, they are provided at the same price as for internal sale, in addition to the shipping cost.
Article 11-11: Limitations on the provision of information.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to impose an obligation on the Parties to communicate any information the disclosure of which they consider contrary to their essential security interests, or which would harm the legitimate business interests of certain companies.
Article 11-12: Metrological standards.
The Parties will make their national metrological standards compatible, to the greatest extent possible, based on the international standards in force at that time, when the former constitute, or create, unnecessary obstacles to trade, in accordance with the annex to this article.
Article 11-13: Protection of health.
1. Medicines, medical equipment and instruments, pharmaceutical goods and other inputs for human, animal and plant health; foods; toxic goods and substances; material goods, radioactive sources and equipment; Sources and equipment emitting ionizing radiation that are subject to registration within the territory of a Party, will be, where appropriate, registered, recognized or evaluated by the competent authority of that Party based on a single national system of a central or federal nature. mandatory observance.
2. The certificates that support compliance with the standards and technical regulations of the companies that produce or condition the goods referred to in paragraph 1 will be accepted only if they have been issued by the competent authorities of the central or federal government of the Parties.
3. The Parties will establish a mutual technical cooperation system that will work on the following:
a. identify specific needs in:
i) the application of good manufacturing practices in the preparation and approval of medicines for human, animal and plant use;
ii) the application of good laboratory practices in the analysis and evaluation systems established in the pertinent international standards and guides in force; Y
iii) the development of common identification and nomenclature systems for auxiliary goods for health and medical instruments;
b. standardize the requirements related to labeling and strengthen, among others, the standardization and surveillance systems in relation to warning labeling;
c. establish training and training programs and organize, among others, a common system of training, continuing education, training and evaluation of sanitary officials and inspectors;
d. develop a system of mutual accreditation for verification units and testing laboratories;
and. update the regulatory legal frameworks; Y
F. Strengthen formal communication systems to monitor and regulate the exchange of goods related to human, animal and plant health.
4. In order to carry out the activities indicated in paragraph 3, the Parties shall establish, in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 4 of article 11-17, a technical subcommittee in charge of monitoring and organizing these activities, in order to guide and recommend to the Parties when they so request.
Article 11-14: Risk assessment.
1. Pursuant to paragraphs 3 and 4 of Article 11-05, each Party may carry out risk assessments within its territory when it deems appropriate. In doing so, you will ensure that you take into account risk assessment methods developed by international organizations, and that your technical regulations and standards are based on a risk assessment.
2. When conducting a risk assessment in its territory, each Party shall take into consideration all relevant scientific evidence, available technical information, intended end use, production processes or methods, operation, inspection, quality, sampling or testing or environmental conditions.
3. When a Party conducts a risk assessment pursuant to paragraph 3 of Article 11-05, once it has established its level of security protection that it deems appropriate, it shall avoid arbitrary or unjustifiable distinctions between similar goods and services at the level of protection it deems appropriate, if those distinctions:
a. have the effect of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination against goods or services of the other Party;
b. they constitute a disguised restriction on reciprocal trade; either
c. They discriminate between similar goods or services for the same use, in accordance with the same conditions that the level of risk poses and that grant similar benefits.
4. When the Party carrying out a risk assessment concludes that the scientific evidence or other information available is insufficient to complete that assessment, it may provisionally adopt a measure based on the pertinent information available. Once sufficient information has been presented to it to complete the risk assessment, the Party shall complete its assessment as soon as possible, review and, where appropriate, modify that measure in light of that assessment.
Article 11-15: Management of toxic and dangerous substances.
1. For the control, handling and acceptance of toxic or dangerous substances or residues, the Parties shall apply the provisions, guides or recommendations of the Basel Convention, the Charter of the United Nations, the London Guidelines on Chemical Substances Object of International Commerce and relevant international agreements to which the Parties are party.
2. When any good or toxic or dangerous substance requires a permit or registration for its handling or transportation, it will be issued by the competent authority at the central or federal level.
Article 11-16: Labeling.
1. The labeling requirements of the goods and services that are part of the scope of this chapter shall be subject to the provisions established therein. Each Party shall apply its relevant labeling requirements within its territory.
2. The Parties shall develop common labeling requirements. The proposals made by each Party will be evaluated by the Subcommittee for Standardization Measures in Labeling, Packaging and Packaging, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 5 of article 11-17.
3. The Subcommittee for Standardization Measures in Labeling, Packaging and Packaging may work and formulate recommendations on, among others, the following areas:
a. a common system of symbols and pictograms for the Parties;
b. definitions and terminology;
c. presentation of information, including language, measurement systems, ingredients, and sizes; either
d. other related matters.
Article 11-17: Committee for Standardization Measures.
1. The Parties hereby establish a Committee for Standardization Measures, hereinafter referred to as the Committee.
2. The functions of the Committee will include, among others:
a. follow up on the application, compliance and administration of this chapter, including the progress of the sub-committees and working groups established pursuant to paragraph 4 and the operation of the information centers established pursuant to paragraph 1 of article 11 -10;
b. facilitate the process through which the Parties will make their standardization and metrology measures compatible;
c. provide a forum for Parties to consult on issues related to standardization and metrology measures;
d. promote that the competent institutions in the matter take into consideration the events on standardization measures at the governmental, non-governmental, regional and multilateral levels, including those of the GATT;
and. develop the necessary procedural mechanisms to achieve the recognition of conformity assessment bodies; Y
F. report annually to the Commission on the application of this chapter.
3. The Committee:
a. It will be made up of an equal number of representatives of the competent government institutions of each Party. Each Party shall establish its procedures for the selection of its representatives;
b. shall meet, unless the Parties agree otherwise:
i) at least once a year;
ii) when requested by any Party; Y
iii) in case of emergency, expeditiously and as soon as possible;
c. It will establish its regulations and make its decisions by consensus.
4. When the Committee considers it appropriate, it may establish the subcommittees and working groups that it deems pertinent and determine their scope of action and mandate. Each subcommittee and working group will be made up of representatives of each Party and may determine its work program, taking into account relevant international activities and, when deemed necessary, include or consult with:
a. representatives of non-governmental organizations, such as standardization bodies, or private sector chambers and associations;
b. representatives of higher academic research and scientific centers;
c. technical experts; Y
d. representatives of government institutions.
5. In addition to paragraph 4, the Committee shall establish the Subcommittee on Health Standardization Measures, Subcommittee on Labeling, Packaging, and Standardization Measures, and any other subcommittees and working groups it deems appropriate to review, among others, the following topics:
a. identification and nomenclature of goods and services subject to standardization measures;
b. technical regulations and quality and identity standards;
c. programs for the approval of goods and for surveillance after its sale;
d. principles for the accreditation and recognition of test facilities, inspection agencies and conformity assessment bodies;
and. implementation and development of a uniform system for the classification and reporting of hazardous chemicals, and chemical hazard communication;
F. programs to ensure compliance with current provisions, including training and inspection by personnel responsible for regulation, analysis, and compliance verification;
g. the application and promotion of good laboratory practices;
h. the application and promotion of good manufacturing practices;
Yo. criteria for the evaluation of potential damage to the environment due to the use of goods or provision of services;
j. analysis of procedures for the simplification of import requirements for specific goods and services;
k. risk assessment methodologies;
he. guidelines for testing chemical substances, including those of an industrial type and those for agricultural, pharmaceutical and biological use; Y
m. Means that facilitate consumer protection, including with regard to compensation.
6. Each Party shall adopt the necessary measures so that government representatives, other than the central or federal government of a Party, participate in the work of the Committee when deemed necessary.
Article 11-18: Technical cooperation.
1. At the request of a Party, the other Party may, to the best of its ability:
a. provide that Party with advice, information or technical assistance on mutually agreed terms and conditions, to strengthen the measures related to the standardization of that Party, its activities, processes and systems on the matter; Y
b. provide that Party with information on its technical cooperation programs related to standardization measures in areas of particular interest.
2. Each Party shall encourage the cooperation of its standards bodies, as appropriate, in standardization activities. For example, by obtaining membership in international standardization bodies.
Article 11-19: Expenses.
Each Party shall endeavor, to the extent possible, to allocate the necessary resources for the operation and due compliance with the provisions of this chapter. In addition, it may charge a reasonable amount, when so required, for the services rendered in connection with the application of this chapter, without this constituting an act of discrimination between the nationals of the Parties.
Article 11-20: Technical consultations.
1. When a Party has doubts about the interpretation or application made by the other Party, it may alternatively resort to the Committee or the dispute settlement mechanism of the Treaty. The Parties may not use both channels simultaneously.
2. When a Party decides to go to the Committee, it will notify it in writing so that it can consider the matter. The Committee may refer it to a subcommittee or working group, or to another competent forum, in order to obtain advice or non-binding technical recommendations.
3. The Committee will consider any matter that is referred to it in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2, as expeditiously as possible and, in the same way, will inform the Parties of any advice or technical recommendation that it prepares or receives in relation to to that matter. Once the Parties receive from the Committee a technical advice or recommendation that they have requested, they will send to the Committee a written response in relation to that technical advice or recommendation, in a period determined by the Committee.
4. In accordance with paragraphs 2 and 3, in the event that the technical recommendation issued by the Committee does not resolve the existing difference between the Parties, they may invoke the dispute settlement mechanism of the Treaty. If the Parties so agree, the consultations carried out before the Committee shall constitute consultations for the purposes of Article 17-05 (Consultations).
5. The Party that asserts that a standardization measure of another Party is inconsistent with the provisions of this Chapter shall bear the burden of proof of that inconsistency.
Annex to the article11-12
Article 11-12 does not confer rights or obligations on Costa Rica until the third year after the entry into force of this Agreement.
Chapter XII
Public Sector Procurement
Section A - Scope of application and national treatment
Article 12-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
goods of another Party: goods originated in the territory of the other Party, in accordance with the provisions of Article 12-05;
scheduled purchase: the purchase in respect of which an entity listed in annexes 2 or 3 to article 12-02 publishes a purchase notice in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 3 of article 12-11 and subsequently invites suppliers who have manifested interest in the purchase to confirm your interest in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4 of article 12-11;
construction services contract: a contract for the performance by any means of civil works or construction;
entity: an entity included in annexes 1, 2 and 3 to article 12-02;
technical specification: a specification that establishes the characteristics of the goods or processes and related production methods, or the characteristics of services or their related methods of operation, including the applicable administrative provisions. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging, marking or labeling requirements applicable to a good, process or method of production or operation;
international standard: "international standard" as defined in Article 11-01 (Definitions);
tendering procedures: open tendering procedures, selective tendering procedures or restricted tendering procedures;
open tendering procedures: the procedures in which all interested suppliers can submit offers;
restricted tendering procedures: the procedures by which an entity communicates individually with suppliers, only in the circumstances and in accordance with the conditions described in article 12-16;
selective bidding procedures: the procedures in which, under the terms of article 12-12, the suppliers whom the entity invites to do so may submit bids;
supplier: a person who has provided or may provide goods or services in response to an entity's invitation to bid;
locally established supplier: which includes a natural person residing in the Party's territory, a company organized or established under the Party's law, and a branch or representative office located in the Party's territory;
services: includes construction service contracts, unless otherwise specified.
Article 12-02: Scope of application.
1. This Chapter applies to measures that a Party adopts or maintains in relation to purchases:
a. of a central or federal government entity indicated in annex 1 to this article; a government company indicated in annex 2 to this article; or a state or municipal government entity indicated in annex 3 to this article in accordance with the provisions of article 12-24;
b. of goods, in accordance with annex 4 to this article; of services, in accordance with annex 5 to this article; or construction services, in accordance with annex 6 to this article; Y
c. when it is estimated that the value of the contract to be awarded equals or exceeds the value of the following thresholds, calculated and adjusted in accordance with the inflation rate of the United States of America as provided in annex 7 to this article, for the case of:
i) central or federal government entities, US$50,000 for contracts for goods, services or any combination thereof, and US$6.5 million for construction service contracts;
ii) government companies, US$250,000 for contracts for goods, services or any combination thereof, and US$8 million for construction service contracts; Y
iii) state or municipal government entities, the value of the applicable thresholds as provided in annex 3 to this article, in accordance with the provisions of article 12-24.
2. Paragraph 1 shall be subject to the transition mechanisms established in annex 8 to this article and to the general notes indicated in annex 9 to this article.
3. Subject to paragraph 4, where a contract to be awarded by an entity is not subject to this chapter, its provisions may not be construed to cover the components of any good or service of that contract.
4. None of the entities of the Parties shall conceive, prepare or structure a purchase contract in such a way as to avoid the obligations of this chapter.
5. Purchases include acquisitions by methods such as purchase, lease, or rental, with or without a purchase option. Purchases do not include:
a. non-contractual agreements or any form of government assistance, including cooperative agreements, transfers, loans, capital transfers, guarantees, tax incentives and government supply of goods and services granted to individuals or to state or municipal governments; Y
b. the acquisition of services from fiscal agencies or deposits, liquidation and administration services for regulated financial institutions, or public debt sale and distribution services.
6. The provisions contained in this chapter establish the general principles that the entities of each Party must observe in their purchasing procedures.
7. The Parties shall ensure that the measures applied by their entities are in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
Article 12-03: Valuation of contracts.
1. Each Party shall ensure that, in determining whether a contract is covered by this Chapter, its entities apply the provisions of paragraphs 2 through 7 to calculate the value of that contract.
2. The value of the contract will be estimated at the time of publication of the call, which will be carried out in accordance with article 12-11.
3. When calculating the value of a contract, entities will take into account all forms of remuneration, including bonuses, rights, commissions and interest.
4. In addition to the provisions of paragraph 4 of article 12-02, an entity may not choose a valuation method or divide purchases into independent contracts in order to evade the obligations contained in this chapter.
5. When an individual requirement results in the award of more than one contract or the contracts are awarded in separate parts, the basis for valuation will be:
a. the actual value of successive contracts of the same nature entered into during the preceding fiscal year or in the preceding 12 months, adjusted where possible for expected changes in quantity and value in the following 12 months; either
b. the estimated value of successive contracts of the same nature entered into during the fiscal year or in the 12 months following the initial contract.
6. In the case of lease or rental contracts, with or without a purchase option, or contracts in which a total price is not specified, the basis for valuation will be:
a. in the case of contracts signed for a specific period, the calculation will be made on the basis of the total value of the contract during its period of validity; either
b. In the case of contracts for an indefinite term, the base will be the estimated monthly payment multiplied by 48.
If the entity is not certain whether a contract is for fixed or indefinite terms, it will calculate the value of the contract using the method indicated in subparagraph b).
7. When the bidding conditions include clauses that allow the quotation of optional or alternative goods or services, the basis for valuation will be the total value of the maximum purchase allowed, including all possible optional purchases.
Article 12-04: National treatment and non-discrimination.
1. With respect to the measures included in this Chapter, each Party shall grant to the goods of the other Party, to the suppliers of those goods and to the service providers of the other Party, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable granted to:
a. its own goods and suppliers; Y
b. the goods and suppliers of another Party.
2. With respect to the measures included in this Chapter, neither Party may:
a. give a supplier established in its territory treatment less favorable than that accorded to another supplier established in its territory by reason of the degree of foreign affiliation or ownership; either
b. discriminate against a supplier established in its territory on the grounds that the goods or services offered by that supplier for a particular purchase are goods or services of the other Party.
3. Paragraph 1 shall not apply to measures relating to customs duties or other charges of any kind on or in connection with importation, the method of collection of such duties and charges, or other import regulations, including restrictions and formalities.
4. The Parties shall not establish representation or local presence requirements that are intended to discriminate in favor of national suppliers.
Article 12-05: Rules of origin.
For the purposes of public sector purchases covered by this Chapter, neither Party shall apply rules of origin to goods imported from the other Party that are different from or incompatible with the rules of origin contained in Chapter V (Rules of Origin).
Article 12-06: Denial of benefits.
A Party may deny the benefits derived from this chapter to a service provider of the other Party after prior notification and consultation, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out important business activities in the territory of any Party and is owned or controlled by persons of a non-Party country.
Article 12-07: Prohibition of special compensatory conditions.
Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not take into account, request or impose special compensatory conditions in the qualification and selection of suppliers, goods or services, in the evaluation of offers or in the award of contracts. For the purposes of this article, special compensatory conditions are understood to be those that an entity imposes or takes into account before or during the purchase procedure to promote local development or improve balance of payments accounts, through local content requirements. , licensing of technology, investment, countertrade or similar requirements.
Article 12-08: Technical specifications.
1. Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not prepare, adopt or apply any technical specification that has the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade.
2. Each Party shall ensure that, where applicable, any technical specifications stipulated by its entities:
a. is defined in terms of performance criteria rather than descriptive or design features; Y
b. is based on international standards, national technical regulations, recognized national standards or building codes.
3. Each Party shall ensure that the technical specifications stipulated by its entities do not require or make reference to a certain brand or trade name, patent, design or type, specific origin, or producer or supplier, unless there is no other sufficiently precise or understandable manner to describe the purchase requirements and provided that, in such cases, words such as "or equivalent" are included in the bidding conditions.
4. Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not solicit or accept, in a manner that has the effect of preventing competition, advice that could be used in preparing or adopting any technical specification with respect to a particular purchase from a person who may have commercial interest in that purchase.
Section B - Tender Procedures
Article 12-09: Tender procedures.
1. Entities will make their purchases through open, selective or restricted tenders. Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 12-16, the entities of each Party may opt for open or selective bidding procedures, provided that the chosen procedure guarantees the maximum possible competition.
2. Each Party shall ensure that the bidding procedures of its entities:
a. are applied in a non-discriminatory manner; Y
b. are consistent with this article and with articles 12-11 through 12-16.
3. In this regard, each Party shall ensure that its entities:
a. do not provide any supplier with information about a particular purchase in a way that has the effect of preventing competition or conferring an advantage on a specific supplier; Y
b. provide all suppliers equal access to information regarding a purchase during the period prior to the issuance of any call or bidding conditions.
Article 12-10: Qualification of suppliers.
1. Pursuant to Article 12-04, in the qualification of suppliers during the bidding procedure, no entity of a Party may discriminate between suppliers of the other Party or between national suppliers and suppliers of the other Party.
2. The qualification of suppliers carried out by an entity will be consistent with the following:
a. The conditions for the participation of suppliers in the bidding procedures will be published sufficiently in advance, so that the suppliers have adequate time to start and, to the extent that is compatible with the efficient operation of the contracting process, finish the procedures. qualification procedures;
b. the conditions for participating in the bidding procedures, such as financial guarantees, technical qualifications and the information necessary to prove the financial, commercial and technical capacity of the suppliers, as well as the verification that the supplier satisfies those conditions, will be limited those essential to ensure compliance with the contract in question;
c. the financial, commercial and technical capacity of a supplier shall be determined on the basis of its global activity, including both its activity carried out in the territory of the Party of the supplier, and its activity in the territory of the Party of the purchasing entity, if any;
d. An entity may not use the qualification process, including the time it takes, to exclude suppliers of another Party from a list of suppliers or not consider them for a given purchase;
and. an entity shall recognize as qualified suppliers those suppliers of another Party that meet the conditions required to participate in a specific purchase;
F. An entity shall consider for a given purchase those suppliers of another Party that request to participate in the purchase and that have not yet been qualified, provided that sufficient time is available to complete the qualification procedure;
g. An entity that maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers will ensure that suppliers can request their qualification at all times, that all qualified suppliers who request it are included in the list within a reasonably short period of time, and that all suppliers those included in the list are notified of the cancellation of the list or their removal from the list;
h. when, after the publication of the call in accordance with the provisions of article 12-11, a supplier that has not yet been qualified requests to participate in a certain purchase, the entity will initiate the qualification procedure without delay;
Yo. An entity will communicate to any provider that has requested its qualification, the decision on whether it has been qualified; Y
j. When an entity rejects a qualification request or ceases to recognize a supplier's qualification, at the supplier's request the entity will promptly provide pertinent information on the reasons for its action.
3. Each Party:
a. it will ensure that each of its entities uses a single qualification procedure, however the procedure for evaluating suppliers will vary according to the nature of the aspects to be analyzed; when the entity establishes the need to resort to a different procedure and, at the request of the other Party, is prepared to demonstrate that need, it may use additional qualification procedures; Y
b. It will try to reduce to a minimum the differences between the rating procedures of its entities.
4. Nothing in paragraphs 2 and 3 shall prevent an entity from excluding a provider for reasons such as bankruptcy or misrepresentation.
Article 12-11: Invitation to participate.
1. Except as provided in article 12-16, in accordance with paragraphs 2, 3 and 5, an entity shall publish an invitation to participate for all purchases, in the corresponding publication indicated in the annex to this article.
2. The invitation to participate will take the form of a call that will contain the following information:
a. a description of the nature and quantity of the goods or services to be purchased, including any future purchase options and, if possible:
i) an estimate of when those options may be exercised; Y
ii) in the case of successive contracts of the same nature, an estimate of when subsequent calls may be issued;
b. an indication of whether the tender is open or selective;
c. if relevant, the date to begin or conclude the delivery of the goods or services to be purchased;
d. when applicable, the address to which the request must be sent to be invited to bid or to qualify on the list of suppliers and the deadline for receipt of the request;
and. the address to which the offers will be sent and the deadline for their receipt;
F. The address of the entity that will award the contract and that will provide any information necessary to obtain specifications and other documents;
g. a statement of any conditions of an economic or technical nature and of any financial guarantees, information and documents required from suppliers;
h. the amount and form of payment of any amount to be paid for the bidding conditions; and
Yo. the indication of whether the entity calls for the presentation of offers for the purchase, lease or rent, with or without a purchase option.
3. In the case of selective bidding, the invitation to participate will contain, in addition to the provisions of paragraph 2, the deadlines indicated for the submission of requests for admission to the bidding, when this does not imply the use of a list of suppliers. .
4. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3, an entity indicated in annex 2 to article 12-02 or in annex 3 to article 12-02 may use as an invitation to participate a scheduled purchase call, which will contain the information in paragraphs 2 and 3 to the extent that it is available to the entity, but which shall include, as a minimum, the following information:
a. a description of the object of the purchase;
b. the deadlines set for the receipt of offers or for the presentation of requests to be invited to bid;
c. the address from which documentation related to the purchase may be requested;
d. an indication that interested suppliers should express to the entity their interest in the purchase; Y
and. the identification of an information center in the entity where additional information can be obtained.
5. An entity that uses a scheduled purchase call as an invitation to participate will subsequently invite all suppliers that have expressed interest in the purchase by submitting a request referred to in subparagraph b) of paragraph 4, to confirm their interest. , based on the information provided by the entity that will include, at least, the information stipulated in paragraphs 2 and 4.
6. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3, an entity indicated in annex 2 to article 12-02 or in annex 3 to article 12-02 may use a call regarding the qualification system as an invitation to participate. An entity that makes use of such a call will offer in a timely manner, in accordance with the considerations referred to in paragraph 8 of article 12-15, information that allows all suppliers that have expressed an interest in participating in the purchase to have a real possibility to assess your interest. The information will normally include the data required for the call referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3. The information provided to an interested supplier will be provided without discrimination to all other interested parties.
7. In the case of selective bidding procedures, an entity that establishes or maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers will insert annually, in the appropriate publication referred to in the annex to this article, a notice containing the following information:
a. a listing of all current lists, including their headings, in relation to the goods or services or categories of goods or services purchased through the lists;
b. the conditions that suppliers must meet to be included in the lists and the methods according to which the entity in question will verify each of those conditions; Y
c. the period of validity of the lists and the formalities for its renewal.
8. When, after the publication of an invitation to participate, but before the expiration of the period set for the opening or receipt of offers, as stated in the calls or in the bidding conditions, the entity considers it necessary to make modifications or reissue the call or the bidding conditions, the entity will ensure that the same diffusion is given to the call or to the new or modified bidding conditions as was given to the original documentation. Any material information provided to one supplier regarding a particular purchase will be simultaneously provided to the other interested suppliers, sufficiently in advance to allow all interested parties appropriate time to review the information and to respond.
9. An entity will indicate in the calls referred to in this article that the purchase is covered by this chapter.
Article 12-12: Selective bidding procedures.
1. In selective bidding procedures, the entity will publish an invitation to participate in accordance with article 12-11.
2. In order to guarantee optimal effective competition between the suppliers of the Parties in the selective bidding procedures, an entity may directly invite, for each purchase, the largest number of national suppliers and suppliers of the other Party that is compatible with efficient operation of the purchasing system.
3. An entity may limit, in accordance with objective criteria and for fully justified reasons, the number of offers to be considered when the analysis of all those received could substantially affect the efficient operation of the purchasing system, as long as the provisions are not breached. of article 12-04.
4. Pursuant to the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 5, an entity that maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers may select those who will be directly summoned to bid on a specific purchase. In the selection process, the entity will give equal opportunities to the suppliers included in the list.
5. Subject to the provisions of subparagraphs f) and h) of paragraph 2 of article 12-10, an entity will allow a supplier that requests to participate in a certain purchase, submit an offer and take it into account. The number of additional suppliers authorized to participate will only be limited for reasons of efficient operation of the purchasing system.
6. When an entity does not summon or admit a provider to the tender, at the latter's request, it will promptly provide relevant information on the reasons for its action.
Article 12-13: Deadlines for bidding and delivery.
1. An entity:
a. by setting a deadline, it will provide suppliers of the other Party with sufficient time to prepare and submit bids before the closing of the bid;
b. In setting a deadline, in accordance with its own reasonable needs, it will take into account factors such as the complexity of the purchase, the anticipated degree of subcontracting, and the time normally required to transmit offers by mail both from foreign locations and within the national territory; Y
c. when establishing the deadline for the receipt of offers or requests for admission to the tender, it will duly consider publication delays.
2. An entity shall provide that:
a. in open bidding procedures, the term for the receipt of an offer is not less than 40 days from the date of publication of a call, in accordance with the provisions of article 12-11;
b. in selective bidding procedures that do not imply the use of a permanent list of qualified suppliers, the deadline for submitting a request for admission to the bidding process is not less than 25 days from the date of publication of a call, from in accordance with the provisions of article 12-11, and the term for the receipt of offers is not less than 40 days from the date of publication of a call; Y
c. in selective bidding procedures that imply the use of a permanent list of qualified suppliers, the term for the receipt of offers is not less than 40 days from the date of the first invitation to bid, but when this last date does not coincides with the publication of a call referred to in article 12-11, no less than 40 days must elapse between publication and receipt of offers.
3. An entity may reduce the periods provided in paragraph 2 in accordance with the following:
a. when a call has been published as provided in paragraphs 3 or 5 of article 12-11, within a period of not less than 40 days and not more than 12 months, the 40-day term for the receipt of offers may be reduced to not less than 24 days;
b. In the case of a second publication or a subsequent publication related to successive contracts of the same nature, in accordance with literal a) of paragraph 2 of article 12-11, the 40-day term for the receipt of offers may be reduced to no less than 24 days;
c. When, for reasons of urgency duly justified by the entity and which it could not have foreseen, the established deadlines cannot be observed, in no case will these deadlines be less than ten days from the date of publication of a call in accordance with article 12-11; either
d. when one of the entities indicated in annex 2 to article 12-02 or in annex 3 to article 12-02 uses as an invitation to participate a call referred to in paragraph 6 of article 12-11, the entity and the selected suppliers may set, by mutual agreement, the deadlines; however, in the absence of an agreement, the entity may set terms sufficiently long to allow the due submission of offers, which in no case shall be less than ten days.
4. An entity shall take into account factors such as the complexity of the purchase, the anticipated degree of subcontracting, and the time realistically required for delivery in scheduling the goods or services in accordance with its reasonable needs. production, dispatch and transportation of the goods from the different places of supply.
Article 12-14: Bidding conditions.
1. When entities provide bidding conditions to suppliers, the documentation will contain all the necessary information that allows them to duly present their offers, including the information that must be published in the call referred to in paragraph 2 of article 12-11, except for the information required under literal h), paragraph 2 of that article. The documentation will also include:
a. the address of the entity to which the offers should be sent;
b. the address where requests for additional information should be sent;
c. the date and time of the closing of the reception of offers and the term during which they will be validated;
d. the persons authorized, other than the participating suppliers, to attend the opening of the offers and the date, time and place of that opening;
and. a description of any conditions of an economic or technical nature and of any financial guarantees, information and documents required from suppliers;
F. a full description of the goods or services to be purchased and any other requirements, including technical specifications, certificates of conformity, and necessary drawings, drawings and instructions;
g. the criteria on which the award of the contract will be based, such as the price and any other factor that will be considered in the evaluation of the offers; The cost elements that will be taken into account when evaluating the prices of the offers will include, where appropriate, aspects such as transportation, insurance and inspection expenses and, in the case of goods or services of the other Party, the rights of customs and other import charges, taxes and currency of payment;
h. the terms of payment; and
Yo. any other stipulations or conditions.
2. An entity:
a. provide the bidding conditions at the request of a supplier participating in open bidding procedures or requesting to participate in selective bidding procedures, and will promptly respond to any reasonable request for clarification thereof; Y
b. will promptly respond to any reasonable request for relevant information from a supplier participating in the tender, provided that such information does not give that supplier an advantage over its competitors in the contract award procedure.
Article 12-15: Presentation, reception and opening of offers and awarding of contracts.
1. The entity will use procedures for the presentation, reception and opening of offers and the awarding of contracts that are consistent with the following:
a. Bids will normally be submitted in writing, either directly or by post;
b. When bids transmitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile or other means of electronic transmission are admitted in the invitation to participate, the bid submitted shall include all the information necessary for its evaluation, in particular the final price proposed by the supplier and a statement that the provider accepts all the clauses and conditions of the call;
c. Offers submitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile or other means of electronic transmission will be confirmed within the term set in the call or in the bidding conditions, sending the original document of the offers or a signed copy of the telex, telegram, telefacsimile or message electronic;
d. the content of the telex, telegram, telefacsimile or electronic message will prevail in case there is a difference or contradiction between it and any other documentation received after the term for the receipt of offers has expired;
