and. it will not be allowed to present offers by telephone;
F. Applications to participate in a selective bidding may be submitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile and, when permitted, by other means of electronic transmission; Y
g. The opportunities to correct involuntary formal errors, such as arithmetic errors or others that do not affect the essence of the offer, which are granted to suppliers during the period between the opening of the offers and the award of the contract, may not be used. in such a way that they discriminate between providers.
For purposes of this paragraph, "electronic transmission means" include those through which the recipient can produce a printed copy of the offer at the place of destination of the transmission.
2. No entity will penalize a supplier for causes exclusively attributable to the entity.
3. All the offers requested by an entity in the open or selective bidding procedures will be received and opened in accordance with the procedures and under the conditions that guarantee the regularity of the opening of the offers. The entity will keep the information corresponding to the opening of the offers. The information will remain available to the participants with legitimate interest and to the competent authorities of the Party to be used, if required, in accordance with article 12-17, article 12-19 or chapter XVII, (Dispute Resolution).
4. An entity shall award contracts in accordance with the following:
a. In order for an offer to be considered for the award, it must comply, at the time of opening, with the requirements stipulated in the call or in the bidding conditions and come from suppliers that meet the conditions of participation;
b. If the entity receives an offer that is abnormally lower in price than the others submitted, the entity may check with the supplier to ensure that the supplier satisfies the conditions for participation and is or will be able to comply with the terms of the contract;
c. unless for reasons of public interest it decides not to award the contract, the entity will award it to the supplier that it has considered capable of performing the contract and whose offer is the lowest price or the most advantageous in accordance with the specific evaluation criteria established in the call or in the bidding conditions;
d. the awards will be made in accordance with the criteria and requirements established in the bidding conditions; Y
and. The clauses that allow the quotation of optional or alternative goods or services will not be used in order to circumvent this chapter.
5. No entity of a Party may condition the award of a contract on the fact that a supplier has previously been assigned one or more contracts by an entity of that Party or on the supplier's previous work experience in the territory of that Party.
6. An entity:
a. upon express request, it will promptly inform the participating providers of the decisions on the awarded contracts and, if requested, do so in writing; Y
b. at the express request of a supplier whose offer has not been chosen, it will provide the relevant information to that supplier about the reasons why its offer was not chosen, the characteristics and advantages of the selected offer and the name of the winning supplier.
7. Within a reasonable period of time after the award of the contract, an entity shall insert a notice in the appropriate publication referred to in the annex to article 12-11 containing the following information:
a. a description of the nature and quantity of the goods or services that are the subject of the contract;
b. the name and address of the entity that awards the contract;
c. the award date;
d. the name and address of each selected provider;
and. the value of the contract; Y
F. the tendering procedure used.
8. Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 through 7, an entity may withhold certain information about the contract award when its disclosure:
a. could impede compliance with laws or be contrary to the public interest;
b. harm the legitimate business interests of a particular person; either
c. out to the detriment of fair competition between suppliers.
9. Subparagraphs b) and c) of paragraph 8 shall not apply when information is requested in matters of public interest.
Article 12-16: Restricted bidding.
1. An entity of a Party may, in the circumstances and in accordance with the conditions described in paragraph 2, use restricted bidding procedures and accordingly deviate from the provisions of Articles 12-09 through 12-15, provided that restricted bidding procedures are not used to avoid the maximum possible competition or in a way that constitutes a means of discrimination between suppliers of the other Parties or of protection of national suppliers.
2. An entity may use restricted tendering procedures in the following circumstances and under the following conditions, as appropriate:
a. in the absence of offers in response to an open or selective call for tenders or when the offers submitted have resulted from collusion or do not comply with the essential requirements of the bidding conditions, or when the offers have been formulated by suppliers that do not comply with the conditions of participation provided in accordance with this chapter, provided that the initial purchase requirements are not materially changed in the award of the contract;
b. when the goods or services can only be supplied by a specific provider without there being other alternatives or reasonable substitutes because they are works of art or for reasons related to the protection of patents, copyrights or other exclusive rights, or reserved information or when for technical reasons there is no competition;
c. to the extent strictly necessary when, for reasons of extreme urgency due to events that the entity cannot foresee, it would not be possible to obtain the goods or services on time through open or selective bidding;
d. in the case of additional deliveries from the initial supplier either as replacement parts or continuing services for existing materials, services or facilities, or as an expansion of existing materials, services or facilities, when a change of supplier would require the entity to acquire equipment or services that do not meet the requirement to be interchangeable with existing equipment or services, including software, to the extent that the initial purchase of the software was covered by this chapter;
and. when an entity acquires prototypes or a first good or service that are manufactured at its request in the course and for the execution of a specific research, experimentation, study or original manufacturing contract. Once the contracts of this class have been fulfilled, the purchase of goods or services that are made as a result of them will be adjusted to articles 12-10 to 12-15. The original development of a first good may include its production in limited quantity in order to take into account the results of field trials and to demonstrate that the good lends itself to mass production meeting acceptable quality standards, but does not include series production to determine commercial viability or to recover research and development costs;
F. for goods purchased in a commodity market whose price is quoted in an international market;
g. for purchases made under exceptionally favorable conditions that are only offered at very short notice, but does not include purchases made under ordinary conditions from regular suppliers. Exceptionally favorable conditions are understood to be those that are substantially advantageous for the purchasing entity in relation to normal market conditions, such as extraordinary disposals made by companies that are not normally suppliers or the disposal of assets of persons in liquidation or under administration. judicial;
h. for contracts to be awarded to the winner of an architectural design competition, provided that the competition is:
i) organized in accordance with the principles of this chapter, including in relation to the publication of the invitation to qualified suppliers to bid;
ii) organized in such a way that the design contract is awarded to the winner; Y
iii) submitted to an independent jury; and
Yo. when an entity requires consulting services related to aspects of a confidential nature, the disclosure of which could reasonably be expected to compromise confidential information of the public sector, cause serious economic damage or, similarly, be contrary to the public interest.
3. The entities will justify the reasons on which they base the use of restricted bidding and will prepare a written report on each contract they have awarded in accordance with paragraph 2. Each report will contain the name of the procuring entity, the value and the class of goods or services procured, the country of origin, and a statement of the circumstances and conditions described in paragraph 2 that justified the use of restricted bidding. The entity will keep each report in a file in which the complete documentation related to the contract will be added. These will be available to the competent authorities of the Party to be used, if required, in accordance with the provisions of Article 12-17, Article 12-19 or Chapter XVII (Dispute Settlement).
Section C - Challenge Procedures
Article 12-17: Challenge procedures.
1. In order to promote fair, open, and impartial procurement procedures, each Party shall adopt and maintain administrative challenge procedures for purchases covered by this Chapter, in accordance with the following:
a. each Party shall establish a procedure for suppliers to challenge the different aspects of the purchasing process which, for the purposes of this article, begins from the moment an entity has defined its purchase requirement and continues until the contract is awarded;
b. Before initiating a challenge procedure, a Party may encourage the supplier to seek a solution to its complaint with the procuring entity;
c. each Party shall ensure that its entities give timely and impartial consideration to any complaint or challenge regarding purchases covered by this chapter;
d. whether or not a supplier has attempted to resolve its complaint with the entity, or after it has failed to reach a successful resolution, neither Party may preclude the supplier from initiating a challenge proceeding or seeking other available remedy;
and. a Party may request a supplier to notify the entity of the initiation of a challenge procedure;
F. a Party may limit the period within which a supplier can initiate the challenge procedure, but in no case shall this period be less than ten business days from the moment the supplier knows or is considered to have known the basis for the complaint. complain;
g. each Party shall establish or designate a specialized reviewing authority with no substantial interest in the outcome of the purchases to receive challenges and issue the resolutions and, where appropriate, the pertinent recommendations;
h. upon receiving the challenge, the reviewing authority will proceed to investigate it expeditiously;
Yo. the reviewing authority will limit its considerations to the challenge itself;
j. the reviewing authority will issue a resolution to resolve the challenge, which may include directives to the entity to re-evaluate the offers, terminate the purchase process or the contract, or submit it again to the contest;
k. generally, entities will follow the recommendations of the reviewing authority;
he. each Party shall empower its review authority to make further written recommendations to an entity, at the conclusion of the challenge proceeding, regarding any phase of its purchasing process that was found to be problematic during the challenge investigation, including recommendations for changes in the entity's purchasing procedures, so that they are consistent with this chapter;
m. the reviewing authority will notify in a timely manner and in writing the result of its inquiries, resolutions and recommendations regarding the challenges, and will make them available to the Parties and interested persons;
no. each Party shall specify in writing and make generally available all of its challenge procedures; Y
either. In order to verify that the procurement process was carried out in accordance with this chapter, each Party shall ensure that each of its entities maintains complete documentation relating to each of its purchases, including a written record of all communications that affect substantially the purchasing process, for a period of at least three years from the date the contract was awarded.
2. A Party may request the initiation of the challenge procedure only after the call has been published or, in case of not being published, after the bidding conditions are available. When a Party establishes this requirement, the term of ten business days referred to in subparagraph f) of paragraph 1, will begin to run no earlier than the date on which the call has been published or the bidding conditions are available.
Section D - General Provisions
Article 12-18: Exceptions.
1. Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to prevent a Party from taking any action or refraining from disclosing information that it considers necessary to protect its essential security interests in connection with the purchase of arms, ammunition, or war materiel. , or any other essential contracting for national security or for national defense purposes.
2. As long as these measures are not applied in such a way that they constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between the Parties where the same conditions exist or that they imply a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties, nothing in this Chapter shall be construed in the meaning of preventing a Party from establishing or maintaining the measures:
a. necessary to protect morality, public order or safety;
b. necessary to protect human, animal or plant life and health;
c. necessary to protect intellectual property; either
d. related to goods or services provided by disabled people, charitable institutions or prison labor.
Article 12-19: Provision of information.
1. In addition to what is established in Article 15-02 (Publication), each Party shall promptly publish any law, regulation, jurisprudence, administrative resolution of general application and any procedure, including model contractual clauses, related to public sector procurement. included in this chapter, by inserting them in the pertinent publications referred to in the annex to article 12-11.
2. Each Party:
a. explain to the other Party, upon request, its public sector procurement procedures;
b. ensure that its entities, upon request from a supplier, promptly explain their public sector procurement practices and procedures; Y
c. shall designate, no later than the entry into force of this Agreement, one or more information centers for:
i) facilitate communication between the Parties; Y
ii) answer, upon request, all reasonable questions from the other Party in order to provide relevant information on aspects covered by this chapter.
3. A Party may request additional information on the award of the contract that may be necessary to determine if a purchase was made in accordance with the provisions of this chapter with respect to offers that have not been selected. For this purpose, the Party of the purchasing entity will provide information on the relative characteristics and advantages of the winning offer and the price of the contract. When disclosure of this information may prejudice competition in future tenders, the requesting Party may not disclose the information except after consulting with and obtaining the consent of the Party that provided the information.
4. Each Party shall provide to the other Party, upon request, the information available to that Party or its entities on its entities' covered purchases and on individual contracts awarded by its entities.
5. No Party may disclose confidential information the disclosure of which would harm the legitimate business interests of a particular person or would be detrimental to fair competition between suppliers, without the formal authorization of the person who provided such information to the Party.
6. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to require a Party to provide confidential information the disclosure of which would impede law enforcement or otherwise be contrary to the public interest.
7. With a view to ensuring effective supervision of purchases covered by this Chapter, each Party shall collect statistics and provide the other Party with an annual report in accordance with the following requirements, unless the Parties otherwise agree:
a. statistics on the estimated value of the contracts awarded, both below and above the value of the applicable thresholds, broken down by entity;
b. statistics on the number and total value of contracts above the value of the applicable thresholds, broken down by entities, by categories of goods and services established in accordance with the classification systems developed under this chapter and by country of origin of the goods and purchased services;
c. Statistics on the total number and value of contracts awarded under Article 12-16, broken down by entity, by category of goods or services, and by country of origin of the goods and services purchased; Y
d. Statistics on the number and total value of contracts awarded in accordance with the exceptions to this chapter established in annexes 8 and 9 to article 12-02, broken down by entity.
8. Each Party may organize by state or municipality any portion of the report referred to in paragraph 7 that corresponds to the entities indicated in Annex 3 to Article 12-02.
Article 12-20: Technical cooperation.
1. The Parties shall cooperate, to achieve a greater understanding of their public sector procurement systems, with a view to achieving the greatest access to public sector procurement opportunities for suppliers of any of them.
2. Each Party will provide the other and its suppliers, on a cost recovery basis, information regarding training and orientation programs related to its public sector procurement systems and access without discrimination to any program it carries out.
3. The training and orientation programs referred to in paragraph 2 include:
a. training of public sector personnel directly involved in public sector procurement procedures;
b. training of suppliers interested in taking advantage of public sector purchasing opportunities;
c. the explanation and description of specific aspects of each Party's public sector procurement system, such as its challenge mechanism; Y
d. information regarding public sector procurement market opportunities.
4. Each Party shall establish, no later than the entry into force of this Agreement, at least one contact point to provide information on the training and orientation programs referred to in this article.
Article 12-21: Joint participation programs for micro, small and medium industry.
1. Upon the entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will establish the Micro, Small and Medium Industry Committee, made up of representatives of each Party. The Committee will meet by mutual agreement of the Parties, but not less than once a year, and will report annually to the Commission on the efforts of the Parties to promote public sector procurement opportunities for their micro, small, and medium-sized industries.
2. The Committee shall work to facilitate the following activities of the Parties:
a. the identification of available opportunities for the training of the personnel of micro, small and medium-sized industries in terms of public sector purchasing procedures;
b. the identification of micro, small and medium-sized industries interested in becoming business partners of micro, small and medium-sized industries in the territory of the other Party;
c. the development of databases on micro, small and medium-sized industries in the territory of each Party to be used by entities of the other Party that wish to make purchases from smaller-scale companies;
d. consultations regarding the factors that each Party uses to establish its eligibility criteria for any program for micro, small, and medium-sized industries; Y
and. carrying out activities to deal with any related matter.
Article 12-22: Rectifications or modifications.
1. A Party may modify its coverage under this chapter only in exceptional circumstances.
2. When a Party modifies its coverage under this chapter:
a. notify its national section of the Secretariat and the other Parties of the modification;
b. it will incorporate the change to the corresponding annex; Y
c. will propose to the other Party appropriate compensatory adjustments to its coverage, in order to maintain a level of coverage comparable to that existing before the modification.
3. Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 and 2, a Party may make exclusively formal rectifications and minor amendments to its schedules in Annexes 1 to 6, 8 and 9 to Article 12-02, provided that it notifies the other Party of those rectifications. and its national section of the Secretariat, and no Party expresses its objection to the proposed rectifications within a period of 30 days. In those cases, it will not be necessary to propose compensation.
4. Notwithstanding other provisions of this Chapter, a Party may carry out reorganizations of its public sector entities covered by this Chapter, including programs for the decentralization of the purchases of those entities or the corresponding public functions cease to be carried out by any public sector entity, whether or not included in this chapter. In those cases, it will not be necessary to propose compensation. Neither Party may carry out such reorganizations or programs in order to evade compliance with the obligations of this chapter.
5. Each Party may resort to the dispute resolution procedure in accordance with the provisions of Chapter XVII, (Dispute Resolution), when it considers that:
a. the adjustment proposed in accordance with subparagraph c) of paragraph 2 is not adequate to maintain a level comparable to that of the mutually agreed coverage; either
b. a minor rectification or amendment in accordance with paragraph 3 or a reorganization in accordance with paragraph 4 does not meet the requirements stipulated in those paragraphs and, as a consequence, requires compensation.
Article 12-23: Alienation of entities.
1. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prevent a Party from disposing of an entity covered by this chapter.
2. If, through the public offering of shares of an entity contained in Annex 2 to Article 12-02, or through other methods, the entity ceases to be subject to central or federal governmental control, the Party may remove that entity from its list in that annex and remove the entity from the coverage of this chapter, after notifying the other Party and its national section of the Secretariat.
3. When a Party objects to the withdrawal of the entity because it considers that the entity in question remains subject to central or federal government control, that Party may resort to the dispute settlement procedure pursuant to Chapter XVII, (Dispute Settlement).
Article 12-24: Future negotiations.
1. With a view to achieving the further liberalization of their respective public sector procurement markets, the Parties shall begin negotiations when so determined by the Commission.
2. In those negotiations, the Parties shall review all aspects of their public sector procurement practices for the purposes of:
a. evaluate the operation of their public sector procurement systems;
b. seek to expand the coverage of the chapter by incorporating:
i) other parastatal companies, decentralized entities and public companies; Y
ii) purchases subject in some way to legislative or administrative exceptions; Y
c. review the value of the thresholds.
3. Prior to such review, the Parties shall consult with their state or municipal governments with a view to reaching commitments, on a voluntary and reciprocal basis, for the incorporation into this chapter of purchases by state or municipal government entities and companies.

Annex 4 to the article12-02
List of goods
Section A - General Provisions
1. This chapter applies to all property, except as provided in paragraphs 2 and 3.
2. In relation to Costa Rica, the assets of a strategic nature indicated in section B acquired by the Ministry of the Interior and the municipalities and the Ministry of Security are excluded from the coverage of this chapter, in accordance with the provisions of article 12 -18.
3. In relation to Mexico, the strategic assets indicated in section B acquired by the Ministry of National Defense and the Ministry of the Navy are excluded from the coverage of this chapter, in accordance with the provisions of article 12-18 .
Section B - List of certain assets
Armament
nuclear war material
fire control equipment
ammunition and explosives
guided missiles
Aircraft and Aircraft Structural Components
Aircraft components and accessories
Aircraft take-off, landing and ground handling equipment
space vehicles
Boats, small structures, pangas and floating docks
Vessels and maritime equipment
Annex 5 to the article12-02
Service List
Section A - General Provisions
1. Without prejudice to the provisions of Chapter IX (General principles on trade in services), this chapter shall apply to purchases of services from the moment each Party draws up its list of reservations in accordance with the agreed commitments and deadlines. in Chapter IX (General principles on trade in services). Until that time, the Parties will apply their legislation in force on the matter on the date of entry into force of this Agreement. No amendment to that legislation may be more restrictive.
2. The Parties shall develop a common classification system for services no later than one year after the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
Annex 6 to the article12-02
Construction services
1. Without prejudice to the provisions of Chapter IX (General principles on trade in services), this Chapter shall apply to purchases of construction services from the moment each Party draws up its list of reservations in accordance with the commitments and deadlines agreed in Chapter IX (General principles on trade in services). Until that time, the Parties will apply their legislation in force on the matter on the date of entry into force of this Agreement. No amendment to that legislation may be more restrictive.
2. The Parties shall develop a common classification system for construction services no later than one year after the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
Annex 7 to the article12-02
Indexing and conversion of threshold value
1. The calculations referred to in literal c), paragraph 1 of article 12-02, will be made in accordance with the following:
a. the inflation rate of the United States of America will be determined based on the producer price index for finished goods published by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States of America;
b. the first adjustment for inflation, which will take effect on January 1, 1997, will be calculated based on the period from November 1, 1995, to October 30, 1996;
c. all subsequent adjustments will be calculated over biennial periods, beginning on November 1, and taking effect on January 1 of the year immediately following the end of the biennial period;
d. the inflationary adjustment will be estimated according to the following formula:
T0 x (1+π i )= T1;
T0 = ​​threshold value in the base period;
π i = accumulated inflation rate in the United States of America in the i-th biennial period; Y
T1 = new threshold value.
2. The exchange rate for determining the value of the thresholds, for the purposes of this chapter, will be the current value of the Costa Rican colon and the Mexican peso in relation to the US dollar as of the date of publication of the notice of the projected contract. The Parties will calculate and convert the value of the thresholds into their own currencies. It is understood that these calculations will be based on the official exchange rate of the Central Bank of Costa Rica and the Bank of Mexico.

Annex 9 to the article12-02
General notes
Costa Rican Roster
1. This chapter does not apply to purchases made:
a. with a view to commercial resale by government stores;
b. in accordance with loans from regional or multilateral financial institutions to the extent that those instruments agree to different procedures; neither
c. between one and another entity of Costa Rica.
2. This chapter does not apply to the purchase of transportation services that are part of a purchase contract, or are related to it.
3. National security exceptions include purchases made in support of safeguarding nuclear materials or technology.
4. The provisions related to the selective bidding procedure will not be applied until Costa Rican legislation regulates and develops this procedure.
5. In literal c), paragraph 1 of article 12-15, the confirmations of the offers presented by the mechanisms authorized therein will be made, if applicable, by any of the means of legal representation.
6. Subparagraph f) of paragraph 1 and paragraph 2 of article 12-17 will not apply in the case of Costa Rica.
7. Challenge and appeal mechanisms:
a. To comply with the provisions of literal a), paragraph 1 of article 12-17 in the case of Costa Rica, suppliers may challenge the conditions established in the call or the bidding conditions for reasons of discrimination, defects in the procedure or for deeming that certain conditions illegitimately limit the freedom of competition or violate equal opportunities; or file an appeal when they consider that the adjudication act is substantially inconsistent with the legal system or that the legal procedure is flawed with absolute nullity;
b. The appeal to challenge the conditions established in the call or the bidding conditions, duly reasoned, will be filed with the reviewing authority within the first third of the term conferred for the receipt of offers. The reviewing authority will dictate its resolution within the second third of the indicated term;
c. The appeal against the adjudication act shall be filed, duly substantiated, before the reviewing authority within five business days following the date of publication referred to in paragraph 7 of article 12-15.
Mexico Roster
1. This chapter does not apply to purchases made:
a. with a view to commercial resale by government stores;
b. in accordance with lending from regional or multilateral financial institutions to the extent that such institutions impose different procedures, except for local content requirements; either
c. between one entity and another in Mexico.
2. This chapter does not apply to the purchase of transportation services that are part of or related to a purchase contract.
3. National security exceptions include purchases made in support of safeguarding nuclear materials or technology.
4. Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, Mexico may reserve purchase contracts for the obligations of this chapter, for an amount equivalent to 5% of its total annual purchases.
5. In accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1 of article 12-17, when investigating the challenge, the reviewing authority may delay the award of the proposed contract until the resolution of the challenge, except in cases of urgency or when the delay could be contrary to the public interest.

Chapter XIII
Investment
Section A - Investment
Article 13-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
ICSID: International Center for Settlement of Investment Disputes;
New York Convention: United Nations Convention on the Recognition and Enforcement of Foreign Arbitral Awards, held in New York, June 10, 1958;
Inter-American Convention : Inter-American Convention on International Commercial Arbitration, held in Panama on January 30, 1975;
ICSID Convention: the Convention on the Settlement of Investment Disputes between States and Nationals of other States, concluded in Washington on March 18, 1965;
claim: the claim made by the disputing investor against a Party under the terms of section B of this chapter;
company: any legal person, constituted or organized under the legislation of a Party, whether or not for profit and privately or governmental property, as well as other organizations or economic units that are constituted or, in any case, duly organized under that legislation, such as branches, trusts, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures or other associations;
enterprise of a Party: an enterprise incorporated or organized under the laws of a Party and having its domicile in the territory of that Party; and a branch located in the territory of a Party that carries out business activities therein;
investment: all kinds of assets and rights of any nature, acquired with resources transferred to the territory of a Party, or reinvested in it, by investors of another Party, such as:
- shares and any other form of participation in the capital stock of companies constituted or organized in accordance with the legislation of the other Party;
- rights derived from all types of contributions made with the purpose of creating economic value (or obligations, credits and rights to any benefit that have economic value);
- movable and immovable property, as well as other real rights such as mortgages, pledge rights, usufruct and similar rights;
- rights in the field of intellectual property; Y
- rights to carry out economic and commercial activities granted by law or under a contract.
but does not include:
- a payment obligation of, nor the granting of a credit to, the State or a State company; neither
- pecuniary claims derived exclusively from:
a. commercial contracts for the sale of goods or services by a national or company in the territory of one Party to a national or company in the territory of another Party; either
b. the granting of credit in relation to a commercial transaction, whose expiration date is less than three years, such as trade financing;
disputing investor: an investor who submits a claim to arbitration under the terms of section B of this chapter;
investment of an investor of a Party: the investment owned or controlled by an investor of a Party made in the territory of another Party. In the case of a company, an investment is owned by an investor of a Party if that investor owns more than 49% of its share capital. An investment is controlled by an investor of a Party if that investor has the power to appoint a majority of its directors or otherwise direct its operations;
investor of a Party: a Party or a company of the same, or a national or company of that Party, that carries out the legal acts tending to materialize the investment, being in the process of committing a significant amount of capital or, in its case, makes or has made an investment in the territory of the other Party;
national of a Party: a natural person who is a national of a Party in accordance with its law;
Disputing Party: the Party against which a claim is made in arbitration under the terms of section B of this chapter;
disputing party: the disputing investor or the disputing Party;
disputing parties: the disputing investor and the disputing Party;
UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules: Arbitration Rules of the United Nations Commission on International Trade Law (UNCITRAL), adopted by the General Assembly of the United Nations on December 15, 1976;
Secretary General: Secretary General of ICSID;
transfers: international remittances and payments;
court: a court established under article 13-25;
accumulation tribunal: an arbitral tribunal established under article 13-28.
Article 13-02: Scope of application and extension of obligations.
1. This Chapter applies to measures adopted or maintained by a Party relating to:
a. investors of another Party, in everything related to their investment;
b. investments of investors of another Party made in the territory of the Party after the entry into force of this Agreement. However, it will also apply to investments made prior to its validity and that have the quality of foreign investment. It will not apply, however, to controversies or claims arising or resolved prior to its entry into force, or related to events that occurred prior to its entry into force, even if its effects remain even after it; Y
c. all investments of investors of a Party in the territory of another Party, in relation to article 13-06.
2. This chapter does not apply to:
a. the economic activities reserved to each Party, in accordance with their legislation in force on the date of signing this Agreement, which will be listed within a period not exceeding one year from the entry into force of this Agreement;
b. the measures adopted or maintained by a Party in the area of ​​financial services;
c. the measures adopted by a Party to restrict the participation of investments by investors of another Party in its territory for reasons of public order or national security.
3. This Chapter applies throughout the territory of the Parties and at any level or order of government notwithstanding any incompatible measures that may exist in the laws of those levels or orders of government.
Article 13-03: National treatment.
Each Party shall provide investors of another Party and the investments of investors of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that which it grants, in similar circumstances, to its own investors and to the investments of those investors.
Article 13-04: Most favored nation treatment.
1. Each Party shall provide to investors of another Party and to investments of investors of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that which it accords in similar circumstances, to investors and to investments of investors of another Party or of a country that is not a party, except as provided in paragraph
2. If a Party has granted special treatment to investors or their investments, coming from a country that is not a party, by virtue of bilateral investment treaties or agreements that establish free trade zones, customs unions, common markets, economic or monetary unions or other similar economic integration institutions, that Party shall not be obliged to grant the treatment in question to investors or to investments of investors of another Party.
Article 13-05: Treatment in case of losses.
Each Party shall grant investors of another Party, with respect to investments that suffer losses in its territory due to armed conflicts or civil strife, in the event of an act of God or force majeure (natural disasters), non-discriminatory treatment with respect to any measure that it adopts or maintains. in connection with those losses.
Article 13-06: Performance requirements.
1. No Party may impose or force compliance with the following requirements or commitments, in relation to any investment of an investor of another Party in its territory:
a. export a certain level or percentage of goods;
b. reach a certain degree or percentage of national content;
c. acquire or use or grant preference to goods produced in its territory or acquire goods from producers in its territory; either
d. relate in any way the volume or value of imports with the volume or value of exports, or with the amount of foreign currency inflows associated with that investment.
2. No Party may condition the receipt of an incentive or the continued receipt thereof, to the fulfillment of the following requirements, in relation to any investment of an investor of another Party in its territory:
a. acquire or use or grant preference to goods produced in its territory or to purchase goods from producers in its territory;
b. reach a certain degree or percentage of national content; either
c. relate in any way the volume or value of imports with the volume or value of exports, or with the amount of foreign currency inflows associated with that investment.
3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply to any requirement other than those stated therein.
4. The provisions contained in:
a. Subparagraphs a), b) and c) of paragraph 1 and subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 2 do not apply in relation to the requirements for qualification of goods with respect to export promotion programs and foreign aid;
b. Subparagraphs b) and c) of paragraph 1 and subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 2 do not apply to purchases made by a Party or by a State enterprise;
c. Subparagraphs a) and b) of paragraph 2 do not apply to the requirements imposed by an importing Party related to the necessary content of the goods to qualify for preferential tariffs or quotas.
5. Nothing in the provisions of this article shall be construed as an impediment for a Party to impose, in relation to any investment in its territory, requirements for the geographical location of productive units, for the generation of employment or labor training, or for carrying out of research and development activities.
6. In the event that, in the opinion of a Party, the imposition by another Party of any of the requirements indicated below negatively affects the flow of trade or constitutes a significant barrier to investment by an investor of another Party, the matter will be considered by the Commission:
a. restrict the sales in their territory of the goods that this investment produces, relating in any way those sales to the volume or value of their exports or to the earnings in foreign currency that they generate;
b. transfer to a person in their territory, technology, production process or other reserved knowledge, except when the requirement is imposed by a judicial or administrative court or competent authority to remedy an alleged violation of competition law or to act in a manner that it is not inconsistent with other provisions of this Agreement; either
c. act as the exclusive supplier of the goods it produces for a specific, regional or global market.
7. If the Commission finds that, in effect, the requirement in question adversely affects the flow of trade or constitutes a significant barrier to investment by an investor from another Party, it shall adopt the necessary measures to suppress the practice in question. The Parties shall consider these provisions as incorporated into this Agreement.
Article 13-07: Senior business management.
1. No Party may require that a company of a Party appoint individuals of any particular nationality to senior management positions in that company.
2. A Party may require that the majority of the members of the governing bodies of a company be of a particular nationality, provided that the result does not materially impair the investor's ability to exercise control of his investment.
Article 13-08: Reservations and exceptions.
1. Articles 13-03, 13-04, 13-06 and 13-07 do not apply to any inconsistent measure maintained or adopted by a Party, whatever the level or order of government, which shall be listed within a period no more than one year from the entry into force of this Agreement. The incompatible measure adopted by a Party may not be more restrictive than those existing at the time that measure is enacted.
2. The treatment granted by a Party in accordance with Article 13-04 does not apply to the treaties or sectors listed within a period not exceeding one year from the entry into force of this Agreement.
3. Articles 13-03, 13-04 and 13-07 do not apply to:
a. acquisitions made by a Party or by a State enterprise; either
b. subsidies or contributions, including government loans, guarantees and insurance granted by a Party or by a State enterprise, except as provided in paragraph 2 of article 13-05.
Article 13-09: Transfers.
1. Each Party shall allow all transfers related to the investment of an investor of one Party in the territory of another Party to be made freely and without delay. Those transfers include:
a. profits, dividends, interest, capital gains, royalty payments, administrative expenses, technical assistance, profits in kind and other amounts derived from the investment;
b. goods derived from the sale or liquidation, total or partial, of the investment;
c. payments made pursuant to a contract to which an investor or an investor's investment is a party, including payments made pursuant to a loan agreement;
d. payments derived from compensation for expropriation concept; Y
and. payments that come from the application of the provisions related to the dispute resolution mechanism contained in section B of this chapter.
2. Each Party shall allow transfers to be made in freely convertible currencies at the prevailing market exchange rate on the date of the transfer.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2, the Parties may prevent the making of transfers, through the equitable and non-discriminatory application of their legislation in the following cases:
a. bankruptcy, insolvency or protection of the rights of creditors;
b. issuance, trading and operations of securities;
c. criminal or administrative offenses;
d. reports of currency transfers or other monetary instruments;
and. guarantee of compliance with sentences or awards rendered in a contentious process; either
F. Establishment of the necessary instruments or mechanisms to ensure the payment of income taxes by means such as withholding the amount related to dividends or other concepts.
4. Notwithstanding the provisions of this article, each Party shall have the right, in circumstances of exceptional or serious balance of payments difficulties, to temporarily limit transfers, in an equitable and non-discriminatory manner, in accordance with internationally accepted criteria. Limitations adopted or maintained by a Party pursuant to this paragraph, as well as their removal, shall be promptly notified to the other Party.
Article 13-10: Expropriation and compensation.
1. No Party may nationalize or expropriate, directly or indirectly, an investment of an investor of another Party in its territory, or take any measure equivalent to the expropriation or nationalization of that investment ("expropriation"), unless it is:
a. for reasons of public utility;
b. on non-discriminatory grounds;
c. with adherence to the principle of legality; Y
d. by compensation in accordance with paragraphs 2 to 4.
2. Compensation will be equal to the fair market value of the expropriated investment immediately before the expropriation measure was carried out ("expropriation date"), and will not reflect any change in value due to the intent to expropriate is known in advance of the expropriation date. The valuation criteria will include the declared fiscal value of tangible assets, as well as other criteria that are appropriate to determine the fair market value.
3. The payment of the compensation will be made without delay and will be fully payable.
4. The amount paid shall not be less than the equivalent amount paid for compensation in a freely convertible currency in the international financial market, on the date of expropriation, and this currency would have been converted at the current market price on the date of expropriation. valuation date, plus the interest that would have been generated at a reasonable commercial rate for that currency, selected by the Party in accordance with international parameters, up to the date of payment.
Article 13-11: Special formalities and information requirements.
1. Nothing in Article 13-03 shall be construed to prevent a Party from adopting or maintaining a measure that prescribes special formalities related to the establishment of investments by investors of another Party, such as investments being constituted in accordance with to the Party's law, provided that such formalities do not materially impair the protection afforded by a Party under this Chapter.
2. Notwithstanding the provisions of Articles 13-03 and 13-04, the Parties may require an investor of another Party or its investment in its territory to provide routine information regarding that investment exclusively for information or statistics. The Party will protect the information that is confidential, from any disclosure that could adversely affect the competitive situation of the investment or of the investor.
Article 13-12: Relationship with other chapters.
In case of incompatibility between a provision of this chapter and the provision of another, the provision of the latter shall prevail to the extent of the incompatibility.
Article 13-13: Denial of benefits.
A Party, upon notice and consultation with another Party, may deny the benefits of this Chapter to an investor of another Party that is an enterprise of that Party and to investments of that investor, if investors from a non-Party own or control the enterprise, within the meaning of the definition of "investment by an investor of a Party" in Article 13-01, and the enterprise does not have substantial business activities in the territory of the Party under whose law it is constituted or organized.
Article 13-14: Extraterritorial application of the legislation of a Party.
1. Each Party, in relation to the investments of its investors constituted or organized under the legislation of another Party, may not exercise jurisdiction or adopt any measure that has the effect of extraterritorial application of its legislation or the obstruction of trade between the Parties. , or between a Party and a country that is not a Party.
2. If a Party fails to comply with the provisions of paragraph 1, the Party where the investment was established may, at its discretion, adopt the measures and exercise the actions it deems necessary, in order to render the legislation or measure without effect. in question and the obstacles to trade resulting therefrom.
Article 13-15: Measures related to the environment.
1. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as preventing a Party from adopting, maintaining, or putting into effect any measure consistent with this chapter that it deems appropriate to ensure that investments in its territory comply with ecological or environmental legislation in that Party. .
2. The Parties recognize that it is inappropriate to encourage investment by relaxing domestic measures applicable to health, safety, ecology or the environment. Consequently, neither Party shall eliminate or undertake to exempt from the application of those measures the investment of an investor, as a means to induce the establishment, acquisition, expansion or maintenance of the investment in its territory. If a Party believes that another Party has encouraged an investment in this way, it may request consultations with that Party.
Article 13-16: Promotion of investments and exchange of information.
1. With the intention of significantly increasing reciprocal investment participation, each Party shall prepare investment opportunity promotion documents and design mechanisms for their dissemination; likewise, each Party will maintain and improve financial mechanisms that make the investments of one Party in the territory of another Party viable.
2. Each Party shall disclose detailed information on opportunities to:
a. investment in its territory, which may be developed by investors from another Party;
b. strategic alliances between investors of each Party, through the investigation and compilation of interests and association opportunities;
c. investment in specific economic sectors of interest to each Party and its investors, according to the express request made by a Party.
3. The Parties agree to stay informed and updated regarding:
a. the investment opportunities referred to in paragraph 2, including the dissemination of available financial instruments that help increase investment in the territory of the Parties;
b. legislation that, directly or indirectly, affects foreign investment including, among others, exchange and fiscal regimes;
c. the behavior of foreign investment in their respective territories.
4. Nothing in paragraphs 1 to 3 shall impose any additional obligation on each Party in relation to the systems of registration, control, verification or investigation of investment opportunities or existing investment in its territory.
Article 13-17: Double taxation
The Parties, with the aim of promoting investments within their respective territories by eliminating obstacles of a tax nature and monitoring compliance with tax obligations through the exchange of tax information, agree to initiate negotiations leading to the conclusion of agreements to avoid double taxation, according to the calendar established between the competent authorities of the Parties.
Section B - Settlement of disputes between a Party and an investor of another Party.
Article 13-18: Purpose.
This section establishes a mechanism for the settlement of disputes of a legal nature in investment matters that arise as a consequence of the violation of an obligation established in section A of this chapter, and that arise between a Party and an investor of another Party to from the entry into force of this Agreement, and which ensures equal treatment between investors of the Parties in accordance with the principle of international reciprocity, as well as the due exercise of the guarantee of hearing and defense within a legal process before a impartial arbitral tribunal.
Article 13-19: Claim by the investor of a Party on its own account or on behalf of a company.
1. Except as provided in the annex to this article and in accordance with this section, the investor of a Party may, on its own account or on behalf of a company of another Party that is a legal person owned or under its direct control or indirectly, to submit to arbitration a claim based on the fact that another Party or a company controlled directly or indirectly by that Party, has violated an obligation established in this chapter, provided that the investor or his investment has suffered losses or damages in by virtue of the violation or as a consequence of it.
2. The investor may not file a claim under this section if more than three years have elapsed from the date on which he knew or should have known of the alleged violation committed and of the losses or damages suffered.
3. When an investor files a claim on behalf of a company that is a legal person owned or under its direct or indirect control, and in parallel an investor that does not have control of a company files a claim on its own as result of the same acts, or two or more claims are submitted to arbitration under the same action taken by a Party, the consolidation tribunal established pursuant to Article 13-28 shall jointly consider those claims, unless that tribunal determines that the legal interests of a disputing party would be harmed.
4. An investment may not submit a claim to arbitration under this section.
Article 13-20: Settlement of disputes through consultation and negotiation.
The disputing parties will first try to settle the controversy through consultation or negotiation.
Article 13-21: Notification of the intention to submit the claim to arbitration.
The disputing investor shall notify the disputing Party in writing of its intention to submit a claim to arbitration, at least 90 days before the claim is formally filed. The notification will state the following:
a. the name and domicile of the disputing investor and, when the claim has been made on behalf of a company, the denomination or business name and domicile of the same;
b. the provisions of this chapter allegedly breached and any other applicable provision;
c. the facts on which the claim is motivated; Y
d. the repair requested and the approximate amount of the damages claimed, in the currency in which the investment was made.
Article 13-22: Conditions prior to the submission of a claim to the arbitration procedure.
1. The consent of the disputing parties to the arbitration procedure in accordance with this chapter shall be considered as consent to that arbitration to the exclusion of any other mechanism.
2. Each Party may require the prior exhaustion of its administrative remedies as a condition of its consent to arbitration under this chapter. However, if after six months from the moment the corresponding administrative resources were filed, the administrative authorities have not issued their final resolution, the investor may resort directly to arbitration, in accordance with the provisions of this section.
3. A disputing investor for its own account and an investor representing a company may submit a claim to the arbitration procedure in accordance with this section, only if:
a. in the case of the investor on his own account, he agrees to submit to arbitration under the terms of the procedures established in this section;
b. in the case of an investor representing a company, both the investor and the company agree to submit to arbitration under the terms of the procedures established in this section; Y
c. both the investor and a company from another Party, waive their right to initiate proceedings before any judicial court of any Party with respect to the measure allegedly in violation of the provisions of this chapter, except for the relief of administrative resources before the executing authorities themselves. of the allegedly infringing measure, provided for in the law of the disputing Party.
4. The consent and waiver required by this article shall be in writing, delivered to the disputing Party, and included in the submission of the claim to arbitration.
Article 13-23: Submission of the claim to arbitration.
1. Except as provided in the annex to this article and as long as six months have elapsed since the measures giving rise to the claim took place, a disputing investor may submit the claim to arbitration in accordance with:
a. the ICSID convention, provided that the disputing Party and the investor Party are party to it;
b. the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, when either the disputing Party or the investor Party, but not both, are parties to the ICSID agreement;
c. the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules, when the disputing Party and the investor Party are not party to the ICSID convention.
2. The rules of each of the arbitration procedures established in this chapter will be applicable except to the extent modified by this section.
Article 13-24: Consent to arbitration.
1. Each Party consents to submit claims to arbitration in accordance with the procedures and requirements indicated in this section.
2. The submission of a claim to arbitration by a disputing investor will imply having complied with the requirements indicated in:
a. Chapter II of the ICSID Convention and the Additional Facility Rules which require the written consent of the Parties;
b. Article II of the New York Convention, which requires a written agreement; Y
c. Article I of the Inter-American Convention, which requires an agreement.
Article 13-25: Number of arbitrators and method of appointment.
With the exception of the provisions of article 13-28, and without prejudice to the fact that the disputing Parties agree otherwise, the tribunal will be made up of three arbitrators. Each disputing Party shall appoint an arbitrator; the third arbitrator, who will be the president of the arbitral tribunal, will be appointed by the disputing Parties by mutual agreement, but will not be a national of one of the disputing parties.
Article 13-26: Composition of the tribunal in the event that a disputing Party does not appoint an arbitrator or an agreement is not reached on the appointment of the president of the arbitral tribunal.
1. The Secretary General shall appoint the arbitrators in the arbitration proceedings, in accordance with this section.
2. When a tribunal other than the one established in accordance with article 13-28, is not integrated within a period of 90 days from the date the claim is submitted to arbitration, the Secretary General, at the request of any of the disputing parties and, to the extent possible, after consulting them, shall appoint the arbitrator or arbitrators not yet appointed, but not the president of the tribunal, who shall be appointed in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 3. In any case, the majority of the arbitrators may not be nationals of one of the disputing parties.
3. The Secretary General shall appoint the president of the tribunal from among the arbitrators from the list referred to in paragraph 4, ensuring that the president of the tribunal is not a national of the disputing Party or a national of the Party of the disputing investor. In the event that an arbitrator available to preside over the tribunal is not found on the list, the Secretary-General shall designate, from the ICSID Panel of arbitrators, the president of the tribunal, provided that he is not a national of the disputing Party or of the investor's Party. contender.
4. As of the date of entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties shall establish and maintain a list of 15 arbitrators as possible presidents of the arbitral tribunal, who meet the qualities established in the ICSID convention, who have experience in international law and in investment matters. The members of the list will be appointed by consensus regardless of their nationality for a period of two years, renewable if the Parties so agree by consensus. In the event of the death or resignation of a member of the list, the Parties by mutual agreement will designate another person to replace him in his functions for the rest of the period for which he was appointed.
Article 13-27: Consent for the appointment of arbitrators.
For the purposes of Article 39 of the ICSID Convention and Article 7 of Part C of the Additional Facility Rules, and without prejudice to objecting to an arbitrator based on Article 13-26.3, or on a basis other than nationality:
a. the disputing Party accepts the appointment of each member of a tribunal established under the ICSID convention or the Additional Facility Rules;
b. A disputing investor, whether on its own behalf or on behalf of a company, may submit a claim to arbitration or continue proceedings under the ICSID convention or the Additional Facility Rules, only on the condition that the disputing investor and, if applicable, , the company that represents, express their consent in writing on the appointment of each of the members of the court.
Article 13-28: Accumulation of proceedings.
1. A consolidation tribunal established pursuant to this article shall be established in accordance with the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules and shall proceed in accordance with the provisions of those Rules, except as provided in this section.
2. When an accumulation tribunal determines that the claims submitted to arbitration under Article 13-22 raise common issues of fact and law, the accumulation tribunal, in the interest of their fair and efficient resolution, and having heard the disputing parties, may assume jurisdiction, process and resolve:
a. all or part of the claims, jointly; either
b. one or more of the claims on the basis that it will contribute to the resolution of the others.
3. A disputing party that seeks consolidation to be determined under the terms of paragraph 2, shall request the Secretary General to set up a consolidation tribunal and shall specify in its request:
a. the name and address of the disputing parties against whom the accumulation agreement is sought;
b. the nature of the cumulation agreement requested; Y
c. the grounds on which the requested petition is based.
4. Within a period of 60 days from the date of the petition, the Secretary General will set up a consolidation tribunal made up of three arbitrators. The Secretary General shall appoint from the list of arbitrators referred to in paragraph 4 of article 13-26, the president of the accumulation tribunal, who shall not be a national of the disputing Party or a national of the Party of the disputing investor. In the event that an arbitrator available to preside over the accumulation tribunal is not found on the list, the Secretary General shall designate, from the ICSID Panel of Arbitrators, the president of that tribunal, who shall not be a national of the disputing Party or a national of the Part of the contending investor. The Secretary General will appoint the other two members of the consolidation tribunal from the list referred to in paragraph 4 of Article 13-26 and, when they are not available on that list, will select them from the list of ICSID arbitrators. If there are no arbitrators available on that list, the Secretary General will make the remaining appointments at his discretion, one of the members being a national of the disputing Party and the other national member of a Party of the disputing investors.
5. When an accumulation tribunal has been established, the disputing investor who has submitted a claim to arbitration, and has not been named in the application for accumulation made in accordance with paragraph 3, may request in writing the accumulation tribunal to include you in the joinder request made in accordance with paragraph 2, and specify in that request:
a. the name and domicile of the disputing investor and, where appropriate, the name or business name and domicile of the company;
b. the nature of the cumulation agreement requested; Y
c. the grounds on which the requested petition is based.
6. The accumulation court will provide, at the expense of the interested investor, a copy of the accumulation petition to the disputing investors against whom the accumulation agreement is sought.
7. A tribunal established under article 13-22 shall not have jurisdiction to decide a claim, or part of a claim, in respect of which an accumulation tribunal has assumed jurisdiction.
8. At the request of a disputing party, a consolidation tribunal may order, pending its decision pursuant to paragraph 2, that the proceedings of a tribunal established pursuant to article 13-22 be stayed, pending a ruling on the origin of the accumulation.
9. A disputing Party shall deliver to the Secretariat, within 15 days from the date it is received by the disputing Party:
a. a request for arbitration made pursuant to paragraph 1 of article 36 of the ICSID convention;
b. a notice of arbitration under Article 2 of Part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules; either
c. a notice of arbitration under the terms provided by the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules.
10. A Party to the dispute shall provide the Secretariat with a copy of the request made in the terms of paragraph 3:
a. within 15 days from the receipt of the request, in the case of a request made by the disputing investor; either
b. within 15 days from the date of the request, in the case of a request made by the disputing Party.
11. A disputing Party shall provide the Secretariat with a copy of a request made under the terms of paragraph 6 within 15 days from the date of receipt of the request.
12. The Secretariat will keep a public register of the documents referred to in paragraphs 9 to 11.
Article 13-29: Notification.
The disputing Party shall deliver to another non-disputing Party:
a. written notice of a claim that has been submitted to arbitration no later than 30 days after the date of submission of the claim to arbitration; Y
b. copy of all the communications presented in the arbitration procedure.
Article 13-30: Participation of a Party.
A Party may submit submissions to any tribunal established pursuant to this section on a question of interpretation of this Agreement, simultaneously notifying the disputing parties in writing of the content of such submission.
Article 13-31: Documentation.
1. A Party will have, covering the expenses that may be generated, the right to receive from the disputing Party a copy of:
a. evidence offered to any court established under this section; Y
b. written communications submitted by the disputing parties.
2. A Party receiving information pursuant to paragraph 1 shall treat the information as confidential as if it were a disputing Party.
Article 13-32: Seat of the arbitration procedure.
The seat of the arbitral proceeding shall be located in the territory of the disputing Party, unless the disputing parties agree otherwise, in which case any court established under this section shall conduct the arbitral proceeding in the territory of a Party that is a party to the New York Convention, which shall be elected in accordance with:
a. the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, if the arbitration is governed by those rules or by the ICSID convention; either
b. the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules, if the arbitration is governed by those rules.
Article 13-33: Applicable law.
1. Any tribunal established pursuant to this section shall decide disputes submitted to it in accordance with this Agreement, the applicable rules of international law and, in addition, the law of the disputing Party.
2. The Commission's interpretation of a provision of this Agreement shall be binding on any court established pursuant to this section.
Article 13-34: Interpretation of the annexes.
1. When a Party alleges as a defense that a measure allegedly in violation falls within the scope of a reservation or exception contained in any of the annexes, at the request of the disputing Party, any tribunal established pursuant to this section shall request the Commission for an interpretation. on that matter. The Commission, within a period of 60 days from the delivery of the request, will present its interpretation in writing to that court.
2. The Commission's interpretation referred to in paragraph 1 shall be binding on any tribunal established pursuant to this section. If the Commission does not submit an interpretation within 60 days, that court will rule on the matter.
Article 13-35: Provisional or precautionary measures.
A tribunal established under this section may apply to domestic courts, or order disputing parties, provisional measures of protection to preserve the rights of the disputing party or to ensure that the jurisdiction or jurisdiction of the tribunal is fully effective. That court may not order compliance with or suspension of the application of the presumably infringing measure referred to in article 13-19.
Article 13-36: Final award.
1. When a tribunal established under this section makes an award unfavorable to a Party, that tribunal may only award:
a. pecuniary damages and corresponding interests; either
b. the restitution of the property, in which case the award will provide that the disputing Party may pay pecuniary damages, plus the applicable interest, instead of the restitution.
2. When the claim is made by an investor representing a company based on article 13-19:
a. the award that provides for the restitution of the property will provide that the restitution be granted to the company;
b. the award that awards pecuniary damages and corresponding interest will provide that the sum of money be paid to the company.
3. For the purposes of paragraphs 1 and 2, damages will be determined in the currency in which the investment was made.
4. The award will be rendered without prejudice to the rights that a third party with a legal interest may have regarding the reparation of the damages suffered, in accordance with the applicable legislation.
Article 13-37: Execution of the award.
1. The award rendered by any court established pursuant to this section shall be binding only on the disputing parties and only with respect to the specific case.
2. In accordance with the provisions of paragraph 3 and without prejudice to the fact that the procedures for clarification, review or annulment of the award provided for under the applicable mechanism are appropriate in the opinion of the Secretary General, a disputing party shall abide by and comply with the award without delay.
3. A disputing party may request enforcement of a final award provided that:
a. in the case of a final award rendered under the ICSID convention:
i) 120 days have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without a disputing party requesting its clarification, revision, or annulment; either
ii) the clarification, revision or annulment procedures referred to in numeral i) have concluded; Y
b. in the case of a final award under the ICSID Additional Facility Rules or the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules:
i) three months have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without a disputing party having initiated a proceeding to review or annul it; either
ii) a court of the disputing Party has denied (dismissed) or admitted a request for reconsideration or annulment of the award that one of the disputing parties has submitted to the national courts in accordance with its law and this decision cannot be appealed.
4. Each Party shall provide for the due enforcement of an award in its territory. The award will be enforced in accordance with the rules on enforcement of judgments or awards that are in force in the territories in which enforcement is sought.
5. When a disputing Party fails to comply with an award, the Commission, upon receipt of a request from a Party whose investor was a party to the arbitration proceeding, shall form a panel pursuant to Chapter XVII (Dispute Settlement). The requesting Party may invoke these procedures to obtain:
a. a determination that failure to comply with the terms of the award is contrary to the obligations of this Treaty; Y
b. a recommendation that the Party conform to and observe the award in question.
6. The disputing investor may resort to the enforcement of an arbitral award in accordance with the ICSID convention, the New York Convention or the Inter-American Convention, regardless of whether or not the procedures contemplated in paragraph 5 have been initiated.
7. For the purposes of Article I of the New York Convention and Article I of the Inter-American Convention, the claim submitted to arbitration pursuant to this section shall be deemed to arise from a commercial relationship or operation.
Article 13-38: General provisions.
1. Moment in which the claim is considered submitted to the arbitration procedure.
A claim is considered submitted to arbitration under the terms of this section when:
a. the request for arbitration under ICSID Article 36 has been received by the Secretary General;
b. the notice of arbitration, pursuant to part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, has been received by the Secretary-General; either
c. the notice of arbitration contemplated in the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules has been received by the disputing Party.
2. Delivery of documents.
The delivery of the notification and other documents to a Party shall be made at the place designated by the Party no later than the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
3. Payments under Insurance or Guarantee Contracts.
In an arbitration proceeding pursuant to the provisions of this section, a Party shall not adduce as a defense, counterclaim, compensation right, or others, that the disputing investor received or will receive, in accordance with an insurance or guarantee contract, compensation or other compensation. for all or part of the alleged damages for which restitution is requested.
4. Publication of awards.
The awards will be published only in the event that there is a written agreement between the disputing parties.
Article 13-39: Exclusions.
The dispute resolution provisions of this section and those of Chapter XVII (Dispute Resolution) shall not apply to the cases contained in the annex to this article.
Annex to Article 13-19
Claim by an investor of a Party, on its own behalf or on behalf of a company
1. Without prejudice to the provisions of article 13-28, in the event that an investor has instituted a process on its own account and, in parallel, another investor of the same investment has instituted a process on behalf of that investment for the same cause, the first of these processes will accumulate to the latter.
2. In the case in which an investor has instituted a process on its own before an arbitral tribunal and, in parallel, another investor of the same investment has instituted a process on its own before a national court, the latter will proceed to attract .
Annex to the article13-23
Submission of the claim to arbitration
When a company of a Party that is a legal person owned by an investor of another Party or that is under its direct or indirect control, alleges in proceedings before a judicial or administrative court, that another Party has allegedly violated an obligation to which referred to in section A of this chapter, the investor or investors may not allege the alleged violation in an arbitration proceeding pursuant to section B of this chapter.
Annex to the article13-39
Exclusions
The resolutions adopted by a Party by virtue of paragraph 2 of Article 13-02, nor the resolution that prohibits or restricts the acquisition of an investment in its territory owned or controlled by nationals of that Party, by an investor of another Party, in accordance with the laws of each Party.
Chapter XIV
Intellectual property
General provisions and basic principles.
Article 14-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
intellectual property rights: all categories of intellectual property that are protected by this chapter, in the terms indicated therein;
nationals of the other Party: with respect to the relevant intellectual property right, persons who would meet the eligibility criteria for protection under the Berne Convention for the Protection of Literary and Artistic Works (1971), the Geneva Convention for the Protection of Phonogram Producers against Unauthorized Reproduction of their Phonograms (1971), the Rome Convention on the Protection of Performers, Phonogram Producers and Broadcasting Organizations (1961) and, where appropriate , the Paris Convention for the Protection of Industrial Property (1967);
public: which includes, for the purposes of copyright and related rights in relation to the rights of communication and execution of the works provided for in articles 11, 11 bis (I) and 14.1.2§ of the Berne Convention, with respect to at least to dramatic, dramatic-musical, musical, literary, artistic or cinematographic works, any group of individuals who are intended to be directed and are capable of perceiving communications or performances of works, regardless of whether they can do so at the same time and in the same place or at different times and places, as long as that grouping is larger than a family and its immediate circle of acquaintances or is not a group made up of a limited number of individuals who have the same type of close relationships,that it has not been formed with the main purpose of receiving those executions and communications of works;
encrypted program-carrying satellite signal: one that is transmitted in a form by which auditory or visual characteristics, or both, are modified or altered to prevent reception by persons lacking equipment designed to eliminate the effects of that modification or alteration of the program carried on that signal.
Article 14-02: Protection of intellectual property rights.
1. Each Party shall grant in its territory to the nationals of the other Party adequate and effective protection and defense of intellectual property rights and shall ensure that the measures aimed at defending those rights do not in turn become obstacles to legitimate trade.
2. Each Party may grant in its legislation a broader protection of intellectual property rights than that required in this chapter, provided that such protection is not incompatible with it.
3. Each Party may freely establish the appropriate method for applying the provisions of this Chapter, within the framework of its own legal system and practice.
Article 14-03: Provisions on the matter.
